**1. With reference to Indian Judiciary, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Provision                                      Feature
1. Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008                    :   Exempts Nagaland, Arunachal Pradesh, Sikkim
2. Contempt of Courts Act, 1971                  :   Defines both civil and criminal contempt
3. Article 137 of the Constitution                 :   Deals with review petitions in the Supreme Court
4. Article 282 of the Constitution                :   Empowers discretionary grants by the Centre and States
5.  Indian Evidence Act, 1872                     :  Rules of evidence applicable in Gram Nyayalayas

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, explicitly exempts certain states and tribal areas from its purview.  The Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, comprehensively defines both civil and criminal contempt. Article 137 of the Constitution grants the Supreme Court the power to review its own judgments.  Article 282 allows for discretionary grants for public purposes.  However, the Indian Evidence Act, 1872, is *not* directly applicable in Gram Nyayalayas; they are guided by principles of natural justice instead.  Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either omit correctly matched pairs or include the incorrectly matched pair related to the Indian Evidence Act. Option (b) accurately identifies the four correctly matched pairs.


**2. With reference to Constitutional Provisions and their Applications, consider the following pairs:**

   Article                                           Application/Feature
1. Article 341(1)                                  :   Specifies Scheduled Castes for states/union territories
2. Article 341(2)                                  :   Parliament's power to alter the Scheduled Castes list
3. Article 72                                      :   President's power to grant pardons, etc., including death sentences
4. Article 142                                    :   Supreme Court's power to do complete justice
5. Article 22(3)                                   :   Exceptions to protection against arrest/detention

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 341(1) correctly defines the President's role in specifying Scheduled Castes.  Article 341(2) accurately describes Parliament's power to modify the Scheduled Castes list. Article 72 correctly outlines the President's pardon powers. Article 142 correctly describes the Supreme Court's inherent powers to ensure complete justice.  Article 22(3) correctly points to the exceptions related to preventive detention where protections against arrest are not applicable.  Therefore, all five pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer. All other options are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.



**3. With reference to the Citizenship Act, 1955 and related legislation, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Provision                                  Feature/Requirement
1. Section 6B of the Citizenship Act, 1955        :   Electronic application for naturalization
2. Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA), 2019         :   Reduced naturalization period for certain religious groups
3. Passport (Entry into India) Act, 1920          :   Affected by CAA exemptions for certain groups
4. Foreigners Act, 1946                          :   Affected by CAA exemptions for certain groups
5.  Article 244(2)                               :   Deals with the Sixth Schedule


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Section 6B of the Citizenship Act, 1955, introduced an electronic application process for naturalization. The CAA, 2019, significantly reduced the naturalization period for specific religious groups from Afghanistan, Bangladesh, and Pakistan.  The CAA, 2019, provided exemptions from the penal consequences under both the Passport (Entry into India) Act, 1920, and the Foreigners Act, 1946.  Article 244(2) is related to the Sixth Schedule provisions, making the last pair incorrect. Therefore, options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair or exclude correctly matched pairs. Option (b) is the most appropriate, correctly identifying four pairs.


**4. With reference to  the Panchayati Raj system and related initiatives, consider the following pairs:**

   Initiative/Program                                      Feature
1. Jan Yojana Abhiyan/People’s Plan Campaign          :   Preparation of Panchayat Development Plans
2.  Gram Nyayalayas                                     :   Settlement of petty disputes at the village level
3.  Panchayat Development Index (PDI)                   :   Assessment of panchayat development
4.  Articles 14 and 21 of the Constitution              :  Guarantee right to be free from adverse effects of climate change
5.  Places of Worship (Special Provisions) Act, 1991   :   Maintains religious character of places of worship as of 15 August 1947


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Jan Yojana Abhiyan focuses on the preparation of Panchayat Development Plans. Gram Nyayalayas are indeed designed to resolve petty disputes at the village level. The Panchayat Development Index (PDI) is used to assess the progress and performance of panchayats. The Places of Worship (Special Provisions) Act, 1991, aims to maintain the religious character of places of worship as it existed on August 15, 1947. However, Articles 14 and 21 are related to the right to life and equality and were interpreted in a recent Supreme Court case to include the right to be free from the adverse effects of climate change, but this is not a direct, original constitutional pairing.   Therefore, options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect. Option (b) correctly identifies four of the five pairs.


**5. With reference to Special Status and Financial Provisions for States, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision/Concept                                  Feature
1. Special Category States (SCS)                     :   No longer exist after 14th Finance Commission recommendations
2.  Article 282 of the Constitution                  :   Empowers discretionary grants for public purposes
3.  Special Packages for States                       :   Additional financial assistance for states facing challenges
4.  Sixth Schedule of the Constitution                :   Provides for Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs) in certain states
5.  Gadgil-Mukherjee Formula                         :   Used for grants to SCS states


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Special Category States (SCS) ceased to exist following the recommendations of the 14th Finance Commission. Article 282 correctly describes the power to make discretionary grants. Special packages are used to support states with specific challenges. The Sixth Schedule correctly outlines the establishment of ADCs and ARCs. The Gadgil-Mukherjee formula was indeed used for distributing grants to SCS states.  Therefore, all five pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer.  Other options are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Amendment                                     Key Provision/Exemption
1. Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008                     :   Exempts Nagaland from its jurisdiction
2.  Indian Evidence Act, 1872                     :   Replaced by Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam
3. Contempt of Courts Act, 1971                   : Defines both civil and criminal contempt
4. Citizenship Act, 1955                          :  Amended by CAA, 2019

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, explicitly exempts certain states, including Nagaland, from its application.  The Indian Evidence Act, 1872, has indeed been replaced by the Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam.  The Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, provides a legal framework for defining and addressing contempt of court, encompassing both civil and criminal contempt.  Finally, the Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA) 2019 directly amends the Citizenship Act, 1955.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.  Understanding the legal framework of these acts and amendments is crucial for comprehending the Indian judicial and citizenship systems.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Amendment/Act                       Provision/Feature
1. 73rd Constitutional Amendment Act, 1992        :   Established AuditOnline application
2.  Article 244(2)                                  :   Empowers Governor to create ARCs
3.  Article 3                                       :   Deals with formation of new states
4. Official Languages Act, 1963                     :   Established the Parliamentary Committee on Official Languages


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The 73rd Constitutional Amendment Act deals with Panchayati Raj Institutions, but the AuditOnline application was developed later by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj, not directly by the amendment itself. Article 244(2) forms the basis for the creation of Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs) in the Sixth Schedule areas.  Article 3 of the Constitution grants Parliament the power to create new states or alter existing ones. The Official Languages Act, 1963, led to the formation of the Parliamentary Committee on Official Languages (PCOL). Therefore, options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they incorrectly associate the 73rd Amendment with AuditOnline and/or omit one or more of the correctly matched pairs.  A complete understanding of the Indian Constitution and its amendments is crucial for answering this question correctly.


**3. With reference to Local Governance Auditing, consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Act                                  Role/Responsibility
1. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) :   Sets global standards for auditing local governance
2.  CAG (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971 :   Mandates CAG's audit of local bodies
3.  Ministry of Panchayati Raj                         :   Developed the AuditOnline application
4. Examiner of Local Fund Accounts (ELFA)           : Works under the technical guidance of the CAG


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3 and 4
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

iCAL aims to establish international standards for local governance auditing. The CAG Act of 1971 grants the Comptroller and Auditor General of India (CAG) the authority to audit local bodies. The Ministry of Panchayati Raj developed the AuditOnline application for online auditing of panchayat accounts.  ELFAs, along with DLFA, operate under the CAG's supervision. Thus all the pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incomplete, omitting at least one of the correctly matched pairs.  This question tests knowledge of the auditing mechanisms in place for local governance in India, highlighting the roles of various central and state-level entities.

**1. With reference to the Panchayati Raj system and planning, consider the following pairs:**

   Scheme/Initiative                                  Key Feature/Objective
1. Jan Yojana Abhiyan (People’s Plan Campaign)     :   Preparation of Panchayat Development Plans (PDPs) for 2025-26 based on Panchayat Development Index (PDI)
2. Sabki Yojana Sabka Vikas                        :   Launched in 2018 to accelerate people's participation in PDP preparation across three Panchayat tiers.
3. Gram Nyayalayas                                 :   Settling petty disputes at the village level through conciliation, guided by principles of natural justice.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Jan Yojana Abhiyan, also known as the People’s Plan Campaign, is a crucial initiative aimed at accelerating people's participation in the preparation of Panchayat Development Plans (PDPs).  The campaign leverages the Panchayat Development Index (PDI) to identify thematic developmental gaps. The PDI is a multi-domain index assessing the overall development of panchayats.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

Sabki Yojana Sabka Vikas was indeed launched in 2018 by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj as the initial name for Jan Yojana Abhiyan. Its core objective is to enhance people's involvement in the preparation of PDPs at all three levels of Panchayats. This makes pair 2 a correct match.

Gram Nyayalayas, established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, are designed to resolve minor civil and criminal disputes at the village level.  A key aspect of their functioning is the use of conciliation to settle disputes, adhering to principles of natural justice rather than strictly following the Indian Evidence Act. Thus, pair 3 is also correctly matched.  All three pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. With reference to the auditing and governance of local bodies, consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Initiative                           Characteristic/Function
1. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) :   Aims to set global standards for auditing local governance bodies, first of its kind in India.
2.  Panchayat Development Plans (PDPs)           :  Prepared with active involvement of elected representatives, frontline workers, and community-based organizations.
3.  Audit of Local Bodies                           :  Ensures accountability and transparency in the financial management of local governance.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL), inaugurated in Rajkot, Gujarat, is indeed the first of its kind in India. Its primary objective is to establish global benchmarks for auditing local governance bodies.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

Panchayat Development Plans (PDPs) are prepared through a participatory process involving elected representatives, government officials, and community organizations like SHGs. This collaborative approach underscores the importance of inclusive planning. Hence, pair 2 is correctly matched.

Auditing of local bodies is an essential mechanism to ensure accountability and transparency in their financial management.  Regular audits help to detect irregularities, promote efficient resource allocation, and build public trust. Thus, pair 3 is correctly matched.  All three pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.



**3. With reference to special category states and financial assistance, consider the following pairs:**

   State-related Policy/Provision                       Feature/Characteristic
1. Special Category States (SCS)                    :   Grants were previously based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula, but this ceased to exist after the 14th Finance Commission's recommendations.
2. Special Financial Packages                       :   Provided to states facing geographical and socio-economic challenges under Article 282.
3.  Sixth Schedule to the Constitution              :   Provides for the administration of tribal areas in certain states, currently not including Ladakh.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Special Category States (SCS) once received financial grants based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula.  However, following recommendations from the 14th Finance Commission, the SCS category was discontinued.  The current special funding for Northeastern and Himalayan states is based on different criteria. This makes pair 1 correct.

Special financial packages, granted under Article 282 of the Constitution, offer additional financial aid and other benefits to states facing significant geographical or socio-economic challenges.  These packages are discretionary and not solely based on need. This clarifies pair 2.

The Sixth Schedule of the Constitution outlines the administrative structure for tribal areas in specific states.  While there's a recent push to include Ladakh, it is currently not included.  This confirms pair 3.

Therefore, all three pairs (1, 2, and 3) are correctly matched, leading to option (d) as the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they miss at least one correctly matched pair.



**4.  With reference to the judicial system and legal processes in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Concept/Process                            Characteristic/Provision
1. Contempt of Court                               :   Defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, with powers vested in the Supreme Court and High Courts under Articles 129 and 215.
2. Mercy Petition                                  :   The President's power to grant pardons, reprieves, etc., is enshrined in Article 72, applicable to death sentences and offenses under Union executive power.
3. Curative Petition                               :   The last constitutional remedy, shaped by the Rupa Ashok Hurra case, arising from Article 142's power to ensure complete justice.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Contempt of Court, as defined by the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, allows the Supreme Court and High Courts to punish individuals for actions that undermine their authority or interfere with the administration of justice.  Articles 129 and 215 grant these courts the power to do so. Thus, pair 1 is correctly matched.

Article 72 of the Constitution empowers the President to pardon, reprieve, or commute sentences, including death sentences, for offenses under Union laws or court-martial proceedings. This explains pair 2.

The Curative Petition, established through the Rupa Ashok Hurra case, serves as the final legal recourse available after a review petition has been rejected by the Supreme Court.  This stems from Article 142, which grants the Supreme Court the power to ensure complete justice.  This makes pair 3 a correct match.

Therefore, all three pairs are accurately matched, making (d) the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one of the correctly matched pairs.


**5. With reference to specific courts and their functions, consider the following pairs:**

   Court/Tribunal                                     Jurisdiction/Function
1. Gram Nyayalayas                                   :   Mobile courts with civil and criminal jurisdiction to settle petty disputes at the village level.
2. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)                :   Centrally sponsored scheme focusing on swift disposal of rape cases and POCSO Act cases.
3.  Special Courts under the Prevention of Corruption Act (PCA), 1988:   Hear cases related to offenses committed by public servants under the PCA.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Gram Nyayalayas, established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, are mobile courts with jurisdiction over petty civil and criminal cases at the village level. They emphasize conciliation to resolve disputes. This makes pair 1 correct.

Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs), launched as a centrally sponsored scheme, are designed to expedite the trial of rape and POCSO Act cases.  Their objective is to ensure swift justice for victims.  This clarifies pair 2.

Special Courts are designated under the Prevention of Corruption Act, 1988, to handle cases involving offenses committed by public servants. These courts play a crucial role in tackling corruption within the government. This explains pair 3.

All three pairs are correctly matched, hence option (d) is correct. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.


**6. With reference to Aadhaar and its related aspects, consider the following pairs:**

   Aadhaar Feature/Characteristic                      Description/Implication
1. Random Number                                     :   Does not contain details like caste, religion, income, health, or geography.
2. Proof of Address and Identity                     :   Serves as proof of address and identity for residents of India, but not citizenship or domicile.
3.  Targeted Delivery of Benefits                    :   Central/State Governments can make Aadhaar mandatory for accessing benefits under schemes funded from Consolidated Funds.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Aadhaar number is a randomly generated unique identifier, devoid of personal details such as caste, religion, income, health status, or geographic location. This ensures privacy to a certain extent.  This makes pair 1 correct.

Aadhaar serves as a proof of address and identity for Indian residents, but it is not a proof of citizenship or domicile.  This distinction is crucial. This clarifies pair 2.

The Aadhaar Act, 2016, allows Central and State Governments to mandate Aadhaar for accessing benefits under schemes funded by Consolidated Funds. This targeted delivery mechanism aims to enhance efficiency and minimize leakages. This explains pair 3.

All three pairs are correctly matched; therefore, option (d) is the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one of the correctly matched pairs.



**7. With reference to Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSSs) and their administration, consider the following pairs:**

   Aspect of CSSs                                    Description/Feature
1. Funding                                          :   Funded jointly by the central and state governments.
2. Implementation                                  :   Implemented through states in sectors falling under the State and Concurrent Lists of the Constitution.
3. Current Framework                               :   Based on the report by a Sub-Group of Chief Ministers on Rationalisation of CSSs (2015).

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSSs) are collaborative ventures between the central and state governments, with shared funding responsibilities. This collaborative nature is a defining characteristic.  This makes pair 1 correct.

CSSs are implemented by state governments in sectors listed under the State and Concurrent Lists of the Indian Constitution.  This ensures that schemes align with the respective state's priorities and needs. This clarifies pair 2.

The current framework governing CSSs is rooted in the recommendations of a Sub-Group of Chief Ministers, established in 2015, which focused on rationalizing these schemes. This explains pair 3.

Since all three pairs are correctly matched, option (d) is the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**8. With reference to  Citizenship in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Citizenship Acquisition Method                        Requirement/Condition
1. Citizenship by Birth                               :   Born in India on or after 26 January 1950
2. Citizenship by Descent                             :   One parent is a citizen of India at the time of the child's birth
3. Citizenship by Naturalization                        :   Adequate knowledge of a language listed in the Eighth Schedule of the Constitution.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Citizenship by birth in India is acquired by individuals born in India on or after January 26, 1950. This straightforward condition is a fundamental aspect of Indian citizenship law. This clarifies pair 1.

Citizenship by descent is granted to children born outside India if at least one parent is an Indian citizen at the time of the child's birth. This provision addresses the citizenship of children born to Indian citizens abroad.  This makes pair 2 correct.

Citizenship by naturalization requires fulfilling certain conditions, including demonstrating adequate knowledge of a language from the Eighth Schedule of the Indian Constitution. This condition reflects the importance of linguistic integration. This explains pair 3.

All three pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they omit at least one correctly matched pair.



**9. With reference to the Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA), 2019, consider the following pairs:**

   CAA Provision                                       Detail/Condition
1.  Eligibility for Non-Muslim Migrants                :   Must have entered India on or before December 31, 2014.
2.  Exemption from Penal Consequences               :   Exempted from penalties under the Passport (Entry into India) Act, 1920, and the Foreigners Act, 1946.
3.  Reduced Naturalization Period                     :   Reduced from 11 years to 5 years for specified categories of migrants.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA), 2019, grants eligibility for citizenship to non-Muslim migrants from specified countries who entered India before December 31, 2014.  This cut-off date is a critical element of the Act. This clarifies pair 1.

The CAA exempts eligible non-Muslim migrants from penalties under the Passport (Entry into India) Act, 1920, and the Foreigners Act, 1946. This provision addresses the legal status of these migrants. This makes pair 2 correct.

The CAA reduces the naturalization period from 11 years to 5 years for the specific categories of migrants mentioned in the Act.  This accelerated path to citizenship is a key feature. This explains pair 3.

Since all three pairs are correctly matched, option (d) is the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.



**10. With reference to Overseas Citizens of India (OCI) and their status, consider the following pairs:**

   OCI Aspect                                          Description/Feature
1.  OCI Cardholders                                  :   Existing OCI rules remain unchanged, addressing concerns about reclassification.
2.  OCI Registration Cancellation                     :   The central government can cancel OCI registration on five specified grounds.
3.  OCI Status                                        :   OCI cardholders are not citizens of India but enjoy certain privileges and benefits.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Recent clarifications from the Ministry of External Affairs confirm that the existing rules for Overseas Citizens of India (OCI) cardholders remain unchanged.  This addresses concerns about potential changes to their status.  This makes pair 1 correct.

The central government retains the power to cancel OCI registration based on five specific grounds outlined in relevant legislation. This provision provides a mechanism for addressing potential misuse or violations. This clarifies pair 2.

OCI cardholders are not Indian citizens but are granted certain privileges and benefits under the relevant laws. This distinction is fundamental to understanding their status. This explains pair 3.

All three pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.



**1. With reference to the Indian Fiscal System, consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision                      Subject Matter
1. Article 270                               :   Distribution of taxes between Union and States
2. Article 275                               :   Grants-in-aid to States
3. Article 292                               :   Borrowing by State Governments outside India
4. Article 280                               :   Appointment of the Union Finance Minister

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 270 of the Indian Constitution deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain taxes between the Union and the States.  Article 275 pertains to grants-in-aid from the Union to the States.  Crucially, Article 292 explicitly grants the Union government the power to borrow money both within and outside India, while state governments can borrow only within India (and not abroad) under Article 293.  The Finance Commission is established under Article 280, not the Union Finance Minister's appointment. The Union Finance Minister's appointment is not directly addressed in the Constitution but is a matter of convention and practice. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched.


**2. With reference to Special Category Status (SCS) in India, consider the following pairs:**

   State                                     Characteristic
1. Andhra Pradesh                            :   Granted SCS in 1969
2. Nagaland                                   :   Granted SCS based on Gadgil-Mukherjee formula
3. Jammu & Kashmir                          :   Received special funding based on 14th Finance Commission recommendations
4. Sikkim                                    :   Received SCS after 1969

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Nagaland was among the initial states granted Special Category Status (SCS) in 1969, along with Jammu & Kashmir and Assam.  The Gadgil-Mukherjee formula was indeed used for the distribution of grants to SCS states.  Jammu & Kashmir's special funding status, however, ceased to exist with the recommendations of the 14th Finance Commission. Sikkim was granted SCS after 1969. Andhra Pradesh was not granted SCS in 1969.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched.

(d) 2 and 3 only

**4. With reference to the Indian Judiciary and Legal Processes, consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Process/Petition                    Key Characteristic
1. Mercy Petition                            :   Article 137 governs its process
2. Curative Petition                         :   Last resort after review petition dismissal
3. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)      :   Exclusively handle cybercrimes
4. Alternative Dispute Resolution (ADR)   :   Settles disputes outside courtrooms


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 empowers the President's power to grant pardons, including mercy petitions, not Article 137 which relates to the Supreme Court's review power. Curative petitions are indeed the last recourse after review petitions are dismissed by the Supreme Court. FTSCs primarily focus on rape cases and POCSO Act cases, not exclusively cybercrimes. ADR mechanisms aim to resolve disputes outside traditional court settings.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched.


**5. With reference to Election Processes in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Concept/Mechanism                        Key Feature

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Model Code of Conduct lacks statutory backing; its enforcement relies on conventions and norms. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article                  Subject Matter
1. Article 270                           :   Taxes levied and collected by the Union, distributed between Union and States
2. Article 275                           :   Grants-in-aid provided by the Centre to States
3. Article 280                           :   Establishment of the Finance Commission
4. Article 292                           :   Union Government's power to borrow money within or outside India
5. Article 293                           :   State Government's power to borrow money within India


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 270 deals with the distribution of tax revenue between the Union and States. Article 275 empowers the Union to provide grants-in-aid to States. Article 280 mandates the establishment of the Finance Commission to advise on the distribution of resources. Article 292 grants the Union the power to borrow money both domestically and internationally. Article 293 allows State Governments to borrow within India, but not abroad, and requires prior Union consent if the State is already indebted to the Centre.  Therefore, option (c) encompassing all five pairs is the correct answer.  There are no inaccuracies or misleading information in any of the pairings.

   Financial Mechanism                     Characteristic/Source

The Model Code of Conduct (MCC) lacks statutory backing, making pair 1 incorrect.  The Election Commission of India (ECI), not the Union Ministry of Home Affairs, determines election schedules, making pair 2 incorrect. The ECI does resolve disputes related to party splits and mergers, making pair 3 correct. The President appoints the Chief Election Commissioner and Election Commissioners, making pair 4 correct.  Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Amendment                                  Key Provision
1.  91st Constitutional Amendment Act, 2003    :   Limited the size of the Council of Ministers to 15% of the Lok Sabha
2.  97th Constitutional Amendment Act, 2011    :   Made the right to form cooperative societies a fundamental right
3.  Citizenship Act, 1955                       :   Provides for dual citizenship
4. Disaster Management Act, 2005              :  Mandates the declaration of heatwaves as notified disasters


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The 91st Constitutional Amendment Act, 2003, correctly limited the size of the Council of Ministers to 15% of the Lok Sabha's total membership. The 97th Constitutional Amendment Act, 2011, correctly made the right to form cooperative societies a fundamental right. The Citizenship Act of 1955 does *not* provide for dual citizenship; it only allows for single citizenship, making pair 3 incorrect. The Disaster Management Act, 2005, does not mandate the declaration of heatwaves as notified disasters; this is a matter of policy and state-level implementation, making pair 4 incorrect. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched.


**5. With reference to the National Human Rights Commission (NHRC), consider the following pairs:**

   NHRC Aspect                                   Detail
1.  Headquarters                               :   Mumbai

3.  Appointment of Chairperson and Members   :  By the President, based on a committee's recommendation

(b) Only two
(c) Only one
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The NHRC's headquarters is in New Delhi, not Mumbai, making pair 1 incorrect. The NHRC was established under the Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993, making pair 2 correct. The President appoints the Chairperson and Members based on a committee's recommendation, making pair 3 correct. The tenure is three years or until age 70, not five years, making pair 4 incorrect. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  Option (b) is too broad, and options (c) and (d) include incorrect pairs.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Article of the Indian Constitution     Subject Matter
1. Article 72                        :   Power of the Governor to grant pardons
2. Article 137                       :   Power of the Supreme Court to review its own judgments
3. Article 142                       :   Power of the Supreme Court to do complete justice
4. Article 342A                      :   Power of the President to specify Socially and Educationally Backward Classes (SEBCs)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution deals with the power of the President, not the Governor, to grant pardons, reprieves, respites or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offence.  Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect. Article 137 grants the Supreme Court the power to review its own judgments.  This is accurate. Article 142 empowers the Supreme Court to do complete justice, which is also correct. Article 342A empowers the President to specify SEBCs, making pair 4 correct.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they include the incorrectly matched pair 1, or exclude the correctly matched pairs 3 and 4.  The correct option (c) accurately reflects the correct pairings of constitutional articles with their respective subject matters.  Understanding the specific powers vested in different constitutional bodies is crucial for comprehending the Indian political system's structure and functioning.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Concept/Doctrine             Description
1. Doctrine of Coverture             :   A legal doctrine that grants equal rights to married women.
2. Doctrine of Harmonious Construction:   A principle used to resolve conflicts between laws by interpreting them in a way that maintains the spirit of both.
3. Zero FIR                           :   An FIR registered in a police station other than the one having jurisdiction over the crime scene.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Doctrine of Coverture, originating in English common law, did *not* grant equal rights to married women; rather, it treated a married woman as a legal extension of her husband, suspending her legal existence. Thus, pair 1 is incorrect. The Doctrine of Harmonious Construction is accurately described as a principle for resolving legal conflicts by maintaining the essence of both conflicting laws.  Pair 2 is correct.  A Zero FIR is indeed registered regardless of the police station's jurisdiction and is later transferred to the appropriate station for investigation; pair 3 is correct. Option (b) is the only option that reflects the correct matching of the legal concepts with their descriptions.  Options (a), (c), and (d) contain the incorrectly matched pair 1, demonstrating the importance of understanding nuances in legal terminology and doctrines.


**3. With reference to the Indian Legal System, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Petition              Court/Authority
1. Mercy Petition                  :   Supreme Court
2. Curative Petition                :   High Court
3. Review Petition                  :   President

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Mercy petitions are addressed to the President (Article 72) or Governor (Article 161), not the Supreme Court.  Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect. Curative petitions are filed in the Supreme Court, not the High Court, as a last resort after a review petition is dismissed. Pair 2 is incorrect. Review petitions are filed in the Supreme Court (Article 137) to review its own judgments, not the President. Pair 3 is incorrect. All three pairs are incorrectly matched, making option (d) the correct answer.  This question highlights the importance of knowing the correct court or authority for different types of legal remedies in India. The distractors are designed to test the candidate's understanding of the hierarchy of courts and their jurisdictions.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Law                                      Key Feature
1.  Indian Telegraph Act, 1885                   :   Regulates postal services
2.  Post Office Act, 2023                        :   Repeals the Indian Wireless Telegraph Act, 1933
3.  The Citizenship Act, 1955                    :   Provides for dual citizenship

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Telegraph Act, 1885, deals with telegraphs, not postal services. The Post Office Act, 1898, regulates postal services. Thus, pair 1 is incorrect.  The Post Office Act, 2023, aims to modernize postal services and does indeed repeal the Indian Wireless Telegraph Act, 1933, along with the Indian Telegraph Act, 1885 as a part of its consolidation effort. Therefore, pair 2 is correct. The Citizenship Act, 1955, *does not* provide for dual citizenship; it outlines ways to acquire Indian citizenship.  Pair 3 is incorrect. Only pair 2 is correctly matched, making option (b) the correct answer.  This question tests knowledge of specific legislation and their key provisions, crucial for understanding the legal framework of India.  The distractors are designed to confuse candidates who may have a superficial understanding of these Acts.

   Position/Role                         Responsibility

(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Pro-tem Speaker's primary duty is indeed administering oaths to newly elected MPs.  Pair 1 is correct. The Deputy Speaker of Lok Sabha is elected by the Lok Sabha itself, not the Rajya Sabha. Pair 3 is incorrect.  Only pair 1 is correctly matched, making option (a) the correct answer. (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

Statement 3 accurately states the requirement of prior consultation with the Union Ministry of Finance for creating Class I or Class II posts in either secretariat. **2. With reference to the President's Address to Parliament, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision                                  Specific Application
1. Article 86                                              :  The President addressing both Houses together
2. Article 87                                              :  The President addressing Parliament at the beginning of every session
3. Article 87, post First Amendment of the Constitution   :  The President addressing at the beginning of the first session after each general election


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is correct because Articles 86 and 87, as amended, accurately reflect the provisions regarding the President's address to Parliament. Article 86 allows the President to address either House or both Houses together, although this specific provision has not been used to date.  Article 87, as amended by the First Amendment, specifies two instances for the President's address to both Houses assembled together—at the beginning of the first session after each general election and at the beginning of the first session of each year.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Before the First Amendment, Article 87 mandated an address at the commencement of every session.  However, this was subsequently amended to the current practice. The inclusion of this incorrect statement serves as a significant distractor, testing the candidate's knowledge of the constitutional amendments and their impact on parliamentary procedure.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they either omit correct statements or include the incorrect statement 2.



**3. With reference to the Election Commission of India (ECI) and the electoral process, consider the following pairs:**

    Legal Provision                                     Specific Application
1. Article 324                                          :  ECI's power of superintendence, direction, and control of elections
2. Article 329(b)                                       :  Limiting judicial intervention in the electoral process post-notification by ECI
3. Section 80 of the Representation of the People Act, 1951:  Challenging the validity of an election exclusively through an election petition


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. Article 324 of the Constitution vests the Election Commission of India (ECI) with the power of superintendence, direction, and control of all elections to Parliament and State Legislatures.  Article 329(b) of the Constitution restricts judicial intervention in the electoral process, particularly after the ECI officially notifies the election process. Section 80 of the Representation of the People Act, 1951, reinforces this by specifying that the validity of any election can only be challenged through an election petition.  There are no incorrect pairings in this question; therefore, options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect.  This question tests the candidate's detailed understanding of the legal framework governing elections in India.  The inclusion of all three correct pairings ensures that the candidate demonstrates a comprehensive understanding of the subject matter.

(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article                     Subject Matter related to Fiscal Federalism
1. Article 246                               : Defines tax bases between Union and States
2. Article 269                               : Taxes levied and collected by the Centre but wholly assigned to Panchayats
3. Article 270                               : Taxes levied and collected by the Union and distributed between Union and States based on the Finance Commission's recommendations
4. Article 280                               : Establishes the Finance Commission
5. Article 293                               : Grants the Union Government the power to borrow money both within and outside the country


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 246 correctly defines the division of tax bases between the Union and States, forming a cornerstone of India's fiscal federalism. Article 270 accurately describes the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the Union, a key aspect of revenue sharing. Article 280 correctly establishes the Finance Commission, responsible for recommending the distribution of resources. **Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 246 of the Indian Constitution clearly delineates the powers of the Union and the States regarding taxation. Article 269 deals with taxes levied and collected by the Union but assigned to the States, not the other way around. Article 270 correctly describes the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the Union among the States based on the Finance Commission's recommendations. Article 275 pertains to grants-in-aid from the Union to States, not borrowing powers outside India. The Union's power to borrow within and outside India is detailed in Article 292. Option (a) is the only one correctly matching the constitutional provisions with their features. Options (b), (c), and (d) include mismatched pairs, demonstrating a lack of understanding of the intricate details of India's fiscal federalism framework as enshrined in the Constitution.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of specific constitutional articles related to fiscal federalism.


**3. With reference to Cantonment Boards in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                                  Detail

(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Cantonments were established by the East India Company after the Battle of Plassey in 1757, making statement 1 correct.  However, the administrative control of Cantonment Boards rests with the Ministry of Defence, not the Ministry of Home Affairs, making statement 2 incorrect. Barrackpore (near Calcutta), not Madras, was the first Cantonment established in 1765. The approximate number of cantonments in India is 61, not 50.  Only statement 1 is correctly matched.  Options (a), (b), and (d) include incorrect information regarding the administrative control, the first cantonment, and the total number of cantonments. This question tests factual knowledge about Cantonment Boards, highlighting the importance of precise details in understanding their historical context and current administrative structure. **Explanation:**

Options (b), (c), and (d) contain incorrect interpretations or mismatched pairings of Articles with their interpretations in recent Supreme Court judgments related to environmental rights. **1. With reference to Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSS), consider the following pairs:**

   Scheme Feature
1. CSS Funding Pattern (North Eastern States) : 60:40 Centre:State
2. CSS Monitoring Jurisdiction                 :  Exclusively Ministry of Finance
3. CSS Implementation                         : Primarily through State Governments
4. CSS Funding Transfer Mechanism             : Through Consolidated Fund of India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only statement 3 is correct. Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSS) are implemented primarily through State Governments, leveraging their on-the-ground expertise and understanding of local contexts. The other statements are incorrect.  The funding pattern for North Eastern States is 90:10 (Centre:State), not 60:40.  NITI Aayog, along with the relevant ministries, has concurrent jurisdiction in monitoring CSSs, not solely the Ministry of Finance.  Finally, all transfers to States for CSSs are routed through the Consolidated Fund of the *State*, not the Consolidated Fund of India.  This ensures that the state government has direct control over the funds allocated for the scheme's implementation within their respective jurisdictions.


**2. With reference to the Aadhaar Act, 2016, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                     Characteristic
1. Aadhaar Metadata Storage Limit            :  Indefinitely
2. Aadhaar's Proof of Citizenship Status     :  Yes
3.  Targeted Delivery of Benefits               :  Mandatory Aadhaar for all schemes
4.  Constitutional Validity                    :  Upheld by the Supreme Court

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only statement 4 is correct. The Supreme Court, in its 2018 judgment, upheld the constitutionality of the Aadhaar Act, 2016, while also setting important limitations on its use.  The other statements are incorrect. Aadhaar metadata cannot be stored for more than six months. Aadhaar is not a proof of citizenship or domicile; it only serves as proof of identity and address for residents of India.  While Aadhaar is mandatory for accessing certain social welfare schemes, it cannot be forced for opening bank accounts or for mobile and internet connections.

**1. With reference to India's Fiscal Federalism, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision                     Specific Provision
    1. Article 270                               :  Taxes levied and collected by the Union, distributed between Union and States.
    2. Article 275                               :  Grants-in-aid provided by the Centre to States.
    3. Article 292                               :  State governments can borrow money from outside India.
    4. Article 280                               :  Establishes the Finance Commission to adjudicate the sharing of resources.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Articles 270 and 280 accurately reflect their descriptions in the provided text.  Article 270 deals with the distribution of tax revenues between the Union and States, a key aspect of fiscal federalism. Article 280 correctly describes the establishment and role of the Finance Commission.  Article 275 correctly states that the Centre provides grants-in-aid to states. However, Article 292 incorrectly states that state governments can borrow money from outside India; the text explicitly states that state governments can borrow only *within* India. This makes option (a) the only correct choice. Options (b), (c), and (d) contain inaccuracies regarding Article 292 and/or incomplete representation of the relevant articles.  The question tests factual recall of constitutional provisions related to India's fiscal federalism and the ability to identify inconsistencies in paired statements, showcasing a deep understanding of the subject matter.

(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Explanation:**

The Election Commission of India (ECI) first introduced the Model Code of Conduct (MCC) during Kerala's state assembly elections in 1960.  This is a well-established fact in Indian electoral history.  The MCC is a set of guidelines aimed at ensuring free and fair elections.

Option 2 is incorrect.  Bharat Electronics Limited (BEL) manufactures EVMs, but it falls under the Ministry of Defence, not the Ministry of Home Affairs. **2. With reference to the Indian Financial System, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                   Function/Characteristic
1. Finance Commission                       :   Recommends the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the union between the union and states based on Article 270.
2. 15th Finance Commission                 :   Allocated 41% of the divisible pool to states based on  criteria including Income Distance, Area, Population (2011), Demographic performance, Forest and Ecology, and Tax and fiscal efforts.
3. Article 293 of the Indian Constitution :   Grants state governments the power to borrow money both within and outside India.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Pair 1 is correctly matched. The Finance Commission plays a pivotal role in the Indian federal system by recommending the vertical and horizontal devolution of resources between the Union and State governments.  Article 270 of the Constitution provides the constitutional basis for this crucial function.  The recommendations of the Finance Commission significantly influence the fiscal balance between the Centre and the States.

Pair 2 is also correctly matched. The 15th Finance Commission indeed allocated 41% of the divisible pool to the states.  It employed a multi-faceted approach, considering various factors to ensure a more equitable distribution of resources among the states. The weighting assigned to different criteria reflects the Commission's attempt to balance various developmental needs and fiscal capacities of the states.

Pair 3 is incorrect. Article 293 of the Indian Constitution allows state governments to borrow money *within* India, not outside. The restriction on borrowing from foreign sources is a crucial aspect of India's fiscal management, aimed at maintaining macroeconomic stability and preventing excessive external debt.

The rationale behind these demands often involves arguments about historical disadvantages or specific developmental challenges faced by these states.

**4.  Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                                Feature
1. Aadhaar Act, 2016                       :   Declared Aadhaar mandatory for accessing all social welfare schemes
2. Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v. UoI judgment :   Affirmed the constitutionality of Aadhaar Act, 2016, but limited its mandatory use.
3. Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023 :   Explicitly includes the "right to be forgotten".


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Pair 1 is incorrect. While the Aadhaar Act allows for the use of Aadhaar in accessing social welfare schemes, the Supreme Court's judgment in *Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v. UoI* clarified that it cannot be made *mandatory* for all schemes. The judgment emphasized the importance of balancing the government's interest in using Aadhaar for efficient service delivery with the fundamental right to privacy.

Pair 2 is correctly matched. The Supreme Court's judgment in *Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v. UoI* upheld the constitutionality of the Aadhaar Act but also imposed significant limitations on its use, notably concerning data protection and the right to privacy.  This decision underscores the importance of judicial review in safeguarding fundamental rights in the context of technological advancements.

Pair 3 is incorrect.  The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023 does not include the "right to be forgotten," a concept found in the European Union's General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR).  The absence of this right in Indian law reflects ongoing debates about data privacy and the balance between individual rights and the needs of the government and businesses.

Pair 2 is correctly matched. GANHRI, a UN-linked alliance, indeed accredits National Human Rights Institutions (NHRIs) based on their adherence to the Paris Principles, a set of international standards for NHRIs.  This accreditation process aims to enhance the credibility and effectiveness of NHRIs worldwide.

Pair 3 is incorrect. The NHRC's accreditation from GANHRI has been deferred, not an 'A' status. This highlights the ongoing concerns about the NHRC's performance and compliance with international standards. The deferral underscores the importance of continuous evaluation and improvement in the work of human rights institutions.


**8. Consider the following pairs:**

   Scheme/Initiative                           Key Feature
1. Mission Karmayogi                         :   Aims to create a professional, well-trained civil service based on a role-based approach to training.

(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Mission Karmayogi is a significant initiative aimed at modernizing the Indian civil service by shifting from a rule-based to a role-based approach to training and capacity building. This participatory approach aims to ensure that development plans are more responsive to local needs and priorities.

Pair 3 is incorrect. The Capacity Building Commission (CBC) was launched in 2021, not 2022, as part of the National Programme for Civil Services Capacity Building (NPCSCB), which is a key component of Mission Karmayogi. **1. With reference to the President's powers regarding mercy petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Article                                      Power Granted
1. Article 72                               :  Grant pardons for offences under state laws only
2. Article 72                               :  Commute death sentences
3. Article 142                              :  Oversee the President's pardon power
4. Article 280                              :  Adjudicate on mercy petitions in cases of national security

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit, or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offense. This includes offences against Union laws and death sentences.  Therefore, pair 2 is correctly matched.  Article 142 deals with the Supreme Court's power to do complete justice, it doesn't oversee presidential pardon powers. Article 280 deals with the establishment of the Finance Commission, not mercy petitions.  Pair 1 is incorrect as Article 72 encompasses offences under both Union and State laws. Pair 4 is completely unrelated.  Option (b) is the only correct choice because it accurately reflects the power granted to the President under Article 72 concerning the commutation of death sentences.


**2. With reference to Curative Petitions in the Supreme Court of India, consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Concept                                  Description
1. Review Petition (Article 137)              :  Filed after a curative petition is dismissed.
2. Curative Petition                           :  Last available constitutional remedy after review petition dismissal.
3. Doctrine of Harmonious Construction        :  Used to interpret conflicting provisions in the Limitation Act, in relation to curative petitions.
4. Principles of Natural Justice               :  Violation can be a ground for a curative petition.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

A curative petition is indeed the last resort available to a litigant after their review petition has been dismissed by the Supreme Court.  This makes pair 2 correct.  A violation of principles of natural justice, such as a judge failing to disclose a conflict of interest, can be grounds for a curative petition, making pair 4 correct.  Pair 1 is incorrect because a review petition is filed *before* a curative petition, not after.  While the Doctrine of Harmonious Construction might be relevant in legal interpretation generally, its direct connection to curative petitions is not established in the provided context. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched.  Option (d) incorrectly includes pairs 1 and 3.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article          Provision Related To
1. Article 72                      :   President's power to grant pardons

   Concept/Policy                     Description

**1. With reference to Constitutional Provisions related to the President's Powers, consider the following pairs:**

    Article                                       Power Granted
    1. Article 72                                : Power to grant pardons in cases of offences against laws relating to matters under the executive power of the Union
    2. Article 142                               : Power to issue curative petitions
    3. Article 137                               : Power to review a Supreme Court judgment
    4. Article 22                                : Power to make laws on preventive detention

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit, or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offense. This power extends to cases where the sentence is by a court-martial, for an offense against any law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends, or a death sentence.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

Article 142 empowers the Supreme Court to do complete justice, which includes the power to pass curative petitions as a last resort.  However, the power is inherent in the Supreme Court's jurisdiction, not explicitly mentioned in Article 142 itself. Article 137 deals with the Supreme Court's power of review of its own judgments, not directly related to the President's powers.  Article 22 allows for the Parliament and State Legislatures to create laws regarding preventive detention, a separate subject from the President's pardoning power. Therefore, only pair 1 and 4 are accurately matched.  Pairs 2 and 3 represent a misunderstanding of the constitutional provisions.


**2. With reference to the Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs), consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                                     Detail
    1. Type of Scheme                           : Centrally sponsored scheme launched in 2019
    2. Funding Source                            : Nirbhaya Fund
    3. Implementing Ministry                    : Ministry of Home Affairs
    4. Primary Objective                         : Swift disposal of POCSO Act cases

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

FTSCs are indeed a centrally sponsored scheme launched in 2019 and extended until 2026 (pair 1).  The funding for FTSCs comes from the Nirbhaya Fund (pair 2).  Their primary objective is the swift disposal of rape cases and those under the POCSO Act (pair 4). However, the implementing ministry is the Department of Justice, under the Ministry of Law and Justice, not the Ministry of Home Affairs (pair 3).  Therefore, options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they include the incorrectly matched pair 3. Only pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched.


**3. With reference to Internet Shutdowns in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Aspect                                      Detail
    1. Governing Legislation                     : Indian Telegraph Act, 1885
    2. Rules for Suspension                      : Temporary Suspension of Telecom Services Rules, 2017
    3. Authority for Issuing Orders              :  District Magistrates
    4. Supreme Court Ruling (Anuradha Bhasin): Indefinite suspension is permissible

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Internet shutdowns in India are primarily governed by the Indian Telegraph Act, 1885, and the Temporary Suspension of Telecom Services (Public Emergency or Public Safety) Rules, 2017 (pairs 1 and 2).  The Supreme Court ruling in Anuradha Bhasin v. Union of India explicitly stated that indefinite suspension of internet services is impermissible.  Therefore, pair 4 is incorrect.  Orders for temporary suspension are issued by the Union/State Home Secretary, not District Magistrates (pair 3).  Consequently, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched.



**4. With reference to the Common Service Centres (CSCs), consider the following pairs:**

    Aspect                                       Detail
    1. Establishment Year                         : 2006
    2. Overseeing Body                           : CSC Special Purpose Vehicle (SPV)
    3. Parent Ministry                            : Ministry of Electronics & IT
    4. One of the Pillars of NeGP                 : National Data Bank/State Data Centres

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The CSC SPV oversees the implementation of the CSC scheme (pair 2), and the Ministry of Electronics & IT set up the CSC SPV (pair 3). However, CSCs are one of the three pillars of the National e-Governance Plan (NeGP) approved in 2006, not established in 2006 itself (pair 1).  The other two pillars include Connectivity and National Data Bank/State Data Centres (pair 4).  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  Pairs 1 and 4 are incorrect due to a misunderstanding of the timeline and components of NeGP.


**5. With reference to Affirmative Action in India and the US, consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                                      India                                  US
    1. Constitutional Basis                     : Explicitly provided for                  Not explicitly enshrined but permitted under 14th Amendment
    2. Primary Targeted Groups                  : Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes   African Americans, Hispanics, Asian Americans
    3. System                                     : Quota System                           Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion (DEI) programs
    4. Legal Upper Ceiling on Reservations     : 50%                                     No legal upper limit

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Constitution explicitly provides for affirmative action through Articles 15(4) and 16(4), while the US Constitution doesn't explicitly mention it but allows for it through interpretations of the Equal Protection Clause of the 14th Amendment (pair 1).  In India, affirmative action primarily targets Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes, along with other Backward Classes, while in the US, it focuses on historically disadvantaged groups like African Americans, Hispanics, and Asian Americans (pair 2). India primarily uses a quota system, while the US employs DEI programs (pair 3).  The Supreme Court of India has set a 50% upper limit on reservations, while there's no such legal limit in the US (pair 4). All the pairs are correctly matched.




**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article          Provision Related To
1. Article 72                     :   Power of the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute death sentences
2. Article 137                    :   Review petitions in the Supreme Court
3. Article 142                    :   Power of the Supreme Court to do complete justice
4. Article 215                    :   Power of High Courts to punish for contempt of court
5. Article 282                    :   Power of the Centre and states to make grants for any public purpose

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 72 explicitly grants the President the power to pardon, reprieve, respite, or commute sentences, including death sentences. Article 137 deals with the Supreme Court's power to review its own judgments, forming the basis for review petitions.  Article 142 empowers the Supreme Court to ensure complete justice, a power often invoked in curative petitions. Article 215 bestows upon High Courts the power to punish for contempt. Finally, Article 282 provides the constitutional basis for discretionary grants by both the central and state governments for public purposes, often seen in special financial packages for states.  There is no mismatch or inaccuracy in any of the provided pairs.


**2. With reference to the Indian judicial system, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Petition                Court/Remedy
1. Mercy Petition                  :   High Court
2. Curative Petition               :   Supreme Court
3. Contempt Petition              :   Supreme Court or High Court
4. Review Petition                 :   Supreme Court
5. Appeal against CAT order        :   High Court only


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Mercy petitions are addressed to the President of India, not the High Court. Curative petitions are a final remedy available in the Supreme Court. Contempt petitions can be filed in either the Supreme Court or High Courts, depending on the nature of the contempt. Review petitions are indeed filed in the Supreme Court. Appeals against Central Administrative Tribunal (CAT) orders primarily lie with the Supreme Court, not High Courts, as clarified by a Supreme Court judgment. Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   State                                     Status under Foreigners Act, 1963
1. Arunachal Pradesh                       : Entirely a Protected Area
2. Sikkim                                  : Partly Restricted Area, Partly Protected Area

4. Andaman & Nicobar Islands               : Entirely a Restricted Area

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Foreigners (Protected Areas) Order, 1958, and the Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963, delineate specific areas within India where the entry and stay of foreigners are regulated.  Arunachal Pradesh, Sikkim, and the Andaman & Nicobar Islands fall under these regulations.  Arunachal Pradesh is entirely a Protected Area,  Sikkim has a portion designated as a Restricted Area and another as a Protected Area, and the Andaman & Nicobar Islands are entirely a Restricted Area.  Jammu & Kashmir, while having protected areas, isn't entirely designated as such under these specific orders.  Therefore, only options 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched. Option (a) is partially correct but misses the entirely restricted status of the Andaman & Nicobar Islands. Option (b) is incorrect because it omits Arunachal Pradesh’s entirely protected status. The question tests factual recall regarding the specific legal designations of different Indian states concerning foreign entry restrictions.
