**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article             Provision Related To
1. Article 72                       :   Power of the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute death sentences
2. Article 137                      :   Review petitions in the Supreme Court
3. Article 142                      :   Power of the Supreme Court to do complete justice
4. Article 244(2)                   :   Establishment of Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs)
5. Article 282                      :   Discretionary grants by the Centre and states


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to pardon, reprieve, respite, or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offense, including those sentenced to death.  This power is a crucial aspect of executive clemency. Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments, allowing for reconsideration of decisions.  Article 142 provides the Supreme Court with the power to ensure complete justice, enabling it to issue orders necessary for the effective execution of its judgments. Article 244(2) forms the basis for the establishment and functioning of Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs) in certain states, primarily in the Northeast.  Article 282 empowers both the central and state governments to make grants for any public purpose, even if it falls outside their legislative powers; this is often used for special financial packages. Therefore, all the pairs are correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Remedy                     Description
1. Mercy Petition                  :   A petition to the President for clemency in a death sentence case
2. Curative Petition                :   Last resort legal remedy after review petition dismissal in the Supreme Court
3. Contempt of Court                :   Wilful disobedience to court orders, defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971
4. Review Petition                  :   A petition to review a Supreme Court judgment
5. Gram Nyayalaya                  :   A court established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, to settle petty disputes.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

A mercy petition is a plea made to the President of India for pardon or commutation of a sentence, often in capital punishment cases.  A curative petition is a last resort for those whose review petition has been rejected by the Supreme Court. Contempt of court is an offense against the authority of a court, encompassing both civil and criminal contempt, and is governed by the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971. Review petitions are a mechanism within the Supreme Court's system for reviewing its own judgments. Gram Nyayalayas are village-level courts established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, with jurisdiction over minor civil and criminal disputes.  All five pairs accurately reflect the legal remedies and their descriptions.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Order/Regulation           Key Feature
1. Bengal Eastern Frontier Regulations of 1873  :   Genesis of the Inner Line Permit (ILP) system
2. Foreigners (Protected Areas) Order, 1958     :   Declaration of Protected Areas in certain states
3. Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963    :   Declaration of Restricted Areas, including Andaman & Nicobar Islands
4. Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008                 :   Establishment of village-level courts
5. The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023 :   Includes the "right to be forgotten"


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Bengal Eastern Frontier Regulations of 1873 laid the foundation for the Inner Line Permit (ILP) system in certain regions of Northeast India. The Foreigners (Protected Areas) Order, 1958, established the framework for designating Protected Areas within various states, restricting access to certain regions. The Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963, further defined Restricted Areas, notably including the entire Andaman and Nicobar Islands. The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, led to the creation of village-level courts to handle minor disputes. The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, does *not* include the "right to be forgotten," a provision found in other jurisdictions like the European Union's GDPR.  Therefore, options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.  Option (c) accurately reflects the correct matches.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Court                Jurisdiction
1. Supreme Court               :   Final appellate jurisdiction in civil and criminal matters
2. High Courts                   :   Appellate jurisdiction over subordinate courts within their respective states
3. Gram Nyayalayas              :   Jurisdiction over petty civil and criminal disputes at the village level
4. Fast-Track Special Courts     :   Primarily handle rape and POCSO Act cases
5. Court of Session              :   Jurisdiction over appeals from Gram Nyayalayas in criminal cases


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Supreme Court of India serves as the apex court with final appellate jurisdiction in both civil and criminal cases. High Courts have appellate jurisdiction over lower courts within their respective states or union territories. Gram Nyayalayas, established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, deal with petty civil and criminal matters at the village level. Fast-Track Special Courts are specifically designed to expedite the handling of rape cases and those under the Protection of Children from Sexual Offences (POCSO) Act. Courts of Session hear appeals from Gram Nyayalayas in criminal cases. Consequently, all the pairs are accurately matched.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incomplete and therefore incorrect.

   State/Union Territory          Special Constitutional Provision

   Body                                          Key Function/Power

3. Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) Act, 2023    :  Establishes the Data Protection Board of India (DPBI).

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The 2020 amendment to the FCRA introduced mandatory Aadhaar submission for NGO office-bearers and requires prior permission for receiving foreign funds.  The Post Office Act, 2023, explicitly repealed the 1998 Act, signifying a significant change in postal regulations. The Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) Act, 2023, indeed establishes the DPBI to oversee data protection and compliance.  Option (d) is incorrect because the Public Examinations (Prevention of Unfair Means) Rules, 2024, deal with preventing cheating in public exams, not data breaches; penalties for data breaches are specified under the DPDP Act. Options (a) and (c) are partially correct but incomplete, missing crucial elements of the correct pairings.  Therefore, only options 1, 2, and 3 are accurately matched.


**2. With reference to the Indian financial framework, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision/Entity                         Feature
1. Article 270                                          :  Distribution of taxes between Union and States
2. 15th Finance Commission                             :   41% share of divisible pool allocated to states.
3. Article 293                                          :  States can borrow money from foreign sources.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Article 270 of the Indian Constitution deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain taxes between the Union and the States.  The 15th Finance Commission's recommendation of a 41% share of the divisible pool for states is a well-established fact.  However, Article 293 allows state governments to borrow *within* India, not from foreign sources. This makes option (d) incorrect.  Options (b) and (c) are incomplete as they omit one of the correctly matched pairs. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched.

**1. With reference to the Aadhaar Act, 2016, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                      Court Ruling (Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v UoI)

2. Violation of fundamental rights (Articles 14, 15, 19, 21) :   Affirmed

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Supreme Court's 2018 judgment in Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v UoI upheld the constitutionality of the Aadhaar Act, 2016, but with crucial stipulations.  Option 2 correctly reflects that the court found the Act did not violate fundamental rights guaranteed under Articles 14, 15, 19, and 21. However, the court imposed significant limitations.  Option 1 is incorrect; the court ruled that Aadhaar metadata could not be stored for more than six months. Option 3 is incorrect because the court explicitly stated that Aadhaar could not be forced for opening bank accounts or mobile/internet connections.  Option 4 is also incorrect; the court prohibited the state from entering into contracts with private corporations for Aadhaar data sharing, emphasizing the right to privacy.  Therefore, only option (b) accurately reflects a single correctly matched pair.


**2. With reference to Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSS), consider the following pairs:**

   Aspect                                         Characteristic

**3. With reference to the Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA), 2019, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                     Detail
1. Illegal Migrants Exempted                    :   Those from Sri Lanka, Myanmar, and China

3. Exempted from Adverse Penal Consequences   :   Passport (Entry into India) Act, 1920 and Foreigners Act, 1946
4. Grounds for OCI Registration Cancellation  :   Ten grounds specified

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The CAA, 2019, exempts specific groups of illegal migrants, but these are from Afghanistan, Bangladesh, and Pakistan, not Sri Lanka, Myanmar, and China. Thus, option 1 is incorrect.  The Act did reduce the naturalization period for specified migrants from 11 years to 5 years, making option 2 correct. **4. With reference to the President's power on mercy petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Article                                         Application
1. Article 72                                  :   Pardon for offences against state laws only
2.  Article 72                                  :   Commutation of death sentences
3.  Article 142                               :   Granting mercy petitions
4. Article 142                               :   Power to do complete justice

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to commute a sentence of any person convicted of any offence against any law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends, including death sentences. Therefore, option 2 is correct. Option 1 is incorrect as Article 72 covers a broader range of offenses. Article 142 is not directly related to granting mercy petitions; its primary focus is the Supreme Court's power to do complete justice, as correctly stated in option 4.  Therefore, only options 2 and 4 are correctly matched.


**5. With reference to the Contempt of Court Act, 1971, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Contempt                                 Description
1. Civil Contempt                               :   Publication of scandalous matter about a court
2. Criminal Contempt                             :   Wilful disobedience of a court order
3. Civil Contempt                               :   Interference with the administration of justice
4. Criminal Contempt                             :   Wilful breach of an undertaking given to a court

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Civil contempt involves willful disobedience of court orders or breach of undertakings given to the court.  Therefore, option 2 is incorrect, and option 4 is correct. Criminal contempt involves publishing matter that scandalizes or lowers the authority of any court or interferes with the administration of justice.  Therefore, option 1 is incorrect, and option 3 is correct.  Hence, only options 2 and 4 are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Provision                                  Key Feature
1. Aadhaar Act, 2016                           :   Metadata retention limited to six months
2. Citizenship Act, 1955                        :   Acquisition of citizenship through naturalization
3. Citizenship (Amendment) Rules, 2024        :   Reduced naturalization period for specified migrants
4. Contempt of Courts Act, 1971                :   Defines civil and criminal contempt
5. Telecommunications Act, 2023               :   Spectrum allocation through auction

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  The Aadhaar Act, 2016, notably limits the storage of Aadhaar metadata to a maximum of six months, a crucial aspect of privacy protection affirmed by the Supreme Court. The Citizenship Act, 1955, outlines the various ways an individual can acquire Indian citizenship, including naturalization, a process involving fulfilling specific residency and other requirements. The Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, provides a legal framework defining and addressing civil and criminal contempt of court. Therefore, option (c) encompassing all five correctly matched pairs is the accurate response.


**2. With reference to the Indian Constitution and related laws, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision/Act                                   Key Aspect

**1. With reference to the Indian Judicial System, consider the following pairs:**

   Court Order                                  Legal Provision/Concept
1. Mercy Petition Rejection                     : Article 142
2. Curative Petition                             : Article 72
3. Contempt of Court Punishment                : Articles 129 and 215
4. Gram Nyayalaya Jurisdiction                  : Indian Evidence Act, 1872

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The President's power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute sentences, including death sentences, is enshrined in **Article 72** of the Indian Constitution.  Therefore, the rejection of a mercy petition falls under this article.  A curative petition is the last resort available to a litigant after the Supreme Court has dismissed their review petition.  This remedy is rooted in the Supreme Court's inherent power under **Article 142** to do complete justice. The power of the Supreme Court and High Courts to punish for contempt is derived from **Articles 129 and 215**, respectively.  Gram Nyayalayas, while not strictly bound by the Indian Evidence Act, 1872, operate under principles of natural justice.  Therefore, option (d) is the only correct pairing. Option (a) is incorrect because Article 142 relates to the curative petition, not the mercy petition. Option (b) is incorrect as Article 72 deals with mercy petitions, not contempt of court. Option (c) is incorrect because both pairs 2 and 4 are incorrectly matched; Article 72 is concerned with the President’s power of pardon and Gram Nyayalayas are not directly governed by the Indian Evidence Act, 1872.

(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

EVMs are manufactured by both Bharat Electronics Limited and Electronics Corporation of India Limited.  Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. VVPATs were first fully deployed in the 2019 Lok Sabha General Elections, not the 2017 Goa Assembly Elections, making statement 2 incorrect. The Model Code of Conduct was indeed first introduced in 1960 during Kerala Assembly Elections; thus, statement 3 is correct. Consequently, only statement 3 is correctly matched, making (b) the correct answer.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article             Provision Related To
1. Article 270                        :   Taxes levied and collected by the Union, wholly assigned to States
2. Article 275                        :   Grants-in-aid provided by the Union to States
3. Article 280                        :   Establishment of the Finance Commission
4. Article 292                        :   Union government's power to borrow money within or outside India
5. Article 293                        :   State government's power to borrow money only within India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 270 deals with the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the Union but assigned to the States. Article 275 outlines the Union's power to provide grants-in-aid to states. Article 280 mandates the establishment of the Finance Commission to recommend the distribution of financial resources. Article 292 grants the Union government the power to borrow both domestically and internationally, while Article 293 restricts state governments to borrowing only within India.  These articles are fundamental to understanding India's fiscal federalism and the distribution of financial resources between the Union and States.  Options (a), (b), and (d) incorrectly omit one or more of the correctly matched pairs, demonstrating a lack of complete understanding of the constitutional provisions related to fiscal federalism.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Finance Commission Recommendation    Feature
1. 15th Finance Commission             :   Vertical Devolution of 41% to States
2. 14th Finance Commission             :   Abolition of Special Category Status
3. 5th Finance Commission              :   Introduction of Special Category Status
4. Gadgil-Mukherjee Formula           :   Used for grants to Special Category States

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. The 15th Finance Commission recommended a vertical devolution of 41% of the divisible pool to the states.  The 14th Finance Commission recommended the abolition of the Special Category Status (SCS) for states. The 5th Finance Commission introduced the concept of SCS.  The Gadgil-Mukherjee formula was the basis for providing grants to states with SCS. These points are crucial for understanding the evolution of fiscal federalism in India and the changing mechanisms for resource allocation between the Union and States. Any option that omits one or more of these correctly matched pairs shows an incomplete grasp of the subject matter.


**3. With reference to the Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

   Scheduled Area              State
1.  Whole of Arunachal Pradesh   :   Arunachal Pradesh
2. Parts of Himachal Pradesh     :   Himachal Pradesh
3. Parts of Jammu & Kashmir      :   Jammu & Kashmir
4. Parts of Rajasthan            :   Rajasthan
5. Parts of Uttarakhand          :   Uttarakhand

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched. The Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution deals with the administration of tribal areas in certain states.  Arunachal Pradesh is entirely a scheduled area.  Parts of Himachal Pradesh, Jammu & Kashmir, Rajasthan, and Uttarakhand are also designated as scheduled areas under the Sixth Schedule.  Therefore, each pair accurately reflects the relationship between the scheduled area and the respective state.  Options (a), (c), and (d) demonstrate a partial or incomplete understanding of the geographical extent of scheduled areas under the Sixth Schedule.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Borrowing              Entity Allowed To Borrow
1. Borrowing within India         :   Union Government
2. Borrowing within India         :   State Government
3. Borrowing outside India        :   Union Government
4. Borrowing outside India        :   State Government
5. Borrowing without Union Consent:   State Government already indebted to Union


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. The Union Government can borrow both within and outside India (Articles 292). State Governments are allowed to borrow only within India (Article 293).  A state already indebted to the Union needs its consent for further borrowing (Article 293).  Pair 4 is incorrect as state governments cannot borrow outside India.  Therefore, only options 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) incorrectly include one or more of the mismatched pairs, demonstrating a misunderstanding of the constitutional restrictions on borrowing powers of the Union and State governments.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Tax Type                           Levied and Collected By
1. Corporation Tax                     :   Union Government
2. Personal Income Tax                 :   Union Government
3. Central Goods and Services Tax (CGST):   Union Government
4. State Goods and Services Tax (SGST):   State Government
5. Integrated Goods and Services Tax (IGST):  Union Government


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched. Corporation tax, personal income tax, and CGST are levied and collected by the Union Government. SGST is levied and collected by the State Governments.  IGST, applicable on inter-state trade, is levied and collected by the Union Government. These are key components of India's tax structure and understanding their allocation is crucial for comprehending the fiscal relationship between the Union and the States.  Any option that omits one or more of the correctly matched pairs indicates an incomplete understanding of the Indian tax system.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision                  Subject Matter
1. Article 270                               :  Taxes levied and collected by the Union, wholly assigned to States
2. Article 292                               :  Borrowing powers of State Governments outside India
3. Article 275                               :  Grants-in-aid provided by the Union to States
4. Article 280                               :  Establishment of a body to adjudicate disputes between the Union and States regarding the distribution of financial resources


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 270 of the Indian Constitution deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain taxes between the Union and the States.  While the Union levies and collects these taxes, a portion is allocated to the States.  Option 1 is thus correct. Article 292 empowers the Union government to borrow money both within and outside India, while State governments are only permitted to borrow within India. This makes option 2 incorrect.  Article 275 mandates that the Union shall provide grants-in-aid to States to ensure that they can meet their financial responsibilities and provide essential services.  Option 3 is therefore correct.  Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission, a constitutional body responsible for recommending the principles governing the distribution of the net proceeds of certain taxes and the grants-in-aid to the States. This makes option 4 correct.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Financial Parameter                      Value (as of March 2023 or as stated)
1.  States’ revenue expenditure met from their own revenue sources     : 73%
2.  Share of states from divisible pool (based on 15th FC recommendations) : 51%
3. Debt-GDP ratio of states                     : 27.5%
4. Weight assigned to Income Distance by 15th FC in horizontal devolution : 55%


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The provided text states that states only meet 58% of their revenue expenditure from their own revenue sources. This makes option 1 incorrect. The share of states from the divisible pool, according to the 15th Finance Commission, is 41%, not 51%. Option 2 is therefore incorrect. The debt-GDP ratio of states as of March 2023 is correctly stated as 27.5% in the text, making option 3 correct. The 15th Finance Commission assigned a weight of 45%, not 55%, to Income Distance in horizontal devolution. This makes option 4 incorrect.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   State                  Special Status/Demand
1. Bihar                     : Granted Special Category Status in 1969
2. Andhra Pradesh          : Demanded Special Category Status
3. Jammu & Kashmir        : Granted Special Category Status in 1969


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(b) 2 and 3 only

(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

Bihar was not granted Special Category Status (SCS) in 1969.  The states granted SCS in 1969 were Jammu & Kashmir, Assam, and Nagaland. Therefore, option 1 is incorrect.  Andhra Pradesh did indeed demand Special Category Status, making option 2 correct. Jammu & Kashmir was correctly identified as receiving SCS in 1969, making option 3 correct.

**1. With reference to Cantonment Boards in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Cantonment Feature                                  Fact
1. First Cantonment established                 :   Barrackpore in 1765
2. Number of Cantonments post-independence establishment :   6
3. Governing Act                                   :   Cantonments Act, 2006
4. Administrative Control                       :   Ministry of Home Affairs
5. Ex-officio President of Cantonment Board    :   Local MLA


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The first cantonment, Barrackpore, was indeed established in 1765 by the East India Company.  Six new cantonments were established in India after independence, adding to the existing number. The Cantonments Act, 2006, governs the administration of cantonments.  However, the administrative control of cantonments rests with the Ministry of Defence, not the Ministry of Home Affairs. The Station Commander of the cantonment serves as the ex-officio President of the Cantonment Board, not a locally elected MLA. Therefore, options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect due to the mismatching of administrative control and the President of the Cantonment Board. Option (b) correctly identifies the accurate matching of pairs 1, 2, and 3.


**2. With reference to the National Human Rights Commission (NHRC), consider the following pairs:**

    NHRC Feature                                        Fact
1. Establishment Act                               :   Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993
2. Appointment of Chairperson and Members        :   Parliamentary Committee
3. Tenure of Chairperson and Members               :   Five years, or until age 70, whichever is earlier
4. Removal from Office                            :   By the President after consultation with the Lok Sabha
5. Powers of NHRC                                :   Powers equivalent to a High Court


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The NHRC was indeed established under the Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993 (as amended).  The Chairperson and members are appointed by the President of India on the recommendations of a committee headed by the Prime Minister, not a parliamentary committee. The tenure is three years or until age 70, not five years. Removal is by Presidential order after consultation with the Supreme Court, not the Lok Sabha. The NHRC possesses powers similar to a civil court under the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, not equivalent to a High Court.  Only pair 1 is correctly matched, making (a) the correct answer. Options (b), (c), and (d) include incorrectly matched pairs.


**3. With reference to the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, consider the following pairs:**

    Act Feature                                    Fact
1.  Regulatory Body                             :   Data Protection Board of India (DPBI)
2.  Appeal Mechanism                            :   Telecom Disputes Settlement and Appellate Tribunal (TDSAT)
3.  Penalty for violation of Data Principal's duties:   Up to ₹50,000
4.  Data Fiduciary Obligation                    :  Appoint a data protection officer
5.  Exemption from Data Principal's rights        :  Notified agencies in the interest of national security


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 5 only
(b) 1 and 5 only
(c) 1, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Data Protection Board of India (DPBI) is the regulatory body as per the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023. Appeals against DPBI decisions go to the Telecom Disputes Settlement and Appellate Tribunal (TDSAT).  The penalty for violation of a data principal's duties is up to ₹10,000, not ₹50,000. Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDFs) are required to appoint a data protection officer.  Exemptions from data principal rights apply to notified agencies for national security reasons.  Thus, only pairs 1, 4, and 5 are correctly matched, making (c) the correct option.  Options (a), (b), and (d) contain incorrectly matched pairs.


**4. With reference to Presidential Powers in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Presidential Power                                   Legal Basis
1.  Granting Pardons                               :   Article 72
2.  Proclaiming Emergency                           :   Article 352
3.  Appointing the Chief Justice of India           :   Article 124
4.  Addressing Joint Sessions of Parliament         :   Article 87
5.  Dissolving the Lok Sabha                         :   Article 85


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit, or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offence. Article 352 deals with the power of the President to proclaim an Emergency. Article 124 outlines the appointment of the Chief Justice of India by the President.  Article 87 allows the President to address joint sittings of Parliament. Finally, Article 85 grants the President the power to dissolve the Lok Sabha.  Therefore, all pairs are correctly matched, making (c) the correct option.  Other options incorrectly exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.


**5. With reference to the Finance Commission of India, consider the following pairs:**

    Finance Commission Feature                        Fact
1.  Constitutional Provision                         :   Article 280
2.  Vertical Devolution Basis                       :   Recommendations of the 14th Finance Commission
3.  Horizontal Devolution Criteria                  :   Population (2011 Census) is a criterion
4.  Grants-in-Aid                                 :   Provided under Article 275
5.  State Borrowing from abroad                    :   Allowed without Union Government consent


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Finance Commission's establishment is mandated by Article 280 of the Constitution.  Population (2011 Census) is one of several criteria used for horizontal devolution.  Grants-in-aid are indeed provided under Article 275. However, the vertical devolution basis is not solely based on the 14th Finance Commission's recommendations; it evolves with each commission's report. States are not permitted to borrow from abroad without the Union Government's consent. Hence, only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched, making (a) the correct option.  The other options include incorrectly matched pairs.


**6. With reference to Special Category Status (SCS) in India, consider the following pairs:**

    SCS Feature                                      Fact
1.  First introduction of SCS                       :   1969
2.  Basis for granting SCS                         :   Geographical and socio-economic disadvantages
3.  Constitutional Provision for SCS                 :   Article 370
4.  Funding mechanism for SCS states               :   Gadgil-Mukherjee formula (currently)
5.  Current Status of SCS                          :   No longer granted to any state


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 5 only
(b) 1 and 5 only
(c) 2 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Special Category Status (SCS) was first introduced in 1969 based on the recommendations of the Fifth Finance Commission. The basis for granting SCS was indeed geographical and socio-economic disadvantages.  There is no specific constitutional provision dedicated solely to SCS; however,  various provisions under Articles 371 and related articles provide special provisions to certain states. The Gadgil-Mukherjee formula was used for funding SCS states, but this is no longer applicable as the concept of SCS, as officially designated, no longer exists, and  no state currently holds the official designation of SCS. Therefore, pairs 1, 2, and 5 are correctly matched, making (a) the correct answer.  The other options contain incorrectly matched pairs.


**7. With reference to the Code of Criminal Procedure (CrPC), 1973, consider the following pairs:**

    CrPC Feature                                      Fact
1.  Forensic Investigation                           :   Mandatory for offences punishable with at least 3 years of imprisonment
2.  Specimen Collection                             :   Magistrate can order any person to provide specimen signatures
3.  Joint Trials                                   :   Allowed only when all accused are present
4.  Timelines for Procedures                       :   Specified for submission of medical reports
5.  Replacing Act                                  :   Indian Evidence Act, 1872


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The CrPC, 1973, mandates forensic investigation for offences punishable with at least seven years, not three years, of imprisonment.  Magistrates can order specimen collection (signatures, handwriting, etc.).  Joint trials can proceed even if some accused are absent.  Timelines are indeed specified for various procedures, including medical report submission.  The CrPC, 1973, did not replace the Indian Evidence Act, 1872;  the Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, replaced the Indian Evidence Act, 1872.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched, making (a) the correct answer. Other options include at least one incorrectly matched pair.


**8. With reference to Articles 14 and 21 of the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

    Article                                          Interpretation by Supreme Court
1.  Article 14                                      :   Right to Equality includes right to be free from adverse effects of climate change.
2.  Article 21                                      :   Right to Life includes right to a healthy environment
3.  Article 14                                      :   Guarantees equality before the law and equal protection of the laws
4.  Article 21                                      :   Right to Life encompasses right to livelihood
5.  Article 21                                      :   Right to Life includes the right to privacy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Supreme Court has interpreted Article 14 to include the right to be free from the adverse effects of climate change. Article 21's right to life has been expanded to include the right to a healthy environment and the right to livelihood.  Article 21 also encompasses the right to privacy. Article 14 does guarantee equality before the law and equal protection of the laws. Therefore, pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched, making (c) the correct answer. Other options incorrectly exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.  The core issue here is the understanding of the expansive interpretation of fundamental rights by the Supreme Court.

**5. With reference to the Indian judicial system, consider the following pairs:**

    Legal Remedy/Petition                    Description
1. Mercy Petition                             :   Filed with the Supreme Court to address errors in a lower court's judgment
2. Curative Petition                          :   Filed with the President seeking clemency for a death sentence
3. Review Petition                            :   Filed after a curative petition is rejected by the Supreme Court
4. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)       :   Dedicated courts to expedite the handling of specific types of cases (rape, POCSO)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. A curative petition is the final legal recourse available to a convict seeking to overturn a Supreme Court decision.  FTSCs are specialized courts designed to expedite the resolution of rape and POCSO cases.  Pair 1 is incorrect; mercy petitions are filed with the President, not the Supreme Court. Pair 3 is incorrect; a review petition is filed with the Supreme Court to review its own judgment, not after a curative petition is rejected. The question tests the understanding of different legal remedies and their appropriate applications within the Indian judicial system.  The distractors are carefully chosen to be plausible but ultimately incorrect, demanding a strong grasp of legal procedures.

**3. With reference to the Fiscal Federalism in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision          Specific Function
1. Article 246                       :   Defines tax bases between Union and States
2. Article 270                       :   Distribution of taxes levied and collected by states
3. Article 275                       :   Grants-in-aid to states
4. Article 292                       :   Union government borrowing powers only within India
5. Article 280                       :   Establishes the GST Council


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Option (a) is correct because:

* **Pair 1:** Article 246 correctly defines the division of tax powers between the Union and States.
* **Pair 3:** Article 275 accurately describes the constitutional provision for grants-in-aid.

Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because:

* **Pair 2:** Article 270 deals with the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the Union, not the states.
* **Pair 4:** Article 292 allows the Union government to borrow both within and outside India.
* **Pair 5:** The GST Council is not a constitutional body established under Article 280.  Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article          Provision Related To

(d) 2 and 4 only

Article 244(2) forms the basis for the establishment of the Autonomous District Councils and Autonomous Regional Councils in specific states. Article 280 mandates the establishment of the Finance Commission to advise on the distribution of financial resources between the Union and States. Article 282 empowers both the Union and State governments to make grants for any public purpose, even beyond their legislative competence. Finally, Article 292 details the borrowing powers of the Union government.  There are no inaccuracies or mismatches in any of the provided pairs. Options (a), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect as they omit correctly matched pairs.

   Financial Provision/Concept       Constitutional Article

(b) 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Vertical devolution, the share of divisible pool to states,  is not specifically tied to a single article but is a consequence of the Finance Commission's recommendations guided by Article 280 and the distribution mentioned in Article 270. **2. With reference to Contempt of Court, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Contempt                     Description
1. Civil Contempt                       :   Publicly criticizing a judge's personal life
2. Criminal Contempt                    :   Wilful disobedience of a court order
3. Civil Contempt                       :   Publishing material that scandalizes a court
4. Criminal Contempt                    :   Refusal to comply with a court summons


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. Let's examine each:

1. **Incorrect:** Publicly criticizing a judge's personal life doesn't directly fall under the definition of civil contempt. Civil contempt involves the willful disobedience of court orders or processes.  While it might indirectly affect the court's authority, it's not the primary definition.

2. **Correct:** Wilful disobedience of a court order is a clear-cut case of civil contempt. This directly undermines the court's authority and its ability to enforce its decisions.

3. **Incorrect:** Publishing material that scandalizes a court is a form of *criminal* contempt, not civil contempt.  Criminal contempt focuses on actions that undermine the court's authority or interfere with the administration of justice.

4. **Correct:** Refusal to comply with a court summons is a form of civil contempt.  It's a direct act of disobedience to a court order or process.


**3. With reference to the President's Power on Mercy Petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Article                                    Application
1. Article 72                               :   Applies only to cases involving offences against state laws
2. Article 72                               :   Empowers the President to pardon individuals convicted by court-martial
3. Article 142                              :   Provides the basis for the President's power of pardon
4. Article 72                               :  Covers offences against laws under the executive power of the Union


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. Let's analyze:

1. **Incorrect:** Article 72's scope extends beyond offences against state laws. It encompasses offences against both Union and State laws, where the sentence is by a court-martial or for an offence against any law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends.

2. **Correct:**  Article 72 explicitly empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute sentences in cases involving court-martial convictions.

3. **Incorrect:** Article 142 deals with the Supreme Court's power to do complete justice, not the President's pardon power.  The President's power is derived from Article 72.

4. **Correct:** Article 72 covers offences against laws that fall under the executive power of the Union. This is a significant part of the President's power in granting pardons.


**4. With reference to Curative Petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Grounds for Filing                     Specific Condition
1. Violation of principles of natural justice :  Requires demonstration of prejudice to the petitioner
2. Judge's undisclosed connection to the case:  Can be filed only after dismissal of a review petition
3. Apprehension of bias                  :   Needs evidence of actual bias demonstrated by the judge
4. Procedural irregularities in the lower court :  Supreme Court's curative jurisdiction is the final remedy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. The explanation follows:

1. **Incorrect:** While a violation of the principles of natural justice is a ground for filing a curative petition, merely demonstrating a violation is insufficient. The petitioner must also show that this violation caused them prejudice or affected the outcome of the case.

2. **Correct:** A judge's undisclosed connection to the case is a valid ground for a curative petition.  Crucially, curative petitions are a final remedy, only available after other avenues like review petitions have been exhausted.

3. **Incorrect:**  An apprehension of bias, while a valid ground, requires more than just suspicion. The petitioner must present evidence suggesting actual bias on the part of the judge that influenced the judgment.  Mere apprehension isn't enough.

4. **Correct:**  Curative petitions are indeed the final constitutional remedy available to a petitioner whose review petition has been dismissed by the Supreme Court.  This signifies the extraordinary nature of this legal recourse.

   Article                                    Application in Recent SC Judgement

2. Article 21                               :   Includes the right to be free from the adverse effects of climate change
3. Article 19                               :   Protects the right to protest against environmental degradation

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched in relation to the Supreme Court's recent judgment on environmental issues.  Let's analyze:

1. **Incorrect:** While Article 14 guarantees equality before the law, the recent SC judgment primarily focused on Articles 21 (right to life) and the interpretation of this right to include freedom from adverse effects of climate change, rather than explicitly establishing a separate "right to a healthy environment" under Article 14.

4. **Correct:** Article 48A, a Directive Principle of State Policy, directs the state to protect and improve the environment.  The SC judgment indirectly aligns with this directive principle by broadening the interpretation of fundamental rights to encompass environmental concerns.

1. **Incorrect:** Nodal Officers for Public Grievances are appointed across all Ministries/Departments, not just at the central government level. This ensures a decentralized approach to grievance handling.

3. **Correct:** The Grievance Redressal Assessment Index (GRAI) is designed to rank Ministries/Departments based on their performance in grievance redressal.  This promotes accountability and encourages improvement in grievance handling processes.

4. **Incorrect:** Dedicated Grievance Cells are mandated to be set up in every Ministry/Department, ensuring adequate resources are allocated to address public grievances effectively. The statement incorrectly suggests they are not mandatory.


**13. With reference to Protected and Restricted Areas, consider the following pairs:**

   Area                                     Specific Feature
1. Protected Areas                          :   Include parts of all states in India
2. Restricted Areas                         :   Encompass the entire Union Territory of Andaman & Nicobar Islands
3. Foreigner Entry to Protected Areas      :   Requires special permit for all foreigners

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. Let's examine each:

1. **Incorrect:** Protected Areas are not located in all parts of all states in India.  Their distribution is concentrated in specific regions known for their ecological significance.

2. **Correct:** The entire Union Territory of Andaman & Nicobar Islands is indeed designated as a Restricted Area under the Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963.

3. **Correct:** Foreigners, except citizens of Bhutan, require special permits to enter and stay in Protected or Restricted Areas. This highlights the stringent regulations governing access to these sensitive areas.

4. **Incorrect:** Sikkim is partly in a Protected Area and partly in a Restricted Area, not entirely a Protected Area.  This reflects the nuanced designation of areas based on their specific characteristics.



**14. With reference to Fiscal Federalism, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision/Concept                          Specific Detail
1. Seventh Schedule                           :   Defines the distribution of taxes between Union and States
2. Vertical Devolution                         :   Refers to the share of states from the divisible pool of taxes
3. Horizontal Devolution                       :   Based solely on population data
4. Finance Commission                          :   Recommends distribution of only direct taxes


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched.  Let's examine each:

1. **Correct:** The Seventh Schedule of the Constitution outlines the division of powers, including the allocation of tax bases, between the Union and State governments, forming the foundation of fiscal federalism in India.

2. **Correct:** Vertical devolution accurately describes the share allocated to states from the divisible pool of taxes collected by the central government. This represents the vertical flow of funds from the center to the states.

3. **Incorrect:** Horizontal devolution considers several factors beyond just population data, including income distance, area, demographic performance, forest and ecology, and tax and fiscal efforts. The statement oversimplifies the criteria.

4. **Incorrect:** The Finance Commission's recommendations encompass the distribution of both direct and indirect taxes, playing a crucial role in determining the allocation of resources between the Union and State governments.

2. **Correct:** Jammu & Kashmir was indeed granted Special Category Status in 1969, reflecting its unique geographical and socio-economic circumstances at the time.

3. **Incorrect:** The criteria for granting Special Category Status are multifaceted, encompassing geographical factors, socio-economic indicators, and other relevant considerations.  The statement oversimplifies the criteria.

**16. With reference to the Tribunal System in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Tribunal/Concept                          Specific Feature
1. Central Administrative Tribunal (CAT)     :   Appeals lie with the High Courts
2. Article 323A                              :   Provides for the establishment of CAT
3. Tribunals                                 :   Always have original jurisdiction only
4.  Jurisdiction of Tribunals                 :   Limited to specific subject matters


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched.  Let's examine each:

1. **Incorrect:** Appeals from the Central Administrative Tribunal (CAT) primarily lie with the Supreme Court, not the High Courts, as clarified by the Supreme Court in 2010.  This highlights the hierarchical structure of the judicial system.

2. **Correct:** Article 323A of the Constitution explicitly provides for the establishment of Administrative Tribunals, including the CAT, to address disputes related to public services.

3. **Incorrect:** Tribunals can have both original and appellate jurisdiction, depending on the specific legislation establishing them.  The statement incorrectly restricts their jurisdiction to original cases only.

4. **Correct:** Each tribunal is given a specific jurisdiction to hear and decide cases within its designated area of expertise.  This ensures specialized knowledge and efficient handling of specific types of disputes.


**17. With reference to the Data Protection Board of India (DPBI), consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                   Specific Detail

2. Appeals against DPBI decisions          :   Lie with the Supreme Court
3. Data Principal's Rights                  :   Includes the right to seek correction of personal data
4.  Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDF)      :   Designation is automatic for all large corporations


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched. Let's examine each pair:

1. **Incorrect:** Board members are appointed for a term of two years, not five years, allowing for periodic review and potential changes in membership.

2. **Incorrect:** Appeals against DPBI decisions lie with the Telecom Disputes Settlement and Appellate Tribunal (TDSAT), not directly with the Supreme Court. This reflects the specialized nature of telecom-related disputes.

3. **Correct:** Data principals have the right to obtain information about the processing of their personal data, seek correction and erasure of their data, and have access to grievance redressal mechanisms. The right to seek correction is a key aspect of data protection.

4. **Incorrect:**  The designation of Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDF) is not automatic for all large corporations. It's based on factors such as volume and sensitivity of data, potential risks, and impact on national security and public order, making it a case-by-case determination.

**2. With reference to the Jan Yojana Abhiyan, consider the following pairs:**

    Campaign Element                    Specific Detail
1.  Aim                                   : To increase government control over panchayat development
2.  Implementation Tier                 : Only at the Gram Panchayat level
3.  Components                            : Includes only Ward Sabhas and Gram Sabhas
4.  Preparation of GPDP                  :  Based solely on data from the Panchayat Development Index (PDI)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) None
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

None of the pairs are correctly matched. The Jan Yojana Abhiyan's aim is to accelerate *people's participation* in Panchayat Development Plan preparation, not to increase government control (pair 1).  The Abhiyan is implemented at all three tiers of Panchayats (Gram, Block, and District) – not just at the Gram Panchayat level (pair 2).  Its components include various types of Sabhas (Ward, Mahila, Gram, Block, District) (pair 3).  Finally, while PDI informs the identification of thematic developmental gaps, the preparation of GPDP involves a broader approach using a 'Whole of Government and Whole of Society approach', incorporating various other inputs besides PDI data (pair 4).  The incorrect options present plausible but ultimately inaccurate details about the Abhiyan's objectives and implementation, testing the candidate's knowledge of grassroots governance initiatives and their understanding of participatory development. This question assesses factual recall and analytical skills.



**3. With reference to the Auditing of Local Bodies in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Entity/Act                              Characteristic
1.  International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL)  : Established under the 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts
2.  AuditOnline application                                  : Awarded the World Summit on Information Society Prizes 2023
3.  CAG’s mandate for audit of Local Bodies                :  Derived from the CAG's (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971
4.  Examiner of Local Fund Accounts (ELFA)                 : Operates independently of the Comptroller and Auditor General of India (CAG)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  The AuditOnline application did indeed receive the World Summit on Information Society Prizes 2023.  The CAG's mandate for auditing local bodies originates from the CAG's (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971. Pair 1 is incorrect because iCAL is a collaborative platform inaugurated recently, not established under the 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts, which provide the framework for local self-governance. Pair 4 is incorrect as ELFAs/DLFAs work *under* the technical guidance and supervision of the CAG, not independently. The incorrect options test the candidate's understanding of the institutional framework for auditing local bodies in India, requiring them to discern between the roles and functions of various entities involved in the process.  The question assesses factual recall and analytical skills related to India's governance structure.


**4. With reference to Alternative Dispute Resolution (ADR) in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Act/Organization                         Feature
1.  Arbitration and Conciliation Act, 1996 :  Based on the UNCITRAL Model Law on International Commercial Arbitration
2.  Mediation and Conciliation Project Committee (MCPC)  : Constituted by the Ministry of Law and Justice
3.  New Delhi International Arbitration Centre Act, 2019 :  Facilitates institutional arbitration
4.  Permanent Court of Arbitration (PCA)              :  Established by the United Nations


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched. The Arbitration and Conciliation Act, 1996, is indeed based on the UNCITRAL Model Law. The New Delhi International Arbitration Centre Act, 2019, aims to facilitate institutional arbitration.  Pair 2 is incorrect because the MCPC was constituted by the Supreme Court of India, not the Ministry of Law and Justice.  Pair 4 is incorrect; the PCA was established by the Convention for the Pacific Settlement of International Disputes (1899), not the United Nations.  The incorrect options provide plausible but inaccurate information about the legal framework and institutions related to ADR, testing the candidate's knowledge of both domestic and international dispute resolution mechanisms. This question assesses factual recall and analytical skills.


**5. With reference to the National Programme for Civil Services Capacity Building (NPCSCB) - Mission Karmayogi, consider the following pairs:**

    Aspect of Mission Karmayogi                Detail
1.  NPCSCB's Aim                              : To exclusively train IAS officers
2.  NPCSCB's Coverage                          : Includes all civil servants, including contractual employees
3.  Guiding Principles                         :  Focuses solely on rule-based training
4.  Capacity Building Commission (CBC)          : Launched in 2022


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 2 is correctly matched.  NPCSCB does indeed cover all civil servants, including contractual employees. Pair 1 is incorrect; NPCSCB's aim is broader than just training IAS officers; it encompasses all civil servants.  Pair 3 is incorrect as a key guiding principle is a *shift* from rule-based to role-based training.  Pair 4 is incorrect; the CBC was launched in 2021, not 2022. The incorrect options offer plausible yet inaccurate details about Mission Karmayogi, testing the candidate's knowledge of civil service reforms and capacity-building initiatives in India.  The question evaluates factual recall and assesses the ability to distinguish accurate from inaccurate information regarding a significant government program.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Body                                       Characteristic
1. National Human Rights Commission (NHRC) : Established under the Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993
2. Capacity Building Commission (CBC)       :  Launched in 2021 as part of Mission Karmayogi
3. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) : Aims to set global standards for auditing local governance bodies in India
4.  Data Protection Board of India (DPBI)     :  Has powers to impose penalties for data breaches.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched.  The National Human Rights Commission (NHRC) is indeed a statutory body established under the Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993 (as amended). The Capacity Building Commission (CBC) was launched in 2021 as a key component of Mission Karmayogi, a national program for civil services capacity building. The International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL), inaugurated in Rajkot, Gujarat, aims to establish global benchmarks for auditing local governance bodies within India.  Finally, the Data Protection Board of India (DPBI) possesses the authority to levy penalties on entities that violate data protection regulations, specifically in cases of data breaches.  Therefore, option (d) encompasses all correctly matched pairs.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete and therefore incorrect, omitting crucial and factually accurate pairings.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Amendment                                  Provision
1. 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Act, 1992 :  Developed AuditOnline application for online audit of panchayat accounts.
2.  The Indian Telegraph Act, 1885                 : Repealed by the Telecommunications Act, 2023
3.  The Indian Wireless Telegraphy Act, 1933          : Repealed by the Telecommunications Act, 2023
4.  Protection of Human Rights Act (PHRA), 1993     : Established the NHRC


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

While the 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts of 1992 established the framework for local self-governance, the development of the AuditOnline application was a later initiative by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj.  Therefore, pair 1 is incorrectly matched.  However, the Indian Telegraph Act of 1885 and the Indian Wireless Telegraphy Act of 1933 were indeed repealed by the Telecommunications Act, 2023, making pairs 2 and 3 correct.  The Protection of Human Rights Act (PHRA), 1993, is correctly linked to the establishment of the NHRC, making pair 4 accurate.  Thus, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched, leading to option (d) as the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (c) include incorrectly matched pairs.

   Scheme/Initiative                           Key Feature

(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

Mission Karmayogi emphasizes a competency-driven approach to civil service capacity building. **4. With reference to the Indian Fiscal System, consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision                     Description
1. Article 270                               :  Taxes levied and collected by the Union are distributed between the Union and States.
2. Article 275                               :  Centre provides grants-in-aid to states.
3. Article 280                               :  Provides for a Finance Commission to adjudicate resource sharing.
4. Article 293                               : States can borrow money from outside India.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Articles 270, 275, and 280 correctly describe the distribution of taxes between the Union and States, the provision of grants-in-aid by the Centre, and the establishment of the Finance Commission, respectively.  However, Article 293 permits states to borrow within India, not outside.  Therefore, pair 4 is incorrectly matched.  Options (a), (c), and (d) either incorrectly include or exclude the correctly matched pairs.  Option (b) accurately identifies the correctly matched pairs, making it the correct answer.
