**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article             Provision Related To
1. Article 72                        :   President's power to grant pardons in cases involving court-martial sentences
2. Article 137                       :   Supreme Court's power to review its own judgments
3. Article 142                       :   Supreme Court's power to do complete justice
4. Article 280                       :   Establishment of the Finance Commission

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offence against any law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends.  This explicitly includes sentences awarded by court-martials, making pair 1 correct. Article 137 deals with the Supreme Court's power to review its own judgments,  a crucial aspect of judicial review, making pair 2 incorrect.  Article 142 grants the Supreme Court the power to do complete justice, which is a broad power allowing the court to issue orders necessary for achieving justice in specific cases; this makes pair 3 correct.  Article 280 mandates the establishment of a Finance Commission to advise on the distribution of tax revenue between the Union and States, making pair 4 correct. Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Scheme                      Key Feature
1. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) :   Established under the Nirbhaya Fund
2. Consumer Protection Act (CPA) 2019 :   Includes online transactions in the definition of 'consumer'
3. Digital Personal Data Protection Act 2023 :   Replaces the Indian Evidence Act, 1872
4. Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam 2023 :   Regulates processing of digital personal data

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) are indeed funded by the Nirbhaya Fund, a centrally sponsored scheme aimed at speedy disposal of rape and POCSO Act cases, making pair 1 correct. The Consumer Protection Act, 2019, significantly broadened the definition of 'consumer' to include those who buy goods or services online or through electronic means, making pair 2 correct. The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, focuses on regulating digital personal data, not replacing the Indian Evidence Act; that was done by the Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, making pair 3 incorrect. The Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, replaced the Indian Evidence Act, 1872, making pair 4 correct.  Therefore, pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Scheduled Area Provision           Characteristic
1. Fifth Schedule                       :   Applicability to specific tribal areas in Assam, Meghalaya, Tripura, and Mizoram
2. Sixth Schedule                       :   Establishment of Tribes Advisory Councils (TACs)
3. Article 244(2)                     :   Empowers the Governor to create Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs)
4. PESA Act 1996                      :  Applicable to Fifth Schedule areas

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Fifth Schedule deals with the administration of Scheduled Areas in several states, but the Sixth Schedule specifically applies to Assam, Meghalaya, Tripura, and Mizoram, making pair 1 incorrect and pair 5 correct. The Sixth Schedule, under Article 244(2), empowers the Governor to create ADCs and ARCs, making pair 3 correct.  Tribes Advisory Councils (TACs) are associated with the Fifth Schedule, not the Sixth, making pair 2 incorrect. The Panchayats (Extension to Scheduled Areas) Act, 1996 (PESA) applies to Fifth Schedule areas, making pair 4 correct.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 4 are correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Law                                   Key Provision
1. Code of Criminal Procedure (CrPC) 1973 :   Mandatory forensic investigation for offences punishable with at least seven years imprisonment
2. Bharatiya Nagrik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023 :   Provision for Zero FIR
3. Limitation Act, 1963                    :   Doctrine of harmonious construction applied to Sections 3 and 5
4. Indian Passport Act, 1920                :   Three classes of passports issued (Ordinary, Diplomatic, Official)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The CrPC 1973 indeed mandates forensic investigation for offences with at least seven years imprisonment, making pair 1 correct. The Bharatiya Nagrik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023, introduced the provision for Zero FIRs, making pair 2 correct. The Supreme Court's application of the doctrine of harmonious construction to Sections 3 and 5 of the Limitation Act, 1963, is a well-established legal principle, making pair 3 correct.  The Indian Passport Act, 1920, does indeed outline three classes of passports: Ordinary, Diplomatic, and Official, making pair 4 correct.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Body                       Characteristic
1. National Commission for Scheduled Castes (NCSC) :   Deals with complaints related to Scheduled Castes
2. Union Public Service Commission (UPSC) :   Conducts civil services examinations
3. State Finance Commission                 :   Adjudicates sharing of resources between Union and States
4. Central Vigilance Commission (CVC)       :   Deals with corruption complaints against government officials
5. NITI Aayog                              :   Replaced the Planning Commission

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) Only one


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The NCSC deals with complaints related to Scheduled Castes, making pair 1 correct. The UPSC conducts the civil services examination, making pair 2 correct. The State Finance Commission advises on the distribution of state finances, not the Union and State distribution, making pair 3 incorrect. The CVC deals with corruption complaints against government officials, making pair 4 correct. NITI Aayog replaced the Planning Commission, making pair 5 correct. Therefore, pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.



**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article                    Related Subject
1. Article 72                               :   Presidential Pardon
2. Article 137                              :   Review Petition in Supreme Court
3. Article 142                              :   Curative Petition in Supreme Court
4. Article 280                              :   Finance Commission
5. Article 244(2)                           :   Fifth Schedule

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offence.  Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments.  Article 280 mandates the establishment of a Finance Commission to recommend the distribution of financial resources between the Union and the States.  The statement regarding Article 142 being related to curative petitions is incorrect; Article 142 deals with the Supreme Court's power to do complete justice.  Article 244(2) pertains to the Sixth Schedule, not the Fifth Schedule, which deals with the administration of tribal areas in certain states. Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched.


**2. With reference to the Right to Information (RTI) Act, 2005, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                     Function/Characteristic
1. Department of Personnel and Training  :   Coordinating agency for RTI Act implementation
2. Central Information Commission          :   Appoints Central Public Information Officers (PIOs)
3. Madras High Court                       :   Ruled that cooperative societies are Public Authorities under RTI Act
4. Supreme Court                          :   Declared the Office of Chief Justice of India a Public Authority
5.  Universal Declaration of Human Rights:  Articulates RTI as a fundamental right


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 1, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Department of Personnel and Training (DoPT) under the Ministry of Personnel, Public Grievances and Pensions is indeed the coordinating agency for the RTI Act. The Supreme Court has ruled that the Office of the Chief Justice of India is a Public Authority under the RTI Act.  However, the Central Information Commission (CIC) does not appoint PIOs; it oversees their functioning and handles appeals. The Madras High Court ruled that cooperative societies are *not* Public Authorities under the RTI Act. The Universal Declaration of Human Rights articulates the right to information, but not specifically as a *fundamental* right in the Indian context.  Thus, only pairs 1 and 4 are correctly matched.


**3. With reference to Cantonment Boards in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Cantonment Related Entity                 Characteristic/Fact
1. Cantonment Act, 2006                    :   Administered under the 73rd Constitutional Amendment Act
2. Barrackpore                               :   First Cantonment established in 1765
3. Ministry of Defence                       :   Under administrative control of Cantonment Boards
4. Station Commander                        :   Ex-officio President of the Cantonment Board
5.  East India Company                     :   Established Cantonments after the Battle of Plassey


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2, 4, and 5 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Barrackpore was indeed the first cantonment established in 1765. The Station Commander serves as the ex-officio President of the Cantonment Board. The East India Company established cantonments after the Battle of Plassey.  However, the Cantonment Act, 2006, is administered in accordance with the 74th, not the 73rd, Constitutional Amendment Act, which deals with urban local bodies.  The Ministry of Defence is responsible for the *overall* administration, not the Cantonment Boards themselves. Therefore, only pairs 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.



**4. With reference to the  Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, consider the following statements:**

   Statement                                 Correctness
1. It replaces the Indian Telegraph Act, 1885 :   True
2. It regulates the processing of digital personal data:  True
3. It provides for measures to protect users from specified messages: True
4. It brings OTT platforms under its regulatory purview: False
5. It establishes a new fund called Digital Bharat Nidhi: False


Which of the statements given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, primarily aims to regulate the processing of digital personal data and includes provisions for user protection, such as mechanisms to deal with unwanted messages. However, it does *not* replace the Indian Telegraph Act, 1885 (that is done by the Telecommunications Act, 2023), nor does it regulate OTT platforms or establish a new fund called Digital Bharat Nidhi (that is done by the Telecommunications Act, 2023). Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Provision                              Description
1. Mercy Petition                               :  Governed by Article 72
2. Curative Petition                           :  Last constitutional remedy after review petition dismissal
3. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)          :  Exclusively handle POCSO Act cases
4.  Nirbhaya Fund                             :  Funds FTSCs under a centrally sponsored scheme
5.  Protection of Children from Sexual Offences (POCSO) Act:  Cases handled by FTSCs


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 correctly governs the President's power regarding mercy petitions. Curative petitions are indeed the last resort after review petitions are dismissed. The Nirbhaya Fund finances the FTSCs, which handle cases under the POCSO Act. While many FTSCs handle POCSO Act cases, it is not *exclusive* to them.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.





**1. With reference to the functioning of the Central Bureau of Investigation (CBI), consider the following pairs:**

   Body/Act                                 Feature
1. Santhanam Committee                     :   Established the CBI in 1963
2. Delhi Special Police Establishment Act, 1946 :  Governs the CBI's operations
3. Ministry of Home Affairs                  :   Oversees the CBI's activities
4. Article 131 of the Constitution          :   Deals with disputes between the Centre and States involving the CBI


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Santhanam Committee on Prevention of Corruption (1962-64) recommended the establishment of the CBI, which was subsequently formed in 1963.  The Delhi Special Police Establishment (DSPE) Act, 1946, provides the legal framework for the CBI's functioning as a premier investigating agency.  While the CBI falls under the Ministry of Personnel, Pension & Public Grievances,  the Ministry of Home Affairs is not directly involved in its daily operations. Article 131 of the Constitution is relevant because the Supreme Court's original jurisdiction extends to disputes between the Union and States, including cases where the CBI's actions are challenged, as seen in the West Bengal vs. Union of India case.  Therefore, options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete or inaccurate.


**2. With reference to the Jan Yojana Abhiyan, consider the following pairs:**

   Program/Initiative                        Characteristic
1. Jan Yojana Abhiyan                       :   Launched in 2018 as 'Sabki Yojana Sabka Vikas'
2. Panchayat Development Plans (PDPs)     :   Prepared for the fiscal year 2025-26 under the Abhiyan
3.  Gram Panchayat Development Plan (GPDP) :   Published on the e-Gram Swaraj portal after approval
4.  Panchayat Development Index (PDI)       :   Used to identify thematic developmental gaps at the block level only


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Jan Yojana Abhiyan, launched in 2018 under the name 'Sabki Yojana Sabka Vikas', aims to enhance people's participation in creating Panchayat Development Plans (PDPs).  These PDPs, specifically for 2025-26, are prepared at various levels, including the Gram Panchayat Development Plan (GPDP), which is published on the e-Gram Swaraj portal after receiving approval. The Panchayat Development Index (PDI) is used to identify thematic developmental gaps at all levels of Panchayats, not just the block level. Thus, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched.


**3. With reference to the auditing of local bodies in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Act                              Role/Function
1. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) :   Established in Rajkot, Gujarat
2. Comptroller and Auditor General of India (CAG)           :   Mandate for auditing local bodies comes from the 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts
3. AuditOnline application                         :   Developed by the Ministry of Rural Development
4. Examiner of Local Fund Accounts (ELFA) / Director of Local Fund Accounts (DLFA): Works under the technical guidance of the Union Ministry of Finance


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) was inaugurated in Rajkot, Gujarat. The CAG's mandate for auditing local bodies stems from the CAG (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971, not the 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts, which deal with local self-governance. AuditOnline is a panchayat account auditing application developed by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj, not the Ministry of Rural Development. ELFA/DLFA work under the technical guidance and supervision of the CAG, not the Union Ministry of Finance.  Therefore, only pair 1 is correctly matched.


**4. With reference to fiscal federalism in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision/Body            Function/Responsibility
1. Article 246                               :   Divides tax powers between the Union and States
2. Article 270                               :   Deals with the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the Union
3. Article 275                               :   Relates to grants-in-aid from the Centre to States
4. 15th Finance Commission                   :   Recommended a 41% share of divisible pool for states based on income distance, area, and population only


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 246 of the Indian Constitution outlines the division of powers to levy and collect taxes between the Union and the States. Article 270 deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain Union taxes between the Union and the States. Article 275 concerns grants-in-aid from the Union to States. However, the 15th Finance Commission's recommendations for the distribution of the divisible pool among states included factors beyond income distance, area, and population; it also considered demographic performance, forest and ecology, and tax and fiscal efforts. Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched.


**5. With reference to Special Category Status (SCS) in India, consider the following pairs:**

   State/Union Territory                    Characteristic
1. Andhra Pradesh                           :   Demanded SCS recently
2. Bihar                                   :   Demanded SCS recently
3. Fifth Finance Commission                  :   First introduced the concept of SCS in 1969
4. Jammu & Kashmir (pre-2019)             :   Granted SCS in 1969


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Andhra Pradesh and Bihar have both recently demanded Special Category Status. The Fifth Finance Commission introduced the concept of SCS in 1969. Jammu and Kashmir was among the states granted SCS in 1969.  All the pairs are correctly matched.


**6. Consider the following pairs related to the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023:**

   Entity/Provision                            Function/Feature
1. Data Protection Board of India (DPBI)    :   Imposes penalties for non-compliance with the Act
2. Data Principal                              :   Has the right to seek correction and erasure of personal data
3. Data Fiduciary                             :   Must ensure data accuracy and build reasonable security safeguards
4. Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDFs)       :   Are exempted from all obligations under the Act


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Data Protection Board of India (DPBI) has the power to impose penalties for violations of the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023.  Data principals have the right to seek corrections and erasure of their personal data. Data fiduciaries have the responsibility to maintain data accuracy and implement security measures.  However, Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDFs) are not exempted from all obligations; they have additional obligations, including appointing a data protection officer and an independent data auditor.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision                    Related Power/Application
1. Article 72                               :   Granting pardons to individuals convicted by a court-martial
2. Article 137                               :   Review of a curative petition by the Supreme Court
3. Article 142                               :   Power to do complete justice in specific cases
4. Article 280                               :   Appointment of the President of India
5. Article 292                               :   Union government's power to borrow money internationally

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 explicitly grants the President of India the power to pardon, reprieve, respite, or remit sentences, including those given by court-martials.  Article 142 empowers the Supreme Court to do complete justice, which is a broader power than just reviewing curative petitions; the review of a curative petition falls under its inherent powers but is not the sole definition of Article 142. Article 292 deals with the borrowing powers of the Union government, explicitly mentioning borrowing within and outside India. Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission, not the appointment of the President. Article 137 deals with the Supreme Court's power to review its own judgments, not curative petitions directly.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, and 5 are correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Court/Institution                        Type of Petition/Remedy
1. Supreme Court                           :   Zero FIR
2.  Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)      :   Mercy Petition
3.  Gram Nyayalayas                        :   Curative Petition
4.  High Courts                             :   Civil Contempt
5.  Arbitral Tribunal                        :   Condonation of Delay


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 and 5 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

High Courts, under Article 215, possess the power to punish for contempt of court, including civil contempt.  The other pairings are incorrect: Zero FIRs are registered by police stations, not the Supreme Court; FTSCs deal with specific types of cases but don't inherently handle mercy petitions; Gram Nyayalayas focus on local dispute resolution, not curative petitions; and arbitral tribunals may deal with condonation of delay, but it's not their exclusive function. The Supreme Court is involved in hearing petitions related to various issues (Curative petition, Mercy petition, etc.)  but does not exclusively deal with them. Therefore, only pair 4 is accurately matched.

   Financial Provision/Institution             Description/Function

(d) 1, 3, and 5 only

The other options are mismatched: Vertical devolution involves the share from the divisible pool, not income distance-based distribution; Horizontal devolution is the distribution among states, not the share from the divisible pool; Grants-in-aid are given under Article 275, not Article 292; and Article 282 allows discretionary grants, not the power for states to borrow internationally. Thus, only pair 4 is correctly matched.

   State Classification/Provision            Characteristic/Feature

   Legal Doctrine/Principle                  Explanation/Application

**1. With reference to the Indian legal framework concerning data protection and the right to be forgotten, consider the following pairs:**

   Concept                                      Legal Instrument/Provision
1. Right to be Forgotten                       :   Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023
2. Regulation of Digital Personal Data        :    European GDPR law
3.  Origin of Right to be Forgotten           :   French jurisprudence


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, a significant piece of legislation in India, notably does *not* explicitly include the "right to be forgotten."  This right, stemming from the broader concept of the "right to oblivion" in French jurisprudence, is a key feature of the European Union's General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR).  Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect because the DPDP Act does not enshrine the right to be forgotten. Pair 2 is correct as the GDPR explicitly addresses the right to be forgotten, allowing individuals to request the deletion of their personal data under certain conditions. Pair 3 is also correct as the concept's origins trace back to French jurisprudence's "right to oblivion," which emphasizes an individual's control over their personal information and its dissemination.  Option (c) accurately reflects this. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they incorrectly associate the right to be forgotten with the wrong legal instrument or misrepresent the origins of the concept.  Understanding the nuances of data protection laws across jurisdictions is crucial for the UPSC exam.

   Legal Remedy                                     Description/Feature

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Data Protection Body (DPBI) Function                    :   Specific Responsibility
1. Monitoring compliance and imposing penalties         :   Hearing grievances made by affected persons
2. Directing data fiduciaries in data breaches           :   Ensuring the accuracy and completeness of data
3. Hearing grievances made by affected persons          :   Appointing a data protection officer (for SDFs)
4. Ensuring the accuracy and completeness of data       :   Informing DPBI and affected persons of a breach

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

None of the pairs are correctly matched. The DPBI's functions are distinct and not interchangeable as presented in the options.  Let's analyze each pair:

1. **Incorrect:** While the DPBI *does* monitor compliance and impose penalties, this is separate from its grievance-hearing function.  These are distinct actions under its purview.

2. **Incorrect:**  Directing data fiduciaries in data breach situations is a key DPBI responsibility, but it's not directly linked to ensuring data accuracy.  Data accuracy is a responsibility of the data fiduciary itself, not the DPBI's primary role in breach response.

3. **Incorrect:**  The DPBI hears grievances, but appointing a data protection officer is an additional obligation specifically for Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDFs), not a general DPBI function.

4. **Incorrect:**  The DPBI doesn't directly ensure data accuracy; that's the responsibility of the data fiduciary. The DPBI's role is more about oversight and enforcement.  Informing the DPBI and affected persons about a breach is a different responsibility of the data fiduciary.


The options are designed to test the understanding of the distinct roles and responsibilities of the DPBI and data fiduciaries, highlighting the crucial distinction between proactive data management (accuracy) and reactive breach response.  The correct answer emphasizes the independent nature of each function of the DPBI.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Jan Yojana Abhiyan Component                     :   Specific Objective
1. Structured Ward/Mahila/Gram Sabha               :   Publication of approved GPDPs on e-Gram Swaraj portal
2. Preparation of Gram Sabha-wise calendar        :   Engagement of youth and elderly in GPDP preparation
3. Identification of thematic developmental gaps    :   Accelerating people’s participation in PDP preparation

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched. Let's examine each pair:

1. **Incorrect:** Structured Sabhas are a key component of Jan Yojana Abhiyan, but their primary purpose isn't the publication of GPDPs on e-Gram Swaraj.  Publication is a later step in the process.

2. **Incorrect:** Preparing a Gram Sabha calendar is a step in planning, but it's not directly connected to the engagement of youth and elderly, though this engagement occurs within the framework of the calendar.

3. **Correct:** Identifying thematic developmental gaps based on the Panchayat Development Index (PDI) is a core aim of the structured Sabhas to inform the development plans.  This directly relates to the overall objective of accelerating people's participation in plan preparation.

4. **Incorrect:** Inclusive participation (engaging youth and the elderly) is a component to improve the quality of planning, but the assessment of Panchayats' development is done through the PDI, which informs the identification of developmental gaps, not directly through participation.

The question tests understanding of the sequential steps and interconnected objectives within the Jan Yojana Abhiyan. The distractors highlight the close relationship between different components, making it challenging to differentiate the direct and indirect connections between components and their objectives.

(c) 3 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.

1. **Incorrect:** iCAL's role is to set global standards and serve as a center of excellence for capacity building, not to conduct online audits of panchayat accounts. That is the function of AuditOnline.

2. **Correct:** The CAG, through its established mechanisms, exercises control and supervision over the proper maintenance of accounts and auditing for all three levels of Panchayati Raj Institutions (PRIs) and Urban Local Bodies (ULBs).

3. **Correct:** AuditOnline is specifically designed for conducting online audits of panchayat accounts, ensuring accountability in the utilization of funds at the ground level.

4. **Incorrect:** ELFA/DLFA audit the utilization of funds granted by the state government to local bodies, they don't directly engage in capacity building of auditors. That's the role of iCAL.

The question aims to assess the understanding of the different entities involved in auditing local bodies and their specific roles, testing knowledge of both established mechanisms (CAG, ELFA) and newer initiatives (iCAL, AuditOnline). Distractors are carefully chosen to reflect the interconnectedness of these entities, requiring a precise understanding of each entity's distinct responsibilities.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article                 Provision Related To

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 explicitly grants the President of India the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute sentences, including death sentences, in cases where the sentence is given by a court-martial or for offenses against laws relating to matters under the Union's executive power.  Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments, a crucial aspect of judicial review. Article 142 allows the Supreme Court to pass orders necessary for doing complete justice, including issuing curative petitions as a last resort.  Finally, Article 244(2) deals with the administration of tribal areas in certain states, as detailed in the Sixth Schedule. All four pairs are correctly matched.    Constitutional Article          Provision Related To

(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

There are no inaccuracies or misleading elements in any of the pairings.  Each pairing accurately reflects a direct and established constitutional provision.

**1. With reference to Gram Nyayalayas, consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                     Specific Detail

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, provides the statutory backing for the establishment of Gram Nyayalayas, not Article 244(2) which deals with the Sixth Schedule areas.  The Act's provisions clearly state that Gram Nyayalayas are located at the headquarters of the intermediate Panchayat.  Option 3 is incorrect; Gram Nyayalayas handle both civil and criminal cases, settling petty disputes at the village level. **2. With reference to Contempt of Court, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Contempt                       Specific Example
1.  Civil Contempt                         :  Publicly criticizing a judge's personal life
2.  Criminal Contempt                      :  Willful disobedience of a court order
3.  Civil Contempt                         :  Publishing an article that prejudices a pending case
4.  Criminal Contempt                      :  Refusal to comply with a court summons


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Civil contempt involves willful disobedience of court orders or undertakings, while criminal contempt involves actions that scandalize the court, prejudice judicial proceedings, or obstruct justice.  Option 1 is incorrect because publicly criticizing a judge's personal life is more aligned with criminal contempt, as it undermines the authority of the court. Option 2 is correctly matched as willful disobedience is a clear example of civil contempt. Option 3 is correctly matched as publishing an article that prejudices a pending case is criminal contempt. Option 4 is correctly matched as refusal to comply with a court summons is civil contempt. Therefore, options 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched, showcasing understanding of the distinct nature of civil and criminal contempt.

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Foreigners Tribunals are quasi-judicial bodies established under the Foreigners (Tribunals) Order, 1964, issued under the Foreigners Act, 1946. They possess powers similar to those of a civil court under the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908, not the powers of a District Judge.  They are established by the Central Government, not state governments. Their decisions are not final and binding; appeals can be made to higher courts.  Crucially, only Foreigners Tribunals have the power to declare someone a foreigner. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 5 are correctly matched. This question tests understanding of the Tribunal's legal framework and its specific functions within the larger context of Indian citizenship law.


**6. With reference to the Right to Information Act, 2005, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                      Specific Detail
1.  Central Information Commission (CIC) Members Appointment:  By the President based on the recommendation of the Prime Minister
2.  Applicability                               :  Includes only Central Government bodies
3.  Exemptions                                  :  Information concerning national security is always exempt
4.  Obligations of Public Authorities          :  Proactive disclosure of certain information
5.  Information Requestor                       :  Only Indian citizens can file RTI requests


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 1, 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3 and 4 only
(d) All five



**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The CIC members' appointments are indeed made by the President based on a committee's recommendation. The RTI Act's applicability extends beyond central government bodies to include various other public authorities. While information concerning national security can be exempt, the decision is case-specific and not always absolute.  The Act mandates proactive disclosure of information by public authorities to minimize the need for requests. The RTI Act allows any person to file a request, not just Indian citizens.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 4 are correctly matched. The question tests factual knowledge of the RTI Act and its application.


**7.  With reference to the President's power on mercy petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Sentence                                Specific Condition
1.  Pardon                                      :  Can only be granted for offenses against state laws
2.  Reprieve                                    :  Temporary postponement of execution
3.  Commutation                                 :  Reduction of death sentence to life imprisonment
4.  Remission                                   :  Complete cancellation of the sentence
5.  Suspension                                  :  Temporary halt to the sentence


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, remissions, and commutations of sentences.  A pardon is not limited to offenses against state laws; it can be granted for offenses under Union laws as well. Reprieve involves a temporary postponement of execution. Commutation refers to the reduction of a sentence (like death to life imprisonment). Remission involves the cancellation of a sentence. Suspension is a temporary halt to the sentence. Thus, options 2, 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched, demonstrating an understanding of the President's powers and the nuances of different types of clemency.

(b) 1, 2, and 5 only
(c) 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) All five



**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The MCC was first introduced in 1960 during Kerala State Assembly elections, not Lok Sabha elections. The ECI is indeed the governing body responsible for the MCC.  The MCC applies to both national and state elections.  The MCC is a set of guidelines, not a legally binding set of rules; violations can lead to action but are not directly punishable under law.  The MCC's purpose is indeed to ensure free and fair elections. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 5 are correctly matched.  The question assesses understanding of the MCC's origins, nature, and application.

   Constitutional Article          Provision Related To

3. Article 280                       :   Establishment of the Finance Commission
4. Article 292                       :   Union Government's power to borrow money within or outside the country
5. Article 293                       :   State Government's power to borrow money within India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 270 deals with the distribution of tax revenues between the Union and States. Article 275 mandates the provision of grants-in-aid by the Centre to States. Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission to adjudicate the sharing of resources. Article 292 grants the Union Government the power to borrow money both domestically and internationally.  Article 293 allows State Governments to borrow within India, but not abroad, and requires prior Union consent if the state is already indebted to the Union.  Therefore, option (d) is the correct answer, encompassing all correctly matched pairs.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

1. Public Accounts Committee                 :   Examines CAG audit reports on appropriation accounts
2. Committee on Public Undertakings          :   Reviews the performance of public sector undertakings
3. Committee of Privileges (Rajya Sabha)    :   Consists of 15 members nominated by the Rajya Sabha Chairman
4. Estimates Committee                       :   Consists of 30 members from Lok Sabha only
5. Parliamentary Committee on Official Languages:  Submits recommendations to the President on Hindi usage


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Public Accounts Committee (PAC) scrutinizes the Comptroller and Auditor General of India's (CAG) audit reports, including those on appropriation accounts.  The Committee on Public Undertakings (COPU) examines the working of public sector undertakings.  The Estimates Committee consists of 30 members, all from the Lok Sabha. The Committee of Privileges in the Rajya Sabha has 10 members, nominated by the Chairman of the Rajya Sabha, not 15. The Parliamentary Committee on Official Languages (PCOL) indeed submits its recommendations regarding the use of Hindi for official purposes to the President. Therefore, pairs 1, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Body                                       Composition/Characteristic
1. Lokpal                                     :   Headed by a former Chief Justice of India
2. National Human Rights Commission (NHRC) :   Appointed by the President based on a committee's recommendation
3. Cabinet Committee                          :   Extra-constitutional in nature
4. Collegium System                           :   Headed by the Chief Justice of India
5. Delimitation Commission                    :   Decisions are considered final and unchallengeable


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Lokpal can be headed by a person who is or has been a Chief Justice of India or a Judge of the Supreme Court, not necessarily a former CJI. The NHRC's Chairperson and members are appointed by the President based on the recommendations of a committee. Cabinet Committees are indeed extra-constitutional bodies. The Collegium System for judicial appointments is headed by the Chief Justice of India.  The Delimitation Commission's decisions are final and not challengeable in court.  Therefore, pairs 2, 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.

(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The CBI is indeed governed by the DSPE Act, 1946.  The SEC is responsible for delimiting constituencies for local body elections. Parliamentary Committees derive their authority from Articles 105 and 118.  However, appeals from the CAT generally lie with the High Courts, not exclusively the Supreme Court. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Article              Provision Related To
1. Article 270                        :   Distribution of taxes between Union and States
2. Article 275                         :   Grants-in-Aid to States
3. Article 280                         :   Establishment of Finance Commission
4. Article 292                         :   Union Government's borrowing powers within India only
5. Article 293                         :   State Government's borrowing powers within and outside India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 270 of the Indian Constitution deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain taxes between the Union and the States.  Article 275 mandates the Union to provide grants-in-aid to states from the consolidated fund of India.  Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission to recommend the distribution of net proceeds of taxes and grants-in-aid. Article 292 empowers the Union government to borrow money within India, while Article 293 allows state governments to borrow only within India, not internationally.  Options (b), (c), and (d) incorrectly include Article 292 or Article 293 or both, misrepresenting their provisions concerning borrowing powers.  Therefore, only option (a) accurately reflects the correct matching of the constitutional articles with their respective provisions.

**1. With reference to Gram Nyayalayas, consider the following pairs:**

    Act/Provision                                   Feature
    1. Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008                 :   Exempts Nagaland, Arunachal Pradesh, and Sikkim
    2. Indian Evidence Act, 1872                  :   Applies to Gram Nyayalaya proceedings
    3.  Court of Judicial Magistrate of First Class :   Status of Gram Nyayalayas
    4.  High Court                               :   Appoints Nyayadhikari in consultation with State Govt.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, establishes Gram Nyayalayas and explicitly exempts certain states and tribal areas.  Gram Nyayalayas are deemed to be Courts of Judicial Magistrates of the First Class, possessing both civil and criminal jurisdiction. The appointment of Nyayadhikari involves consultation between the State government and the High Court.  Crucially, Gram Nyayalayas are *not* bound by the Indian Evidence Act, 1872; they operate under principles of natural justice. This makes option (a) the only entirely correct combination. Option (b) incorrectly includes the High Court's role in appointing Nyayadhikari; while the High Court is consulted, the State government makes the appointment. Option (c) is incorrect as it wrongly links the Indian Evidence Act to Gram Nyayalaya proceedings. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the mismatched pair concerning the Evidence Act.


**2. With reference to Contempt of Court, consider the following pairs:**

    Type of Contempt                         Description
    1. Civil Contempt                         :   Publication of matter scandalizing a court
    2. Criminal Contempt                      :   Willful disobedience of a court order
    3. Article 129 of the Constitution of India :   Grants power to High Courts to punish contempt
    4. Contempt of Courts Act, 1971           : Defines contempt of court


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Civil contempt involves willful disobedience of court orders, while criminal contempt encompasses actions like publishing material that scandalizes or interferes with the court's authority.  Article 129 grants the Supreme Court, not High Courts, the power to punish contempt; Article 215 extends this power to High Courts. The Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, provides the legal framework defining contempt.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. Option (b) incorrectly attributes the definition of civil contempt to the wrong category and incorrectly links Article 129 to High Courts. Option (c) is partially correct, but omits the correct pairing of criminal contempt and its description. Option (d) is incorrect due to the mismatched pair involving Article 129.

**8. With reference to Fiscal Federalism in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Aspect of Fiscal Federalism                Detail
    1.  Constitutional Basis                    :   Seventh Schedule
    2.  Vertical Devolution                     :   Distribution among states from their allocated share
    3.  Horizontal Devolution                   :   Share of states from divisible pool
    4.  Article 275                             :   Grants-in-aid

(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only

   Scheme Feature

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

None of the pairs are correctly matched. Let's analyze each pair:

A superficial understanding can lead to inaccurate conclusions.  The question tests the candidate's ability to recall and accurately match specific details related to CSS, a crucial component of India's federal financial architecture.

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. Let's analyze each pair:

4. **Correct:** A key principle of Mission Karmayogi is the shift from rule-based to role-based training and capacity building.  This reflects a modern approach to civil service training that emphasizes practical skills and competencies.

This question assesses the candidate's understanding of Mission Karmayogi's scope, objectives, and key principles.  The inclusion of several incorrect pairs, particularly those with minor discrepancies, requires careful examination and precise knowledge of the subject.

   Feature                                      Description

(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

All the pairs accurately reflect aspects of the Aadhaar Act, 2016, and the Supreme Court's 2018 judgment on its constitutionality.  The Aadhaar number is indeed a random number, not revealing sensitive personal details.  It serves as proof of address and identity for Indian residents. The Supreme Court's ruling mandates that Aadhaar metadata cannot be retained beyond six months.  The 2018 judgment affirmed the Act's constitutionality. **4. With reference to the Telecommunications Act, 2023, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                   Detail
1. Spectrum Allocation                         :   Primarily through auction; specified uses on an administrative basis

5. OTT Platform Regulation                   :   Not regulated under the Telecommunications Act 2023

(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only

(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

The Telecommunications Act, 2023, introduced significant changes in the telecom sector.  Spectrum allocation is primarily done through auctions, with certain exceptions for administrative allocation for specified purposes.  The Act establishes a non-discriminatory RoW framework. **2. With reference to the Indian governmental structure, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision/Act             Feature/Application
1. Article 280                              :  Establishes the Finance Commission
2. Article 275                              :  Governs grants-in-aid from the Union to States
3. Article 292                              :  Deals with the borrowing powers of the Union government
4. 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts:  Provide provisions on local self-governance
5.  Article 72                               :  Empowers the President to grant pardons

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched. Article 280 of the Indian Constitution mandates the establishment of the Finance Commission to recommend the distribution of financial resources between the Union and the States. Article 275 details the provision of grants-in-aid from the Union government to the States, often for specific developmental purposes.  Article 292 outlines the borrowing powers of the Union government, both domestically and internationally. The 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts established the framework for local self-governance in rural and urban areas respectively, devolving power to local bodies. Finally, Article 72 grants the President of India the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment, including for death sentences. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete and therefore incorrect.

**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Type of Petition/Remedy                     Key Feature/Provision

4.  Review Petition                            :  Article 137 of the Constitution
5.  Special Category Status (SCS)              :  Classification given by the Centre to states facing socio-economic disadvantages.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

**2. With reference to  Auditing of Local Bodies, consider the following pairs:**

    Entity                                     Function/Characteristic
1. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL): Aims to set global standards for auditing local governance bodies.
2. AuditOnline application: Developed by the Ministry of Rural Development.
3. Comptroller and Auditor General (CAG): Exercises control over the audit of only Urban Local Bodies.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) is correctly matched with its aim of establishing global standards for auditing local governance.  The AuditOnline application, while used for online auditing of panchayat accounts, is developed by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj, not the Ministry of Rural Development as stated in option 2.  Furthermore, the CAG's mandate extends to auditing both Panchayati Raj Institutions (PRIs) and Urban Local Bodies (ULBs), making option 3 incorrect. Therefore, only pair 1 is correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they include the mismatched pairs related to the AuditOnline application's developer and the CAG's scope of audit. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of the institutional framework for local body audits in India and the roles played by different entities.  Accurate understanding of these entities and their functions is crucial for comprehensive preparation.


**3.  With reference to  Special Category Status (SCS) and Special Packages, consider the following pairs:**

    Item                                 Characteristic
1. Special Category Status: Grants based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula.
2. Special Packages: Provided only to states facing geographical challenges.
3. Fourteenth Finance Commission: Recommended the continuation of SCS.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) None
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are incorrectly matched.  While SCS was historically associated with grants based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula, this is no longer the case after the recommendations of the Fourteenth Finance Commission.  Special Packages are not limited to states facing only geographical challenges; socio-economic factors also play a role.  Finally, the Fourteenth Finance Commission recommended the discontinuation of SCS, not its continuation.  Therefore, none of the pairs are correctly matched.  The question tests the candidate's understanding of the evolution of financial assistance mechanisms for states in India.  The changing nature of these mechanisms and the role of the Finance Commissions are important aspects of governance.


**4. With reference to  Aadhaar, consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                                     Description
1. Random Number: Captures details like caste, religion, income, health, geography, etc.
2. Proof of address and Identity:  Aadhaar is a proof of citizenship.
3. Targeted Delivery: Aadhaar is mandatory for opening bank accounts.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) None
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are incorrectly matched.  The Aadhaar number is a random number and does not capture any personally identifiable information like caste, religion, income, etc., making statement 1 incorrect.  Aadhaar is a proof of identity and address but not citizenship, contradicting statement 2.  While Aadhaar can be used for targeted delivery of benefits, it is not mandatory for opening bank accounts, making statement 3 incorrect. Therefore, none of the pairs are correctly matched. This question tests the candidate's understanding of the Aadhaar system, its features, and its limitations.  The Supreme Court's judgment on Aadhaar is relevant here, emphasizing the importance of privacy and data security.


**5. With reference to the  Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

    Item                                       Feature
1. Sixth Schedule:  Applies to the entire state of Jammu and Kashmir.
2. Bardoloi Committee: Recommended the inclusion of Ladakh in the Sixth Schedule.
3. Article 244(2):  Deals with the administration of tribal areas in the Northeast.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched. The Sixth Schedule applies to specific tribal areas in four states of Northeast India, not the entire state of Jammu and Kashmir.  The Bardoloi Committee's recommendations did not directly address the inclusion of Ladakh in the Sixth Schedule; the demand is a recent development. Article 244(2) correctly deals with the administration of tribal areas in the Northeast, as outlined in the Sixth Schedule. Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include the mismatched pairs related to the applicability of the Sixth Schedule and the Bardoloi Committee's recommendations. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of the constitutional provisions related to tribal administration.  Understanding the intricacies of the Sixth Schedule and its historical context is crucial.


**6. With reference to  Cantonment Boards, consider the following pairs:**

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 2 is correctly matched. Cantonment Boards are administered by the Ministry of Defence, not directly by state governments. While recent news indicates the merging of land portions from some cantonment boards with state local bodies, this doesn't change the primary administrative control. The land administered by cantonment boards is not always under the concurrent list; it is governed by specific laws and regulations. Therefore, only pair 2 reflects a correct statement. **7. With reference to  Common Service Centres (CSCs), consider the following pairs:**

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 2 is correctly matched. The CSC Special Purpose Vehicle (SPV) was set up under the Companies Act, 1956, not the Information Technology Act, 2000.  The National e-Governance Plan (NeGP) correctly includes CSCs as one of its three pillars.  CSCs offer a diverse range of services, including G2C (Government-to-Citizen), B2C (Business-to-Citizen), and financial services, not primarily G2G (Government-to-Government) services. Therefore, only pair 2 is accurately matched. This question tests the candidate's understanding of the CSC scheme, its role in the national e-governance plan, and the services it provides.  Understanding the digital infrastructure and its impact on service delivery is important for UPSC preparation.

**9. With reference to  Mercy Petitions and Curative Petitions, consider the following pairs:**

    Petition Type                                   Feature
1. Mercy Petition:  Can only be filed by the convict.
2. Curative Petition:  Available after the dismissal of a review petition.
3. Article 72:  Deals with the President's power to grant pardons, including for death sentences.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  A mercy petition can be filed by the convict or on their behalf by others, making statement 1 incorrect.  A curative petition is correctly paired with its availability after the dismissal of a review petition.  Article 72 accurately deals with the President's power to grant pardons, including those related to death sentences.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. **10. With reference to  Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs), consider the following pairs:**

    Item                                         Characteristic

3. Objective of FTSCs: To ensure swift disposal of rape cases and those under the POCSO Act.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

The funding for FTSCs comes from the Nirbhaya Fund, not solely from state budgets, making statement 2 incorrect.  The objective of FTSCs is accurately described as ensuring the speedy disposal of rape and POCSO Act cases. Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched. **1. With reference to the Indian legal system, consider the following pairs:**

    Provision                                     Description
    1. Article 72                               :   Empowers the President to commute death sentences
    2. Article 137                               :   Relates to the Supreme Court's power of review
    3. Article 142                               :   Grants the Supreme Court power to do complete justice
    4.  Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008             :   Establishes courts at intermediate panchayat headquarters.
    5. Contempt of Courts Act, 1971           :   Defines civil and criminal contempt of court.

    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1, 2, and 3 only
    (b) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
    (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
    (d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to pardon, reprieve, respite, remit, or commute the punishment of any person convicted of any offense, including death sentences.  Article 137 deals with the Supreme Court's power to review its own judgments.  Article 142 empowers the Supreme Court to do complete justice in any case before it, a crucial provision for ensuring equitable outcomes. The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, establishes a system of village-level courts, and their location at intermediate panchayat headquarters is a key feature. Finally, the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, provides the legal framework for dealing with contempt of court, differentiating between civil and criminal contempt.  Therefore, option (c) encompassing all pairs is the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. With reference to special provisions for states in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Provision/Concept                         Feature
    1. Special Category Status (SCS)          :   Currently granted to several Northeastern and Himalayan states based on Sub-Group of Chief Ministers' recommendations.
    2. Article 282                              :   Empowers the Centre to make discretionary grants for any public purpose.
    3. Sixth Schedule of the Constitution     :   Provides for the administration of tribal areas in certain states.
    4.  Article 371 (and subsequent clauses)   :   Provides a wide range of special provisions for several states.
    5. Special Financial Packages             :   Discretionary support for states facing geographical and socio-economic challenges.


    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1, 2, and 3 only
    (b) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
    (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
    (d) 1, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The Special Category Status (SCS), while previously a formal categorization, is now functionally applied through special provisions and funding patterns recommended by bodies like the Sub-Group of Chief Ministers. Article 282 of the Constitution allows the central government to make discretionary grants, a crucial mechanism for providing financial assistance to states. The Sixth Schedule details administrative arrangements for tribal areas in specific states. Articles 371 and its subsequent clauses provide special provisions tailored to the unique circumstances of several states. Finally, special financial packages offer additional financial support to states grappling with geographical or socio-economic challenges.  Therefore, option (c) is the accurate answer.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

    Concept/Act                                  Description/Feature
    1. EVM-VVPAT System                        :   Includes a Voter Verifiable Paper Audit Trail for increased transparency.
    2. Model Code of Conduct (MCC)            :   Guidelines for political parties and candidates to ensure free and fair elections.
    3. Association for Democratic Reforms vs ECI :   Supreme Court case concerning EVM verification.
    4.  Bharat Electronics Limited (BEL)       :   Manufactures EVMs.
    5. Election Commission of India (ECI)        :   Issues directives on MCC violations.


    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1, 2, and 3 only
    (b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
    (c) 2, 3, and 5 only
    (d) 1, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

All pairs are correctly matched.  The EVM-VVPAT system incorporates a paper trail to enhance transparency and voter confidence. The Model Code of Conduct (MCC) provides guidelines to maintain the fairness of elections. The Association for Democratic Reforms vs ECI case involved a legal challenge to the EVM system's verification process. Bharat Electronics Limited (BEL) is a key manufacturer of Electronic Voting Machines (EVMs). The Election Commission of India (ECI) is responsible for issuing directives and enforcing the Model Code of Conduct.  Therefore, option (b), which includes all the pairs, is correct. Other options are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**4. With reference to governance and administration in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Entity/Program                              Characteristic/Function
    1. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)       :   Handle rape cases and POCSO Act cases.
    2.  Nirbhaya Fund                           :   Funds FTSCs.
    3.  Department of Justice, Ministry of Law :   Implements FTSCs.

    (b) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
    (c) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
    (d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) are specifically designed to expedite the resolution of rape cases and those under the Protection of Children from Sexual Offences (POCSO) Act.  The Nirbhaya Fund provides financial support for their operation. The Department of Justice, Ministry of Law and Justice, is responsible for implementing the FTSC scheme. However, the Citizen's Charter is a separate concept related to service delivery and transparency, not directly a component of Mission Karmayogi itself. Therefore, option (b) is the correct answer. Option (a) is incorrect because it omits pair 5.  Option (c) is wrong because it includes pair 4 incorrectly. Option (d) is incorrect because it incorrectly includes pair 4.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                  Characteristic
1. Passport issued in India                :   Available in red, white, and blue colours
2.  CBI Director Selection Panel          :   Comprises the Prime Minister, Leader of Opposition, and Chief Justice of India
3.  The Model Code of Conduct (MCC)       :   Enforceable through provisions in statutes like the Representation of the People Act, 1951
4.  Common Service Centres (CSCs)         :   Established under the National e-Governance Plan (NeGP)
5.  Inner Line Permit (ILP)               :   Applicable to NRIs, PIO Card holders, and OCI holders


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is correct because pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.

* **Pair 2:** The CBI Director's selection panel indeed comprises the Prime Minister, Leader of the Opposition, and the Chief Justice of India. This reflects the importance given to maintaining the independence and impartiality of the agency.  The composition ensures a balance of executive, legislative, and judicial oversight.

* **Pair 3:** While the Model Code of Conduct (MCC) doesn't have statutory backing, its violations can be addressed through provisions within existing laws like the Representation of the People Act, 1951. This demonstrates how the MCC, despite its non-statutory nature, exerts influence on electoral conduct.  The legal framework provides avenues for redressal against violations.

* **Pair 4:** Common Service Centres (CSCs) are integral to the National e-Governance Plan (NeGP), aiming to extend government services to rural areas. This reflects the government's commitment to digital empowerment and inclusive governance.  CSCs function as crucial access points for various government and private services.

Pair 1 is incorrect as Indian passports are issued in blue, white, and maroon, not red. Pair 5 is incorrect because NRIs, PIO cardholders, and OCI holders are *not* eligible for ILPs; they require Protected/Restricted Area Permits.  These inaccuracies highlight the importance of precise factual recall in governance-related questions.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Amendment                                 Provision/Feature
1.  Delhi Special Police Establishment (DSPE) Act, 1946 :  Governs the Central Bureau of Investigation (CBI)
2.  73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts, 1992 :   Relate to local self-governance
3.  The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023     :   Explicitly mentions the ‘right to be forgotten’
4.  Bengal Eastern Frontier Regulations of 1873        :   Origin of the Inner Line Permit (ILP) system
5.  Companies Act, 1956                           :   Governs the establishment of Common Service Centres (CSC) SPV


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1 and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is correct as pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.

* **Pair 1:** The Delhi Special Police Establishment Act, 1946, is the legal framework governing the CBI's operations.  This highlights the legal basis for the CBI's investigative powers and its role within the Indian legal system.

* **Pair 2:** The 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts of 1992 are foundational to the structure of local self-governance in India.  These acts established Panchayati Raj Institutions (PRIs) and Urban Local Bodies (ULBs), respectively, playing a significant role in decentralization.

* **Pair 4:**  The Bengal Eastern Frontier Regulations of 1873 are the historical origin of the Inner Line Permit (ILP) system, designed to regulate access to certain areas in Northeast India.  Understanding this historical context helps in analyzing the contemporary implications of the ILP system.

* **Pair 5:** The Companies Act, 1956, is the legal framework under which the CSC SPV (Special Purpose Vehicle) was established.  This underscores the legal structure supporting the implementation of the CSC scheme and its role in delivering citizen services.

Pair 3 is incorrect. While the European GDPR includes the "right to be forgotten," the Indian Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, does not explicitly mention it.  This demonstrates differences in data protection approaches across jurisdictions.  The inclusion of such a right is a matter of ongoing discussion and debate within the Indian legal framework.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Institution/Body                             Key Function/Characteristic
1.  Cabinet Committees                         :   Constitutional bodies mentioned in the Constitution of India
2.  Parliamentary Privileges Committee (Lok Sabha) :   Consists of 10 members nominated by the Speaker
3.  Rajya Sabha                               :   Elects members using proportional representation through a single transferable vote
4.  Finance Commission                           :   Recommends the sharing of resources between the Union and States
5.  Committee on Official Language               :   Submits recommendations to the Prime Minister


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3 and 4 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 5 only
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Option (a) is correct because only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.

* **Pair 3:** The Rajya Sabha indeed uses proportional representation with a single transferable vote system for electing its members. This reflects a specific electoral mechanism designed to ensure representation for different groups.

* **Pair 4:** The Finance Commission is constitutionally mandated to advise on the distribution of resources between the Union and States.  This highlights the crucial role of the Finance Commission in maintaining fiscal balance and equitable resource allocation.

Pair 1 is incorrect; Cabinet Committees are extra-constitutional. Pair 2 is incorrect; the Lok Sabha's Privileges Committee has 15 members, not 10.  Pair 5 is incorrect; the Committee on Official Language submits recommendations to the President, not the Prime Minister. These inaccuracies underscore the need for precise knowledge of institutional structures and procedures.  Understanding the nuances of these differences is crucial for analyzing the Indian political system.

1. CPGRAMS                                     :   Single portal for lodging grievances
2.  E-Nivaran                                   :   Launched by CBDT
3.  Sevottam Model                               :   Focuses on improving quality of public service delivery
4.  Pro-Active Governance and Timely Implementation (PRAGATI) :   Multi-purpose platform to address grievances


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. CPGRAMS is a single-window portal for citizens to lodge grievances. E-Nivaran is a platform launched by the Central Board of Direct Taxes (CBDT) to address taxpayer grievances.  The Sevottam Model is designed to improve the quality of public service delivery, and PRAGATI is a multi-purpose platform for addressing grievances and monitoring government programs. This question assesses knowledge of different grievance redressal mechanisms used in Indian governance.  The comprehensive nature of the correct option and the accuracy of all pairings make this a challenging question.


**1. With reference to Local Self-Governance and its Audit in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Institution                                      Key Feature/Responsibility
1. 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Act, 1992 :  Established the AuditOnline application for online audit of panchayat accounts
2. Ministry of Panchayati Raj                         : Developed the AuditOnline application, awarded the World Summit on Information Society Prizes 2023
3. Comptroller and Auditor General of India (CAG)     : Exercises control and supervision over the auditing of all three levels of Panchayati Raj Institutions (PRIs) and Urban Local Bodies (ULBs) through ELFA/DLFA.
4. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) : Aims to set global standards for auditing local governance bodies and is located in Rajkot, Gujarat.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts of 1992 laid the foundation for local self-governance in India, but the AuditOnline application was developed later by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj.  The Ministry of Panchayati Raj did indeed develop the AuditOnline application and received the World Summit on Information Society Prizes 2023 for it. The CAG's role in auditing local bodies stems from the CAG's (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971, and it is carried out primarily through the ELFA/DLFA system across states.  Finally, the International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) inaugurated in Rajkot, Gujarat aims to set global standards for auditing local governance bodies.  Therefore, options 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Option 1 incorrectly links the 1992 amendments directly to the AuditOnline application; the application is a later development building upon the framework established by the amendments.
