**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Law                                      Key Feature
1. Telecommunications Act, 2023             : Repeals Indian Telegraph Act, 1885 and Indian Wireless Telegraphy Act, 1933
2. Public Examination (Prevention of Unfair Means) Act, 2024 :  Establishes a three-member Review Committee at the state level
3. Temporary Suspension of Telecom Services (Public Emergency or Public Safety) Rules, 2017 : Governs internet shutdowns based on public safety grounds
4. Bharatiya Nagrik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023 :  Provides for the registration of Zero FIRs

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The Telecommunications Act, 2023, significantly overhauls the legal framework for telecommunications in India, replacing the outdated Indian Telegraph Act, 1885, and Indian Wireless Telegraphy Act, 1933.  This makes pair 1 correct.  The Temporary Suspension of Telecom Services (Public Emergency or Public Safety) Rules, 2017, explicitly address the legal basis for internet shutdowns in India, making pair 3 correct. The Bharatiya Nagrik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023, incorporates the provision for Zero FIR registration, aligning with recommendations from the Justice Verma Committee, thus pair 4 is also correct.

Pair 2 is incorrect. The Public Examination (Prevention of Unfair Means) Act, 2024, focuses on preventing unfair means in public examinations and outlines penalties. It does not establish a three-member review committee at the state level; that function is associated with the 2017 Rules concerning telecom service suspensions.  The inclusion of a state-level review committee is a crucial element differentiating the regulatory mechanisms.  Therefore, option (b) is the most accurate representation of the correctly matched pairs. Options (a), (c), and (d) include at least one incorrectly matched pair.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Doctrine/Principle                      Description
1. Doctrine of Coverture                         :  Treats a married woman as a single entity with her husband
2. Doctrine of Harmonious Construction          :  Relates to the discretionary power of a court to extend time limits
3. Anti-Defection Law                           :  Deals with disqualification of MLAs who voluntarily give up party membership.
4.  Mercy Petition                               :  Deals with the President's power to pardon convicts sentenced to death.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

The Doctrine of Coverture, originating from English common law, indeed treated a married woman as legally subsumed under her husband, impacting her property rights and legal standing.  The Doctrine of Harmonious Construction is a legal principle guiding courts in interpreting statutes to avoid conflicts between different provisions. The Anti-Defection Law (10th Schedule) addresses the disqualification of legislators who switch parties.  The President's power to grant pardons, including commutation of death sentences, is established through the process of mercy petitions.  All four pairs accurately reflect the core essence of the respective legal concepts.  Therefore, option (b) encompassing all four pairs is the correct answer. The other options incorrectly exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Article of the Indian Constitution     Provision Related to
1. Article 72                         : Power of President to grant pardons
2. Article 137                        : Review petitions in Supreme Court
3. Article 142                        : Power of Supreme Court to do complete justice
4. Article 19(1)(a)                   : Freedom of speech and expression
5. Article 19(2)                      : Reasonable restrictions on freedom of speech

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offence.  Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments.  Article 142 allows the Supreme Court to pass any order necessary for doing complete justice. Article 19(1)(a) guarantees the fundamental right to freedom of speech and expression, while Article 19(2) outlines the permissible restrictions on this right. Therefore, option (d) encompassing all five pairs is the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.

**1. With reference to the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

     Article                                         Provision
1. Article 244(2)                               :   Formation of Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs)
2. Article 280                                   :   Establishment of the Finance Commission
3. Article 371                                   :   Special Provisions for certain States and Union Territories
4. Article 282                                  :   Power to make grants for any public purpose
5. Article 324                                  :   Power of superintendence, direction and control of elections


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 244(2) deals with the Sixth Schedule of the Constitution, which empowers the Governor to establish ADCs and ARCs in specified states. Article 280 mandates the establishment of the Finance Commission to advise on the distribution of financial resources between the Union and States. Article 371 provides special provisions for certain states, addressing unique regional needs and concerns. Article 282 empowers both the Central and State governments to make grants for any public purpose, not necessarily restricted to their legislative competence. Article 324 vests the Election Commission with the power to supervise, direct, and control all elections to Parliament, State Legislatures, the offices of the President and Vice-President.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they omit one or more of the correctly matched pairs.


**2. With reference to the Election Process in India, consider the following pairs:**

     Act/Code                                    Key Feature
1.  Representation of the People Act, 1951       :   Deals with electoral offences like impersonation
2.  Model Code of Conduct (MCC)                :   Applies to all political parties during elections, lacks statutory backing
3.  Indian Penal Code (IPC)                      :   Contains provisions for prosecuting violations of the MCC
4.  Bhartiya Nyaya Sanhita (BNS)                :   Contains provisions related to electoral offences
5.  The Cantonments Act, 2006                   :   Governs the administration of Cantonment Boards


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Representation of the People Act, 1951, indeed deals with various electoral offences. The Model Code of Conduct (MCC) applies to all political parties and candidates during the election period, but it's crucial to note that the MCC is not a statute and hence lacks direct legal enforceability.  While the IPC and BNS contain provisions that can be used to prosecute certain actions that violate the spirit of the MCC, the MCC itself doesn't have its own enforcement mechanisms. The Cantonments Act, 2006, is unrelated to the election process.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched. Option (a) is incorrect because it omits the correct pairing of the BNS. Options (c) and (d) incorrectly include the IPC and the Cantonments Act, respectively.


**3. With reference to Special Status for States in India, consider the following pairs:**

     State/Concept                            Characteristic
1.  Special Category Status (SCS)              :   Based on recommendations of Finance Commissions, ceased to exist after 14th FC
2.  Special Financial Packages                :   Discretionary grants under Article 282, not necessarily need-based
3.  Fifth Finance Commission                    :   First introduced Special Category Status (SCS)
4.  Fourteenth Finance Commission              :   Recommended discontinuation of SCS
5.  Article 371                                  :   Provides for special provisions for certain states


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Special Category Status (SCS) was indeed a classification used to provide additional financial and developmental assistance to states facing socio-economic challenges, based on the recommendations of Finance Commissions; it was discontinued after the 14th Finance Commission. Special financial packages are discretionary grants under Article 282, not always tied to a specific need. The Fifth Finance Commission introduced the SCS concept, while the Fourteenth Finance Commission recommended its cessation.  Article 371 provides for special provisions for certain states, enabling tailored approaches to their unique circumstances.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they omit one or more of the correctly matched pairs.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Body/Act                     Key Feature/Provision
1. Cantonments Act, 2006                  :   Administered under the Ministry of Defence
2. 74th Constitutional Amendment Act      :   Deals with local self-government of cantonments
3. Article 244(2)                           :   Relates to the formation of Autonomous District Councils (ADCs)
4. Article 72                               :   Empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, etc.
5. Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008              :   Establishes courts at intermediate Panchayat headquarters

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Cantonments Act, 2006, governs the administration of cantonments, which are under the administrative control of the Ministry of Defence.  The 74th Constitutional Amendment Act deals with urban local bodies, and the administration of cantonments falls under its purview regarding local self-governance. Article 244(2) pertains to the Sixth Schedule of the Constitution, which establishes provisions for Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs) in certain states of Northeast India.  Article 72 outlines the President's power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment. The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, establishes Gram Nyayalayas (village courts) at the headquarters of intermediate Panchayats.  Option (a) is incorrect because it excludes the correctly matched pair related to Article 72 (President's pardon powers). Option (c) is incorrect as it omits the correct pairing of Article 72. Option (d) is incorrect because it incorrectly includes the pairing of Article 244(2) with Cantonments.


**2. With reference to Centre-State relations, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision/Concept                         Description
1. Seventh Schedule                           :   Defines the tax bases between the Union and States
2. Article 269                               :   Taxes levied and collected by the Centre but wholly assigned to States
3. Article 282                               :   Empowers the Centre and States to make discretionary grants
4. Article 3                                  :   Deals with the formation of new States
5. Sixth Schedule                             :   Empowers the Governor to create Autonomous District Councils (ADCs)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Seventh Schedule of the Indian Constitution clearly delineates the powers and responsibilities of the Union and State governments, including the allocation of tax bases. Article 269 specifies that certain taxes levied and collected by the Union government are assigned to the states.  Article 282 empowers both the Union and State governments to make grants for any public purpose, even beyond their legislative competence, encompassing discretionary grants. Article 3 of the Constitution deals with the formation of new states and alteration of existing state boundaries. The Sixth Schedule, under Article 244(2), empowers the Governor to establish Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs) in specific states. All the pairs are correctly matched; therefore, option (d) is the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.


**3. With reference to the Indian judicial system, consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Concept/Procedure                   Description/Provision
1. Contempt of Court                         :   Defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971
2. Mercy Petition                             :   Covered under Article 72 of the Constitution
3. Curative Petition                          :   A last resort remedy after review petition dismissal
4. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)       :   Handle rape and POCSO Act cases under a centrally sponsored scheme
5.  Right to be Forgotten (RTBF)             : Explicitly mentioned in the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, defines contempt of court. Article 72 of the Constitution empowers the President to grant pardons, including considering mercy petitions. A curative petition is the last legal recourse available to a litigant after a review petition is dismissed by the Supreme Court. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) are established under a centrally sponsored scheme to expedite the disposal of rape and POCSO Act cases.  The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, does *not* explicitly mention the right to be forgotten. Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Option (b) is incorrect as it omits the correct pairing for FTSCs. Option (c) is incorrect because it incorrectly includes the pairing of RTBF with the Digital Personal Data Protection Act. Option (d) is incorrect for the same reason.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Order/Scheme                         Key Feature/Provision
1. Foreigners (Protected Areas) Order, 1958 :   Deals with Protected Areas between the Inner Line and International Border
2. Inner Line Permit (ILP)                   :   Regulates movement in protected areas, aiming to protect tribal cultures
3. Bengal Eastern Frontier Regulations, 1873:   Historical genesis of the ILP system
4.  Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963:  Covers Andaman & Nicobar Islands and parts of Sikkim
5.  National e-Governance Plan (NeGP)      :  Includes Common Service Centres (CSCs) as a key component


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Foreigners (Protected Areas) Order, 1958, designates areas between the Inner Line and the International Border as Protected Areas, requiring permits for entry. The Inner Line Permit (ILP) system regulates entry into these areas, primarily to protect the unique cultural heritage of tribal communities.  The Bengal Eastern Frontier Regulations of 1873 represent the historical origin of the ILP system. The Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963, declares certain areas, including the entire Union Territory of Andaman & Nicobar Islands and parts of Sikkim, as Restricted Areas. The National e-Governance Plan (NeGP) includes Common Service Centres (CSCs) as a crucial element for delivering government services to rural citizens.  All five pairs are correctly matched, making (d) the correct option. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete, omitting at least one correctly matched pair.

**1. With reference to Grievance Redressal Mechanisms in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Mechanism                                   Key Feature
    1. CPGRAMS                               :   Handles grievances related to service delivery at the state level only

    3. Department of Administrative Reforms and Public Grievances (DARPG) :  Developed the GRAI tool for comparative analysis of GRMs
    4.  E-Nivaran                              :  A platform launched by CBDT to address taxpayer grievances.

(a) 1 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because it accurately matches the mechanisms with their key features.  CPGRAMS (Centralized Public Grievance Redress and Monitoring System) is a pan-India online portal for lodging grievances with various ministries and departments at both the central and state levels, making statement 1 incorrect.  The Directorate of Public Grievances operates under the Ministry of Personnel, Public Grievances and Pensions (MoPPG&P), making statement 2 correct. The Department of Administrative Reforms and Public Grievances (DARPG) is responsible for developing tools like GRAI (Grievance Redressal Assessment Index) to evaluate grievance redressal mechanisms, thus validating statement 3. 1. Public Accounts Committee                    :   Examines the audit reports of the Comptroller and Auditor General of India (CAG)
2. Estimates Committee                         :   Scrutinizes the demands for grants presented to Parliament
3. Committee on Public Undertakings (COPU)   :   Reviews the working of public sector undertakings

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Public Accounts Committee (PAC) is a crucial parliamentary committee that examines the CAG's audit reports on the government's revenue and expenditure. This ensures accountability and transparency in government finances.  The Estimates Committee scrutinizes the government's budget proposals (demands for grants) before they are approved by Parliament, helping to improve efficiency and effectiveness in resource allocation.  The Committee on Public Undertakings (COPU) focuses specifically on the performance of public sector undertakings, assessing their profitability, efficiency, and adherence to good governance principles.  All three committees play distinct but vital roles in parliamentary oversight and governance. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.  The question is designed to test the candidate's knowledge of the functions of key parliamentary committees, highlighting their importance in the Indian parliamentary system.


**2. With reference to the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

   Article                                         Provision
1. Article 72                                    :   Power of the President to grant pardons
2. Article 137                                   :   Power of the Supreme Court to review its judgments
3. Article 142                                   :   Power of the Supreme Court to do complete justice

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to pardon, reprieve, respite, remit, or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offense.  Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments, allowing for corrections or reconsiderations if necessary. Article 142 is a crucial provision that enables the Supreme Court to pass any order necessary to do complete justice, even if it means exceeding its ordinary powers.  This ensures the Supreme Court can effectively resolve complex cases and ensure equitable outcomes.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete, failing to recognize the accuracy of all three pairings. The question assesses the candidate's understanding of key constitutional provisions related to presidential and judicial powers, emphasizing their significance in maintaining the rule of law and upholding justice.

**1. With reference to the constitutional provisions related to Special Category States (SCS), consider the following pairs:**

   Provision/Feature                                 Detail
1. Initial Grant of SCS                         :   Based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula
2. Constitutional Basis for SCS                 :   Explicitly mentioned in the Constitution under Article 370
3. Cessation of SCS                              :   Recommended by the 14th Finance Commission

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The first pair is correctly matched.  SCS states initially received grants based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula. This was a significant aspect of the financial arrangement for these states. The third pair is also correctly matched. The 14th Finance Commission recommended the discontinuation of the SCS status, leading to the current system where special funding for Northeastern and Himalayan states is based on other recommendations rather than their SCS status.  However, the second pair is incorrect. The Constitution does *not* explicitly mention Special Category States in a single article like Article 370 (which dealt with J&K's special status, now revoked).  While the Constitution provides for special provisions under Articles 371, 371-A to 371-H, and 371-J for various states,  there's no single constitutional article defining or granting SCS status. This is a crucial distinction that highlights the difference between constitutional provisions and administrative classifications.  The inclusion of Article 370 as a distractor tests the candidate's understanding of the evolution of special status provisions within the Indian constitutional framework.


**2. With reference to the Aadhaar Act, 2016 and its constitutional implications (Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v. UoI), consider the following pairs:**

   Aspect of Aadhaar                                   Court Ruling
1. Metadata Retention Period                       :   Unlimited storage permitted
2. Applicability to Bank Accounts                    :   Mandatory for opening bank accounts
3. Sharing of Aadhaar Data with Private Entities    :   Permitted under specific government contracts

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are incorrectly matched. The Supreme Court's 2018 judgment in *Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v. UoI* clarified several aspects of the Aadhaar Act.  First, it ruled that Aadhaar metadata cannot be stored for more than six months, contradicting statement 1. Second, the court held that Aadhaar cannot be *forced* on people for opening bank accounts or for mobile and internet connections, contradicting statement 2. The court also explicitly stated that the state cannot enter into contracts with private corporations for sharing of Aadhaar data, as it infringes on the right to privacy, thus contradicting statement 3.  The options are designed to test the candidate's understanding of the nuances of the Supreme Court's judgment on Aadhaar's constitutionality, especially concerning data privacy and mandatory usage.  The "None" option serves as a crucial distractor, ensuring that candidates understand the complete judgment and not just isolated parts.


**3. With reference to the Parliamentary Committees in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Committee                                       Characteristic/Function

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only the third pair is correctly matched. The Parliamentary Committee on Official Languages (PCOL) was indeed constituted under Section 4 of the Official Languages Act, 1963. The first pair is incorrect; the Public Accounts Committee (PAC) consists of members from both Lok Sabha and Rajya Sabha. The second pair is also incorrect; the Estimates Committee's function is to examine the government's *expenditure*, not revenue. The PAC is responsible for auditing revenue and expenditure.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the composition and functions of different parliamentary committees, highlighting the differences between PAC and Estimates Committee.  The incorrect options are carefully chosen to resemble the correct answer, testing the candidate's precise understanding of each committee's role.


**4. With reference to the President of India's powers concerning mercy petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Sentence                                     Presidential Power under Article 72
1. Sentence by a Court Martial                       :   Cannot grant pardon, reprieve, etc.
2. Sentence for an offence against a Union Law       :   Can grant pardon, reprieve, etc.
3. Life Imprisonment                               :   Can only commute, not remit


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only the second pair is correctly matched. Article 72 explicitly empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to commute sentences for offences against Union laws. The first pair is incorrect; the President *can* grant pardons, reprieves, etc., for sentences given by a Court Martial. The third pair is also incorrect; the President can remit (completely cancel) a life imprisonment sentence, in addition to commuting it (reducing it to a lesser sentence).  This question tests the detailed understanding of Article 72 and the scope of the President's mercy powers. The distractors are designed to be plausible, challenging the candidate to recall the precise extent of the President's powers in different sentencing scenarios.

The Aadhaar Act, 2016, as affirmed by the Supreme Court, makes Aadhaar mandatory for accessing certain social welfare schemes while upholding the right to privacy by not mandating it for bank accounts or mobile connections. **5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Act/Amendment/Policy                             Key Feature

The 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts, 1992, are foundational for the establishment and functioning of Panchayati Raj Institutions and Urban Local Bodies in India. **1. With reference to Gram Nyayalayas, consider the following pairs:**

    Act/Provision                                     Feature
    1. Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008                    :   Exempts all Northeastern states
    2. Indian Evidence Act, 1872                     :   Applies to Gram Nyayalaya proceedings
    3. Article 142 of the Constitution                 :   Source of curative petition power
    4. Court of Session                              :   Appeals from criminal cases in Gram Nyayalayas


    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1 only
    (b) 2 and 3 only
    (c) 3 and 4 only
    (d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, exempts only Nagaland, Arunachal Pradesh, Sikkim and specified tribal areas, not all Northeastern states.  The Indian Evidence Act, 1872, does *not* apply to Gram Nyayalaya proceedings; they are guided by principles of natural justice.  Article 142 is the source of the Supreme Court's power to do complete justice, which underpins the curative petition process.  Appeals from criminal cases originating in Gram Nyayalayas go to the Court of Session. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.


**2. With reference to Contempt of Court, consider the following pairs:**

    Type of Contempt                                  Description
    1. Civil Contempt                               :   Publication of matter scandalizing a court
    2. Criminal Contempt                            :   Wilful disobedience of a court order
    3. Article 129 of the Constitution                :   Grants power to High Courts to punish contempt
    4. Contempt of Courts Act, 1971                  :   Defines and outlines procedures for contempt


    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1 only
    (b) 2 and 4 only
    (c) 3 and 4 only
    (d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Civil contempt involves willful disobedience of court orders, while criminal contempt includes actions like publishing material that scandalizes or undermines the court's authority.  Article 129 grants the Supreme Court the power to punish for contempt, and a similar power is granted to High Courts under Article 215. The Contempt of Courts Act, 1971, defines and provides the legal framework for dealing with contempt of court. Thus, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.


**3. With reference to Mercy Petitions and Curative Petitions, consider the following pairs:**

    Petition Type                                    Provision/Feature
    1. Mercy Petition                               :   Governed by Article 72
    2. Curative Petition                            :   First established in Rupa Ashok Hurra v. Ashok Hurra
    3. Article 137 of the Constitution                :   Deals with review petitions
    4. President of India                            :   Can commute death sentences


    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1 and 2 only
    (b) 1, 2, and 3 only
    (c) 1, 3, and 4 only
    (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, etc., including commuting death sentences, which is central to the process of mercy petitions.  The curative petition, a final recourse after review petition dismissal, was established through the case of *Rupa Ashok Hurra v. Ashok Hurra*. Article 137 deals with the Supreme Court's power to review its judgments, making review petitions a prerequisite for a curative petition.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched.

**10. With reference to the Scheduled Castes and sub-classification, consider the following pairs:**

    Provision/Concept                               Characteristic
    1. Article 341(1)                               :   Allows for sub-classification of SCs
    2. Article 341(2)                               :   Prohibits sub-classification of SCs
    3.  State of Punjab & Others v Davinder Singh    :   Upheld the permissibility of sub-classification
    4.  Substantive equality                         :   Considers historical injustices


    Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
    (a) 1 and 3 only
    (b) 1 and 4 only
    (c) 2 and 4 only
    (d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 341(1) deals with the President's power to specify Scheduled Castes, and the Supreme Court case *State of Punjab & Others v. Davinder Singh* affirmed that sub-classification within the SCs is permissible. Substantive equality, a key concept in affirmative action, acknowledges historical injustices and seeks to address them. Article 341(2) allows Parliament to modify the list of Scheduled Castes, it does not prohibit sub-classification. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.  This highlights the importance of carefully understanding the nuances of constitutional provisions.


**1. With reference to India's Fiscal Federalism, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision                     Specific Provision
1. Article 270                               :   Taxes levied and collected by the Union, distributed between Union and States
2. Article 275                               :   Grants-in-aid provided by the Centre to States
3. Article 292                               :   Union government's power to borrow money within or outside the country
4. Article 280                               :   Establishment of the Finance Commission

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched.  Article 270 deals with the distribution of tax revenue between the Union and States.  Article 275 outlines the provision for grants-in-aid from the Centre to States. Article 292 explicitly grants the Union government the power to borrow both domestically and internationally. Finally, Article 280 mandates the establishment of the Finance Commission to advise on the distribution of financial resources.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.  Understanding the specific constitutional provisions governing fiscal federalism is crucial for comprehending the intricate financial relationship between the Union and State governments in India. This demonstrates a strong grasp of the constitutional framework underlying India's federal system.


**2. With reference to the Special Category Status (SCS) in India, consider the following pairs:**

    State                                      Characteristic
1. Jammu & Kashmir (pre-2019)           :   Received SCS based on Gadgil-Mukherjee formula
2. Andhra Pradesh                           :   Currently holds Special Category Status
3. Sikkim                                   :   Granted SCS after 1969
4. Nagaland                                 :   One of the initial states granted SCS in 1969


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Jammu and Kashmir (before its reorganization in 2019) was indeed granted Special Category Status and received funding based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula.  Sikkim and Nagaland were among the initial recipients of SCS in 1969. Andhra Pradesh's claim for SCS has been a significant political issue, but it has not been granted this status. Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they either include the incorrectly matched pair related to Andhra Pradesh or exclude correctly matched pairs related to J&K, Sikkim, and Nagaland.  The question tests the candidate's understanding of the historical context and evolution of the SCS policy in India, including the discontinuation of the SCS designation itself following the 14th Finance Commission's recommendations.


**3. With reference to the Common Service Centres (CSCs) scheme, consider the following pairs:**

    Aspect                                    Detail
1.  Governing Body                           :   Ministry of Electronics & IT
2.  Legal Framework                         :   Companies Act, 1956
3.  National e-Governance Plan (NeGP) Pillar:  National Data Bank/State Data Centres
4.  Service Category Provided              :    G2C services only


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The CSC SPV, which oversees the CSC scheme, was indeed set up by the Ministry of Electronics & IT and is governed under the Companies Act, 1956. The National e-Governance Plan (NeGP) comprised three pillars: Connectivity, National Data Bank/State Data Centres, and Common Service Centres (CSCs).  However, CSCs offer a broader range of services than just G2C; they also include B2C and financial services.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the incorrectly matched pair concerning the service categories provided by CSCs. Option (a) and (c) are also incorrect, as they omit crucial correctly matched pairs. The question assesses the candidate's understanding of the CSC scheme's structure, governance, and its role within the larger framework of the National e-Governance Plan.


**4. With reference to the Foreign Contribution (Regulation) Act (FCRA), consider the following pairs:**

    Provision                                 Specification
1.  Designated Account                       :   Any branch of any scheduled bank in India
2.  Validity of Registration                 :   Five years with renewal option
3.  Administrative Expenses Limit           :   20% of the total foreign contribution received
4.  Implementing Ministry                   :   Ministry of Home Affairs


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The validity of FCRA registration is five years, with a provision for renewal.  The permissible limit for administrative expenses is 20% of the total foreign contribution. The Ministry of Home Affairs is responsible for implementing the FCRA. However, the designated FCRA account must be in specified branches of the State Bank of India, New Delhi, not just any scheduled bank. Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect either by including the incorrectly matched pair regarding the designated account or excluding correctly matched pairs related to the validity of registration, administrative expense limits, and the implementing ministry. This question tests the candidate’s knowledge of the FCRA's key provisions and regulatory aspects.


**5. With reference to Aadhaar, consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                                   Description
1.  Data Storage                             :   Decentralized storage across multiple servers
2.  Proof of Identity                         :   Proof of Citizenship
3.  Targeted Delivery Mechanism             :   Utilizes UID-enabled bank account network
4.  Constitutional Validity                  :   Affirmed by the Supreme Court in 2018


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Aadhaar's data is stored centrally, not decentralized.  Aadhaar is a proof of address and identity for residents of India, but it's not a proof of citizenship. Aadhaar does utilize a UID-enabled bank account network for targeted delivery, and the Supreme Court did affirm its constitutional validity in 2018. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include incorrectly matched pairs regarding data storage and proof of identity. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of the technical features, legal aspects, and constitutional implications of Aadhaar.


**6. With reference to Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSS), consider the following pairs:**

    Aspect                                     Detail
1. Funding Source                            :   Solely funded by the Central Government
2. Implementing Agency                      :   Usually implemented by the State Governments
3. Constitutional Basis                      :   State and Concurrent Lists of the Constitution
4.  Rationalization Report                   :   Report of the Sub-Group of Chief Ministers (2015)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

CSSs are jointly funded by the Centre and States, not solely by the Centre.  They are implemented by State Governments. Their constitutional basis lies in the State and Concurrent Lists. The 2015 report of the Sub-Group of Chief Ministers provided recommendations for the rationalization of CSSs.  Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they either include the incorrectly matched pair concerning funding or exclude correctly matched pairs related to implementation agencies, constitutional basis, and rationalization reports. This question assesses the candidate's understanding of the nature, implementation, and governance of Centrally Sponsored Schemes.


**7. With reference to the President's Power of Mercy, consider the following pairs:**

    Type of Sentence                           Constitutional Provision
1.  Death Sentence                           :   Article 72
2.  Sentence by Court-Martial                :   Article 72
3.  Sentence for Offenses against Union Laws :   Article 72
4.  Sentence for Offences against State Laws :   Article 161


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Articles 72 and 161 deal with the President and Governor's power of pardon, respectively.  Article 72 specifically covers death sentences, sentences by court-martial, and sentences for offenses against laws to which the executive power of the Union extends.  State laws fall under the Governor's power of mercy (Article 161). Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include the incorrectly matched pair concerning offenses against State laws or exclude correctly matched pairs related to death sentences, court-martial sentences, and Union law offenses.  This question tests the understanding of the constitutional provisions related to the President's power of mercy and its scope.


**8. With reference to the Consumer Protection Act, 2019, consider the following pairs:**

    Entity                                     Function
1.  Central Consumer Protection Authority (CCPA):  Set up consumer tribunals
2.  Consumer Mediation Cell                  :  Attached to District and State Commissions
3.  Product Liability Action                 :  Against manufacturers and service providers
4.  Misleading Advertisement Penalty         :   Up to Rs. 10 lakh fine and two years imprisonment for first offense


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The CCPA does not set up consumer tribunals; that is the function of the National Consumer Disputes Redressal Commission and other consumer forums.  Consumer Mediation Cells are attached to District and State Commissions. Product liability actions are indeed possible under the Act.  The penalty for misleading advertisements is correctly stated. Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they either wrongly include the function of setting up tribunals under CCPA or exclude correctly matched pairs concerning consumer mediation cells, product liability actions, and penalties for misleading advertisements.  This question assesses the candidate's understanding of the key features and provisions of the Consumer Protection Act.


**9. With reference to the Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

    State/Region                                 Feature
1.  Assam                                     :   Contains provisions for Autonomous District Councils
2.  Meghalaya                                 :   Does not fall under the Sixth Schedule
3.  Tripura                                   :   Contains provisions for Autonomous District Councils
4.  Ladakh (Demand for Inclusion)            :   Currently not included in the Sixth Schedule

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Sixth Schedule of the Constitution deals with the administration of tribal areas in certain states, including Assam, Meghalaya, and Tripura.  Meghalaya is not covered under the Sixth Schedule.  There is a demand to include Ladakh, but it is not currently included. Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they either wrongly include Meghalaya or exclude correctly matched pairs concerning Assam, Tripura, and the demand for Ladakh's inclusion.  This question tests the candidate's understanding of the Sixth Schedule's provisions and its geographical scope.  The inclusion of Ladakh highlights current political and administrative debates.


**10. With reference to Protected and Restricted Areas in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Area                                       Status
1.  Entire Arunachal Pradesh                 :   Protected Area
2.  Parts of Himachal Pradesh                :   Restricted Area
3.  Andaman & Nicobar Islands                :   Restricted Area
4.  Part of Sikkim                            :   Restricted Area

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Arunachal Pradesh is entirely designated as a Protected Area.  Andaman & Nicobar Islands and part of Sikkim are classified as Restricted Areas.  However, parts of Himachal Pradesh are classified as Protected Areas, not Restricted Areas. Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either wrongly include Himachal Pradesh under Restricted Areas or exclude correctly matched pairs concerning Arunachal Pradesh, Andaman & Nicobar Islands, and part of Sikkim.  This question assesses the candidate's understanding of the geographical demarcation of Protected and Restricted Areas in India and the implications for foreign visitors.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article              Provision Related To
1. Article 280                      :   Establishment of the Finance Commission
2. Article 275                      :   Grants-in-aid to states
3. Article 292                      :   Union government borrowing powers within and outside India
4. Article 246                      :   Tax bases between Union and States
5. Article 269-A                    :   Levy and Collection of GST in Inter-State Trade


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)


**Explanation:**

Article 280 of the Indian Constitution deals with the establishment of the Finance Commission.  This commission plays a crucial role in the distribution of financial resources between the Union and State governments. Article 275 empowers the Union government to provide grants-in-aid to states that are in need of financial assistance.  Article 292 outlines the borrowing powers of the Union government, both domestically and internationally. Article 246 clearly delineates the tax bases that are allocated to the Union and State governments, forming a fundamental aspect of India's fiscal federalism. Article 269-A specifically addresses the levy and collection of Goods and Services Tax (GST) in inter-state trade or commerce, a key aspect of India's indirect taxation system.  Therefore, options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs. Option (c) accurately reflects the correct pairings.  The inclusion of Article 292 in option (c) is slightly misleading as it doesn't specifically mention *only* borrowing powers within India, but the primary focus is indeed on the Union's borrowing capabilities.




**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   State/UT                          Special Status/Provision
1.  Arunachal Pradesh                :   Sixth Schedule Area
2.  Sikkim                           :   Protected Area (entirely) and Restricted Area (partly)
3.  Nagaland                         :   Previously granted Special Category Status
4.  Jammu & Kashmir (before 2019) :   Previously granted Special Category Status
5.  Andaman & Nicobar Islands       :   Restricted Area (entirely)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)


**Explanation:**

Arunachal Pradesh is a state covered under the Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution, which provides for the establishment of Autonomous District Councils. Sikkim is unique in having parts of its territory designated as both Protected Areas and Restricted Areas under the Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963.  Nagaland and Jammu & Kashmir (prior to the 2019 constitutional changes) were previously granted Special Category Status, a classification providing additional central assistance.  The Andaman and Nicobar Islands are entirely designated as a Restricted Area, requiring special permits for foreign visitors. Thus, all the pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (c) incorrectly exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.



**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Court/Petition             Legal Basis/Feature
1. Gram Nyayalayas                   :   Jurisdiction limited to civil disputes only
2. Contempt of Court                 :   Defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971
3. Curative Petition                  :   A remedy available after dismissal of a review petition
4. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs):   Exclusively handle cases under the POCSO Act


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)


**Explanation:**

Gram Nyayalayas, established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, possess both civil and criminal jurisdiction.  Contempt of Court is indeed defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971.  A curative petition is the last resort available in the Supreme Court after a review petition is dismissed.  However, FTSCs handle not only POCSO Act cases but also rape cases. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are entirely correct.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include one or more incorrectly matched pairs.  Option (a) accurately identifies the correctly matched pairs.



**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Financial Instrument/Policy       Feature/Characteristic
1.  Net Borrowing Ceiling (NBC)    :   Monetary policy tool
2.  Special Category Status (SCS)  :   Based on Gadgil-Mukherjee formula (currently)
3.  Special Packages               :   Provided under Article 282
4.  Grants-in-Aid                   :   Provided under Article 275
5.  Central Sponsored Schemes (CSS):   Funding pattern is always 90:10 (Centre:State)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3 and 4 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)


**Explanation:**

The Net Borrowing Ceiling is a fiscal policy tool, not a monetary policy tool. While SCS used to be based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula, this is no longer the case. Special Packages are indeed provided under Article 282, and grants-in-aid are provided under Article 275. The funding pattern for CSSs varies; it's not always 90:10. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are entirely correct. Options (b), (c), and (d) include at least one incorrect pairing. Only option (a) accurately reflects the correct matches.

    Scheme/Initiative                      Implementing Ministry/Body
1. Mission Karmayogi                   :   Ministry of Panchayati Raj

3. Common Service Centres (CSCs)       :   Ministry of Electronics & IT
4. International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) :   Ministry of Defence


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

Mission Karmayogi falls under the Capacity Building Commission. Jan Yojana Abhiyan is implemented by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj.  Common Service Centres (CSCs) are indeed overseen by the Ministry of Electronics & IT. The International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL) is not associated with the Ministry of Defence. Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) incorrectly include one or more mismatched pairs. Only option (b) accurately identifies the correct match.


**1. With reference to Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSSs) in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Scheme Feature
1. CSS Funding Pattern for 8 North Eastern States and 3 Himalayan States : Centre:State = 50:50
2. CSS Monitoring Jurisdiction                      :  Exclusively NITI Aayog
3.  Abolition of Plan-Non Plan Distinction          :  Post 2017
4. Number of CSSs                               :  75 across 3 categories
5. Percentage of Centre's Budget Expenditure on CSSs: 20.4%


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2, 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) because only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.  The funding pattern for the 8 Northeastern and 3 Himalayan states under CSS is 90:10 (Centre:State), not 50:50 as stated in pair 1.  NITI Aayog has concurrent jurisdiction in monitoring CSSs along with other entities, not exclusive jurisdiction as mentioned in pair 2. The abolition of the Plan-Non Plan distinction happened in 2017, making pair 3 correct. The number of CSSs across 3 categories is indeed 75, making pair 4 correct.  The percentage of the Centre's budget expenditure on CSSs is approximately 10.4%, not 20.4% as stated in pair 5.  Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 reflect accurate information regarding CSSs in India. This question tests factual recall and analytical skills by requiring the candidate to identify the correctly matched pairs among several plausible distractors.


**2. With reference to Mission Karmayogi, consider the following pairs:**

   Aspect                                    Detail
1. Launch Year of Capacity Building Commission : 2020
2. Target Group of NPCSCB                    :  All Union Government employees excluding contractual staff
3. Guiding Principle of Mission Karmayogi     :  Emphasis on rule-based training
4. Full form of NPCSCB                       : National Programme for Civil Services Capacity Building
5. Aim of NPCSCB                             : Creation of a less professional civil service.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 4 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 4 is correctly matched. The Capacity Building Commission was launched in 2021, not 2020 (pair 1).  NPCSCB covers all civil servants, including contractual employees (pair 2). A core guiding principle of Mission Karmayogi is a shift *from* rule-based to role-based training (pair 3). The full form of NPCSCB is correctly given in pair 4. The aim of NPCSCB is to create a *more* professional civil service (pair 5).  This question tests factual recall and requires careful attention to detail to avoid the plausible distractors presented in the incorrect pairs. The candidate needs to accurately recall the launch year, target group, and core principles of Mission Karmayogi.


**3. With reference to the Finance Commission and Fiscal Federalism in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                       Characteristic
1. 15th Finance Commission Recommendation     :  Vertical Devolution at 31%
2. Article 270                                 :  Taxes levied and collected by states, distributed to states
3. Article 293                                 :  State borrowing from outside India is permitted
4.  Basis of Horizontal Devolution              :  Income Distance (55%)
5. Article 275                                 :  Grants-in-aid to states


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 5 only
(c) 5 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 5 is correctly matched. The 15th Finance Commission recommended a vertical devolution of 41%, not 31% (pair 1). Article 270 deals with taxes levied and collected by the Union and distributed between the Union and States (pair 2). Article 293 states that state governments can borrow *within* India, not outside (pair 3). In horizontal devolution, Income Distance has a weight of 45%, not 55% (pair 4). Article 275 correctly pertains to grants-in-aid to states (pair 5). This question tests factual recall, requiring the candidate to remember specific articles of the Indian Constitution related to fiscal federalism and the recommendations of the 15th Finance Commission.  The distractors are designed to test the candidate’s ability to differentiate between closely related concepts.


**4. With reference to Special Category Status (SCS) and Special Packages in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                           Characteristic
1.  Year SCS was first introduced                    : 1979
2.  States granted SCS in 1969                     :  Jammu & Kashmir, Assam, Nagaland, Sikkim
3.  Basis for granting Special Packages             :  Explicit constitutional provision
4.  14th Finance Commission Recommendation        : SCS remains in effect
5.  Funding source for Special Packages             :  Article 282


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 5 only
(c) 5 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 5 is correctly matched. SCS was first introduced in 1969, not 1979 (pair 1).  Sikkim was granted SCS later, making pair 2 incorrect. Special packages are discretionary and not based on an explicit constitutional provision (pair 3). The 14th Finance Commission recommended the discontinuation of SCS (pair 4). Article 282 correctly empowers the Centre to make discretionary grants for public purposes, including special packages (pair 5).  This question tests knowledge of the historical context of SCS, the constitutional basis for special financial assistance, and the recommendations of the Finance Commissions.  The distractors include incorrect years, inaccurate lists of states, and misconceptions about the legal basis for special packages.


**5. With reference to the Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                         Characteristic
1.  Article enabling the Sixth Schedule           :  Article 244(1)
2.  Bodies established under the Sixth Schedule  :  Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) only
3.  Number of ADCs currently in existence        : 12
4.  Power of ADCs and ARCs                       :  Cannot collect land revenue
5.  Recommendation for Sixth Schedule             :  Nehru Committee


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 4 and 5 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

None of the pairs are correctly matched. The Sixth Schedule is enabled by Article 244(2), not Article 244(1) (pair 1).  The Sixth Schedule also empowers the establishment of Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs) in addition to ADCs (pair 2). Currently, there are 10 ADCs, not 12 (pair 3). ADCs and ARCs do have the power to collect land revenue (pair 4). The Sixth Schedule resulted from the Bardoloi Committee's recommendations, not the Nehru Committee (pair 5). This question tests detailed knowledge of the Sixth Schedule, including the relevant constitutional article, the types of councils established, their powers, and the committee that recommended its inclusion in the Constitution.  The distractors aim to test the candidate's precise understanding of the subject matter.  A superficial understanding would likely lead to incorrect answers.


**6. With reference to Local Self-Governance and its Audit in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                           Characteristic
1.  73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Act    :  Deals with local self-governance, not auditing
2.  AuditOnline Application                       :  Developed by Ministry of Rural Development
3.  CAG's Mandate for Auditing Local Bodies      :  Derived from the CAG (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971
4.  Examiner of Local Fund Accounts (ELFA)      :  Works independently of the CAG
5.  International Centre for Audit of Local Governance (iCAL): Located in Mumbai


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched. While the 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts deal with local self-governance, they don't explicitly outline the auditing mechanisms (pair 1). AuditOnline was developed by the Ministry of Panchayati Raj, not the Ministry of Rural Development (pair 2).  The CAG's mandate for auditing local bodies is indeed derived from the CAG (Duties, Powers and Conditions of Service) Act, 1971 (pair 3). ELFAs/DLFAs work under the technical guidance and supervision of the CAG, not independently (pair 4). iCAL is located in Rajkot, Gujarat, not Mumbai (pair 5). This question tests detailed knowledge of the constitutional basis for local self-governance, the mechanisms for auditing local bodies, and the roles of different organizations involved in the process.  The distractors test the candidate's understanding of the specific roles and responsibilities of various ministries and agencies.


**7. With reference to Cantonment Boards in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                                         Characteristic
1.  Recent development related to Cantonment Boards:  Merger of land portions with state local bodies
2.  Legal basis for Cantonment Boards              :  Indian Constitution, Article 244
3.  Governance structure of Cantonment Boards     :  Directly under the Ministry of Defence
4.  Number of Cantonment Boards in India           :  62
5.  Primary Function of Cantonment Boards         :  Providing civilian amenities in cantonment areas only


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3 and 5 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 1 is correctly matched.  The recent news involves the merger of land portions from 10 cantonment boards with concerned state local bodies (pair 1). Cantonment Boards are established under various laws, not specifically under Article 244 of the Indian Constitution (pair 2). While they are overseen by the Ministry of Defence, they have their own governance structures (pair 3). The exact number of cantonment boards may vary, and 62 might not be entirely accurate (pair 4). Cantonment Boards have broader functions beyond civilian amenities, including military administration (pair 5). This question tests knowledge of current affairs related to Cantonment Boards and their organizational structure.  The distractors test the candidate's understanding of the legal basis for their existence, their governance, and their precise functions.






**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article           Provision
1. Article 72                        : Power of President to grant pardons
2. Article 82                         : Delimitation of constituencies for Lok Sabha
3. Article 99                         : Oaths of office for Members of Parliament
4. Article 104                       : Penalty for sitting in Parliament without oath
5. Article 137                        : Power of Supreme Court to review its judgments

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to commute sentences in certain cases. Article 82 deals with the delimitation of constituencies for the Lok Sabha, ensuring fair representation based on population.  Article 99 outlines the procedure for Members of Parliament (MPs) to take oaths of office before assuming their duties.  Article 104 prescribes penalties for MPs who participate in Parliament proceedings without having taken the required oath.  While Article 137 relates to the Supreme Court's power of review, it's important to note this is a self-review mechanism, not an appeal process. Therefore, all pairs 1, 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.  Option (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.


**2. With reference to the Citizenship Act, 1955, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Amendment             Provision
1. Citizenship Act, 1955         : Permits dual citizenship
2. Citizenship Amendment Act, 1985: Added Section 6A to the Citizenship Act, 1955
3. Assam Accord                 :  Framework for granting Indian citizenship to certain groups
4. Section 6A of Citizenship Act, 1955 :  Deals with acquisition of citizenship by naturalisation

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Citizenship Act of 1955 does not provide for dual citizenship; India recognizes only single citizenship. The Citizenship Amendment Act of 1985 is directly linked to the addition of Section 6A, a special provision addressing citizenship issues related to the Assam Accord.  The Assam Accord itself provided a framework for resolving the issue of illegal immigrants in Assam and granting citizenship to certain groups. Section 6A deals specifically with the acquisition of Indian citizenship in specific circumstances, not solely through naturalization, but rather through a path outlined by the Assam accord. Option (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit one or more crucial connections.


**3. With reference to Cantonment Boards in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                   Detail
1. First Cantonment established               : Barrackpore in 1765
2. Governing Legislation                     : Cantonments Act, 2006
3. Number of Cantonments in India          : 70
4. Administrative Control                    : Ministry of Defence
5. President of Cantonment Board            : Station Commander (ex-officio)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Barrackpore was indeed the first cantonment established in 1765. The Cantonments Act, 2006, governs the administration of cantonments in India. There are currently 61 cantonments (not 70),  The Ministry of Defence holds administrative control over cantonments. The Station Commander serves as the ex-officio President of the Cantonment Board. Therefore, pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. Option (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they either omit correctly matched pairs or include an incorrect pair (number of cantonments).


**4. With reference to the Supreme Court's powers, consider the following pairs:**

   Power                                      Legal Basis
1.  Review of its own judgments               : Article 137
2.  Issuing directions or orders              : Article 142
3.  Condoning delay in filing appeals           : Inherent power of the court
4.  Hearing curative petitions                 : Flows from Article 142
5.  Judicial Review of Delimitation Commission Orders:  Inherent power of the court to review manifestly arbitrary actions

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 137 explicitly grants the Supreme Court the power to review its own judgments. Article 142 empowers the court to issue directions or orders necessary for doing complete justice. The power to condone delays in filing appeals is an inherent power of the court based on principles of equity and justice. Curative petitions, the last resort for legal redress, are rooted in the court's power under Article 142.  The Supreme Court possesses inherent powers to review decisions of other bodies if those decisions are demonstrably arbitrary or violate fundamental rights.  Therefore all pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                                   Key Feature
1. Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023              : Replaces the Indian Penal Code, 1860
2. Indian Penal Code, 1860                     :  Originally drafted under Thomas Babington Macaulay
3. The Places of Worship (Special Provisions) Act, 1991:  Freezes the religious character of places of worship as it stood on August 15, 1947
4.  Limitation Act, 1963                        : Contains provisions for condonation of delay
5.  The Protection of Children from Sexual Offences (POCSO) Act:  Has dedicated Fast-Track Special Courts for speedy disposal of cases

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita, 2023, is a comprehensive criminal law that replaces the existing Indian Penal Code (IPC) of 1860. The IPC was indeed drafted under the leadership of Thomas Babington Macaulay. The Places of Worship (Special Provisions) Act, 1991, maintains the religious character of places of worship as it existed on August 15, 1947. The Limitation Act, 1963, includes provisions related to the condonation of delays in legal proceedings. The POCSO Act has a dedicated system of Fast-Track Special Courts to ensure the speedy trial of cases.  All five pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are therefore incorrect.



**6. With reference to Special Category States (SCS) in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                             Detail
1.  Origin of SCS                                      : Recommendations of the Fifth Finance Commission
2.  Funding mechanism for SCS (Historically)           : Gadgil-Mukherjee formula
3.  Constitutional basis for SCS                       : Explicit mention in the Constitution
4.  Current status of SCS                              : No longer exist
5.  Alternative funding for Northeastern states          : Based on recommendations of a Sub-Group of Chief Ministers

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 5 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The concept of Special Category States (SCS) originated from the recommendations of the Fifth Finance Commission. Historically, the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula was used to determine the grants allocated to these states. The Constitution does not explicitly categorize any state as an SCS; special provisions were made through other articles. Following the recommendations of the Fourteenth Finance Commission, the SCS category ceased to exist.  Northeastern and Himalayan states now receive special funding based on the recommendations of a Sub-Group of Chief Ministers.  Therefore, pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect due to the inclusion of a wrongly matched pair or exclusion of correctly matched pairs.

   Legal Doctrine/Concept                            Description/Origin
1. Doctrine of Coverture                               :  Legal concept from English common law
2. Doctrine of Harmonious Construction               : Origin traced to the Shankari Prasad case
3.  Condonation of Delay                             : Discretionary power of courts to extend time limits
4.  Mercy Petition                                     :  Power of the President under Article 72
5.  Curative Petition                                  : Last resort legal remedy available in the Supreme Court


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The doctrine of coverture originated in English common law. The doctrine of harmonious construction has its roots in the Shankari Prasad case. Curative petitions are a final legal recourse available in the Supreme Court. All five pairs are correctly matched. Therefore, options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Body                                     Act/Amendment/Article
1. CAG                                      Article 151
2.  Delimitation Commission                 Article 324
3. National Human Rights Commission       Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993
4.  Press Council of India                  Indian Press Council Act, 1978

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Comptroller and Auditor General (CAG) of India is a constitutional body whose powers and duties are laid down in Articles 148 to 151 of the Indian Constitution.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched. The National Human Rights Commission (NHRC) is a statutory body established under the Protection of Human Rights Act, 1993. Thus, pair 3 is correct.  The Press Council of India was re-established under the Press Council Act, 1978, after being dissolved during the Emergency. Hence, pair 4 is also correct.  Pair 2 is incorrect; the Delimitation Commission is appointed by the President of India under Article 82 of the Constitution (for Parliament) and Article 170 (for State Legislatures). It does not directly relate to Article 324 which deals with the Election Commission of India.  Option (b) accurately reflects the correct pairings.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Institution                                   Key Feature/Responsibility
1. RTI Act, 2005                                  Replaced the Freedom of Information Act, 2002
2.  Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023      Regulates processing of digital personal data
3.  Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023            Replaces the Indian Evidence Act, 1872

(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, aims to protect citizens' digital personal data. The Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, modernizes evidence admissibility in Indian courts, replacing the outdated Indian Evidence Act, 1872. **3.  With reference to Constitutional Bodies, consider the following pairs:**

   Body                                              Appointment/Tenure
1.  Central Information Commissioner                  President of India, 3-year term
2.  Comptroller and Auditor General (CAG)            President of India, 6 years or until 65
3.  Chairperson, National Human Rights Commission   President of India, 3 years or until 70
4.  Director, CBI                                     Panel consisting of PM, Leader of Opposition and CJI, 2 years (previously)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. The Central Information Commissioner (CIC) is appointed by the President of India for a three-year term. The CAG is also appointed by the President for a six-year term or until the age of 65, whichever is earlier.  The Chairperson of the NHRC is appointed by the President for a term of three years or until the age of 70.  The Director of the CBI was previously appointed for a two-year term by a panel comprising the Prime Minister, the Leader of the Opposition, and the Chief Justice of India.  While recent changes have extended the tenure, the original structure of appointment remains accurate for this question. Therefore, option (d) is correct.


**4. With reference to the Election Process in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Aspect                                          Provision/Body
1.  Model Code of Conduct                         Article 324
2.  Superintendence, direction and control of elections  Election Commission of India
3.  Single-member constituency in Lok Sabha elections  Territorial representation
4.  Enforcement of Model Code of Conduct          Statutory backing


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2, 3 only
(d) 1,2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Pair 2 is correct: The Election Commission of India (ECI) has the power of superintendence, direction, and control of elections to Parliament, State Legislatures, the President, and the Vice-President, as per Article 324 of the Constitution. Pair 3 is also correct: Lok Sabha elections utilize a system of territorial representation, with each constituency electing only one representative (single-member constituency).  Pair 1 is incorrect: The Model Code of Conduct (MCC) is not explicitly mentioned in the Constitution; it is a set of guidelines issued by the ECI. Pair 4 is incorrect: The MCC lacks statutory backing; its enforcement relies on moral suasion and persuasive measures rather than legal penalties. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched, making option (a) the correct answer.
