**1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Article                 Subject Matter
1. Article 270                            :   Distribution of taxes between Union and States
2. Article 275                            :   Grants-in-aid to states
3. Article 280                            :   Establishment of Finance Commission
4. Article 292                            :   Union government's borrowing powers within India only
5. Article 293                            :   State government's borrowing powers within and outside India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Article 270 of the Indian Constitution deals with the distribution of the net proceeds of certain taxes and duties between the Union and the States.  Article 275 mandates the Union to grant financial assistance to States that are in need of such assistance.  Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission, a crucial body for recommending the distribution of financial resources.  Article 292 grants the Union government the power to borrow money both within and outside India.  Crucially, Article 293 allows state governments to borrow only within India, not internationally.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) incorrectly include Article 292 or 293 which are mismatched. The inclusion of these incorrect pairings makes options (b), (c), and (d) incorrect.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Financial Parameter                     Value (as of March 2023)
1. States’ revenue as percentage of revenue expenditure : 58%
2. States' debt-GDP ratio                   : 27.5%
3.  Share of States from divisible pool    : 41% (Based on 15th FC)
4. Weight assigned to Income Distance by 15th FC : 25%
5. Weight assigned to Tax and fiscal efforts by 15th FC : 10%

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The provided text states that states' revenue covers only 58% of their revenue expenditure, their debt-GDP ratio stands at 27.5%, and the share of states from the divisible pool is 41% as per the 15th Finance Commission.  These figures accurately reflect the data provided in the source. However, the weights assigned by the 15th Finance Commission to Income Distance and Tax and fiscal efforts are incorrectly stated in options (d) and (b). The 15th FC allocated 45% weight to Income Distance and 2.5% to Tax and fiscal efforts.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect due to the inclusion of these mismatched data points related to the 15th Finance Commission's weightage allocation.


**3. With reference to Special Category Status (SCS), consider the following pairs:**

    State                                      Status
1. Jammu & Kashmir (J&K) in 1969       : Granted SCS
2. Andhra Pradesh in 2024                 : Granted SCS
3. Bihar in 2024                           : Granted SCS
4. Sikkim                                    : Granted SCS at a later date
5. Nagaland in 1969                       : Granted SCS


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 4, and 5 only
(b) 1 and 5 only
(c) 1, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The text explicitly mentions that Jammu & Kashmir, Assam, and Nagaland were granted Special Category Status (SCS) in 1969.  It further notes that Sikkim and other states received SCS later.  The text does not support the assertion that Andhra Pradesh and Bihar were granted SCS in 2024;  it only mentions that they *demanded* it.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include the incorrect assertions about Andhra Pradesh and Bihar receiving SCS in 2024.  This demonstrates the importance of carefully evaluating the factual accuracy of each statement.  The question tests the ability to distinguish between demands for SCS and the actual granting of the status.


**4. With reference to Centre-State relations, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision              Subject Matter
1. Seventh Schedule                      :   Delineation of tax bases between Union and States
2. Article 269-A                         :   Levy and Collection of GST in intra-State Trade 
3. Article 269                           : Taxes levied and collected by Centre but wholly assigned to States
4. Article 282                           : Discretionary Grants
5. Article 244(2)                        : Sixth Schedule

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(b) 1, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Seventh Schedule of the Indian Constitution clearly defines the division of powers and tax bases between the Union and the States. Article 269 deals with taxes levied and collected by the Centre but assigned to the States. Article 282 empowers both the Centre and States to make grants for any public purpose. Article 244(2) is related to the Sixth Schedule, which deals with the administration of tribal areas. Article 269-A, however, deals with the levy and collection of GST in *inter-state* trade or commerce, not intra-state trade. Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include the mismatched pair (Article 269-A) or exclude correctly matched pairs.  The question emphasizes the need for precise understanding of constitutional provisions related to Centre-State financial relations.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Financial Provision                     Description
1. Vertical Devolution                     :   Distribution among states from their allocated share
2. Horizontal Devolution                  :   Share of states from divisible pool
3. Grants-in-Aid                          :   Provided by Centre as per Article 275
4.  Borrowing by States                   :   Requires prior consent of Union if indebted
5.  Borrowing by Union                    :   Can borrow within and outside India


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3, 4, and 5 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(c) 3 and 5 only
(d) 1, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Vertical devolution refers to the distribution of the divisible pool between the Union and the States, while horizontal devolution is the distribution *among* the states from their allocated share.  Grants-in-aid are provided by the Centre to states as per Article 275.  If a state is indebted to the Union, it needs prior consent for further borrowing. The Union can borrow both within and outside India.  Therefore only pairs 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.  Options (b), (c), and (d) incorrectly pair vertical and horizontal devolution and incorrectly include or exclude other pairs.  This question highlights the nuances of fiscal federalism and the importance of understanding the precise meanings of key terms.

**3.  With reference to the Indian Constitution and its amendments, consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision/Act               Related Subject/Feature

2. Article 282                               :   Discretionary grants by Centre and States
3. Article 244(2)                            :   Provisions related to the Sixth Schedule
4. Articles 371, 371-A to 371-H, and 371-J  : Special provisions for certain states (replacing SCS)

(a) 1 only

(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute sentences, including those related to mercy petitions. Article 282 empowers both the central and state governments to make grants for any public purpose. **4. With reference to the Indian judicial system, consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Concept/Procedure                   Description/Application
1. Contempt of Court                         :   Defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971
2. Curative Petition                          :   Last resort remedy after review petition dismissal by Supreme Court
3. Mercy Petition                             :   President's power to pardon or commute sentences
4. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)         :   Handle rape and POCSO Act cases, funded by Nirbhaya Fund


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Contempt of Court is indeed defined under the Contempt of Courts Act, 1971. A Curative Petition serves as the final legal recourse available after a review petition is rejected by the Supreme Court. The President's power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or commute sentences is enshrined in the Constitution and exercised through mercy petitions.  Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) are specifically designed to expedite the handling of rape and POCSO Act cases, with funding provided by the Nirbhaya Fund.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched.


**5. With reference to governance and administration in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                                      Relevant Aspect
1. 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts :   Local self-governance provisions
2.  Fiscal Federalism                           :   Centre-State revenue sharing arrangements
3.  Protected Areas (PA) and Restricted Areas     :   Foreigner access regulations (Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963)
4.  Passport Issuance                             :   Central Government's power to issue passports to non-citizens


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The 73rd and 74th Constitutional Amendment Acts fundamentally altered the structure of local self-governance in India. Fiscal federalism is the core principle governing the distribution of financial resources between the central and state governments. The regulations concerning access to Protected and Restricted Areas for foreigners are clearly defined under the Foreigners (Restricted Areas) Order, 1963.  The Central Government retains the authority to issue passports even to non-citizens in specific circumstances of public interest.  All four pairs are correctly matched.

   Feature/Aspect                                 Characteristic

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

None of the pairs are correctly matched.

Pair 1 is incorrect because Aadhaar numbers are unique; no resident can have a duplicate number.

Pair 2 is incorrect because the Supreme Court affirmed the constitutionality of the Aadhaar Act, 2016, in 2018, albeit with certain conditions.

Pair 3 is incorrect because the Supreme Court ruled that Aadhaar metadata cannot be stored for more than six months.

Pair 4 is incorrect because while Aadhaar is mandatory for accessing certain social welfare schemes, it cannot be forced upon individuals for other purposes like opening bank accounts.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Amendment                                     Key Provision/Feature
1. Indian Telegraph Act 1885                       :   Repealed by the Telecommunications Act 2023
2. Indian Wireless Telegraphy Act 1933           :   Replaced by the Telecommunications Act 2023
3. Telecommunications Act, 2023                 :   Establishes Digital Bharat Nidhi
4.  Telecommunications Act, 2023                 :   Spectrum allocation primarily through auction


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Telecommunications Act, 2023, significantly overhauls the telecommunications regulatory landscape in India.  It explicitly repeals both the outdated Indian Telegraph Act of 1885 and the Indian Wireless Telegraphy Act of 1933, reflecting the technological advancements in the sector.  The Act introduces the Digital Bharat Nidhi, a fund under central government control to support research and development in telecommunications.  Finally, a core element of the act is the shift towards primarily auction-based spectrum allocation, though it retains administrative allocation for specified purposes like national security and disaster management.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.

(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article              Subject Matter
1. Article 270                         :   Distribution of taxes between Union and States based on Finance Commission recommendations.
2. Article 275                         :   Grants-in-aid provided by the Centre to States.
3. Article 280                         :   Establishment of the Finance Commission.
4. Article 292                         :   Union government's power to borrow money within or outside the country.
5. Article 293                         :   State government's power to borrow money within India.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 270 explicitly deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain taxes between the Union and the States, as recommended by the Finance Commission. Article 275 empowers the Union to grant financial assistance to States that are in need of such assistance. The establishment of the Finance Commission is enshrined in Article 280, a crucial body for adjudicating the sharing of resources between the Union and the States. Article 292 grants the Union the power to borrow money both within and outside India, while Article 293 restricts State borrowing to within India, reflecting the hierarchical fiscal structure of the Indian federation.  Any option excluding even one of these articles would be incorrect, highlighting the integral role each plays in India's fiscal federalism.

   Financial Provision/Concept       Description

Horizontal devolution focuses on the distribution of funds among the states themselves based on various criteria like income distance, population, and geographical factors.  Grants-in-aid, as per Article 275, are crucial for assisting states with specific needs. The debt-GDP ratio of states provides a crucial measure of their financial health, and the given figure is accurate as per the provided information.  The Special Category Status (SCS), while previously granted to certain states, was discontinued following the recommendations of the 14th Finance Commission.  Therefore, all statements accurately reflect the given facts.

    1. Mediation and Conciliation Project Committee (MCPC) : Established under the Arbitration and Conciliation Act, 1996
    2. New Delhi International Arbitration Centre Act, 2019 :  Facilitates international commercial arbitration
    3. Arbitration and Conciliation (Amendment) Act, 2021 : Allows for conditional stay of enforcement of arbitral awards in cases of fraud.

**Explanation:**

The Mediation and Conciliation Project Committee (MCPC) was constituted by the Supreme Court of India in 2005, not under the Arbitration and Conciliation Act, 1996.  Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect. The New Delhi International Arbitration Centre Act, 2019, aims to facilitate institutional arbitration, primarily focusing on domestic disputes, although it can involve international elements if the parties agree.  Thus, pair 2 is partially inaccurate in its description. The Arbitration and Conciliation (Amendment) Act, 2021, allows for an *unconditional* stay of enforcement of arbitral awards obtained through fraud or corruption, making pair 3 incorrect. The Indian Council of Arbitration is indeed a society registered under the Societies Registration Act, 1860, making pair 4 correct.  Hence, only pair 4 is entirely accurate.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to differentiate between nuanced details within legal frameworks.


**2. With reference to India's Fiscal Federalism, consider the following pairs:**

    Constitutional Provision/Institution          Specific Function/Characteristic
    1. Article 270                               :  Taxes levied and collected by states and distributed between union and states
    2. 15th Finance Commission                   : Recommended a 50% share of divisible pool for states
    3. Article 293                               : States can borrow money both within and outside India
    4. Horizontal Devolution                      : Distribution among states based solely on population (2011 Census)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 270 deals with the distribution of taxes levied and collected by the Union, not the states.  The 15th Finance Commission recommended a 41% share of the divisible pool for states, not 50%. Article 293 restricts state borrowing to within India; they cannot borrow internationally. Horizontal devolution considers several factors beyond just the 2011 population census, including income distance, area, demographic performance, forest and ecology, and tax and fiscal efforts.  All pairs contain inaccuracies, demonstrating a need for precise knowledge of constitutional provisions and fiscal policies.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to identify incorrect information.


**3. With reference to Special Category Status (SCS) in India, consider the following pairs:**

    State/Entity                                   Relevant Detail
    1. Fifth Finance Commission                    : Recommended abolishing the SCS concept
    2. 14th Finance Commission                    : Recommended the continuation of SCS based on Gadgil-Mukherjee formula
    3. Andhra Pradesh                             :  Currently enjoys Special Category Status
    4. Article 371                                : Contains provisions for special provisions to states, irrespective of SCS


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 4 only
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Fifth Finance Commission introduced the concept of SCS, not its abolishment. The 14th Finance Commission recommended the cessation of SCS, ending the special funding pattern based on the Gadgil-Mukherjee formula.  Andhra Pradesh does not currently enjoy Special Category Status. Article 371 does indeed contain provisions for special provisions to certain states, independent of the SCS classification. Therefore, only pair 4 is accurately matched. The question assesses factual recall and analytical skills to identify misleading information related to the history and current status of SCS.


**4. With reference to the Foreign Contribution (Regulation) Act (FCRA), consider the following pairs:**

    Amendment/Provision                          Specific Detail
    1. 2020 FCRA Amendment                        : Permits NGOs to receive foreign funds without registration
    2. FCRA Account                               : Can be used for purposes other than those specified for the received funds
    3. Validity of FCRA Registration              : Is for a period of two years
    4. Maximum Limit for Administrative Expenses :  20% of the received foreign contribution


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 4 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The 2020 FCRA amendment mandates prior permission and registration for receiving foreign funds, making pair 1 incorrect.  The FCRA account is strictly designated for foreign contributions and cannot be used for other purposes. The validity of FCRA registration is for five years, not two.  Only the statement regarding the maximum limit for administrative expenses (20%) is correct.  The question tests knowledge of the FCRA, its amendments, and its provisions, emphasizing the ability to identify discrepancies and factual inaccuracies.  It assesses factual recall and analytical skills.


**5. With reference to the Post Office Act, 2023, consider the following pairs:**

    Provision/Entity                                    Feature/Power
    1. India Post Office Act, 1998                     : Remains in effect alongside the 2023 Act
    2. Director General of Postal Services (DGPS)       :  Lacks the power to make regulations on postal charges
    3. Government's Power to Intercept Postal Articles : Limited to reasons of national security and public safety
    4. Post Office Liability                            :  Completely exempt from liability for any service provided


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 4 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Post Office Act, 2023, repeals the 1998 Act. The DGPS has the power to make regulations on postal charges. The government's power to intercept postal articles extends beyond the specified reasons, including public order and emergency situations.  The Post Office is not completely exempt from liability; it is liable for services as prescribed. Therefore, all pairs are incorrect, testing the candidate's understanding of the new Post Office Act and its implications. This question emphasizes factual recall and analytical skills in evaluating the accuracy of statements about a recent legislative change.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Provision                                   Key Feature
1. Article 72                                      :   Empowers the President to commute death sentences
2. Article 137                                     :   Relates to the Supreme Court's review jurisdiction
3. Article 142                                     :   Provides the Supreme Court power to do complete justice
4. 10th Schedule                                  :   Deals with anti-defection law
5.  Section 8 of RTI Act                           :   Specifies exemptions from information disclosure

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to commute a sentence of any person convicted of any offense against any law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends.  This includes the power to commute a death sentence. Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments. This is a crucial aspect of the judicial review process, ensuring the Supreme Court can correct any errors or inconsistencies in its decisions.  Article 142 of the Constitution vests the Supreme Court with the power to do complete justice in any case before it, and this power is often invoked to ensure that the ends of justice are served. The 10th Schedule of the Constitution, added through the 52nd Amendment Act of 1985, introduced the anti-defection law, which aims to prevent legislators from changing their party affiliations for personal gain. Section 8 of the Right to Information Act, 2005, details specific exemptions from the right to information, safeguarding sensitive information and maintaining national security. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete, omitting one or more correctly matched pairs.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Scheme                                      Implementing Body/Source of Funds
1. Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)            :   Ministry of Home Affairs
2. People’s Plan Campaign (Jan Yojana Abhiyan) :   Ministry of Rural Development
3.  Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023 :    Department of Justice
4.  Common Service Centres (CSC) Scheme       :    Ministry of Electronics & IT

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) are a centrally sponsored scheme implemented by the Department of Justice, Ministry of Law and Justice, funded by the Nirbhaya Fund.  The People’s Plan Campaign (Jan Yojana Abhiyan) falls under the purview of the Ministry of Panchayati Raj, not the Ministry of Rural Development.  The Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, is a legislation enacted by the Parliament and implemented by the government. Common Service Centres (CSCs) are overseen by the CSC Special Purpose Vehicle (SPV), which is set up by the Ministry of Electronics & IT. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) include incorrectly matched pairs.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legal Concept                                  Associated Legal Provision/Remedy
1. Mercy Petition                               :   Article 142
2. Curative Petition                            :   Article 137
3.  Proportional Representation                  :   52nd Amendment Act
4.  Right to Privacy                             :   Article 21
5.  Preventive Detention                        :   Article 22


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) Only four


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Mercy petitions are addressed to the President under Article 72, not Article 142.  Curative petitions, the last legal recourse in the Supreme Court, are based on the Supreme Court's inherent powers under Article 142, not Article 137 (which concerns review petitions).  Proportional representation is not directly related to the 52nd Amendment Act (which dealt with anti-defection).  The right to privacy, although not explicitly mentioned, is now considered a fundamental right under Article 21.  Preventive detention is addressed under Article 22 of the Constitution.  Therefore, only four pairs are correctly matched.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they underestimate the number of correctly matched pairs.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article           Provision Related To
1. Article 72                     :   Power of the President to grant pardons in cases of death sentence
2. Article 137                    :   Review petition in the Supreme Court
3. Article 142                    :   Power of the Supreme Court to do complete justice
4. Article 32                     :   Right to Constitutional Remedies (Supreme Court)
5. Article 226                    :   Power of High Courts to issue writs

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to commute a sentence of any person convicted of any offense against any law relating to a matter to which the executive power of the Union extends, including death sentences.  Article 137 empowers the Supreme Court to review its own judgments. Article 142 is a crucial provision that allows the Supreme Court to pass any order necessary for doing complete justice in any case before it, including issuing directions or writs. Article 32 guarantees the right to constitutional remedies, allowing citizens to approach the Supreme Court for enforcement of fundamental rights.  Article 226 similarly empowers High Courts to issue writs for the enforcement of fundamental rights and other legal rights.  Therefore, pairs 1, 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.    State                                        Characteristic
1. Andhra Pradesh                               :   Currently holds Special Category Status.
2. Bihar                                        :   Has demanded Special Category Status.
3. Jammu & Kashmir (pre-reorganisation)       :   Was granted Special Category Status in 1969.
4.  Gadgil-Mukherjee formula                   :   Determined grants for SCS states before the 14th Finance Commission.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched. J&K, Assam, and Nagaland were indeed granted SCS in 1969. The Gadgil-Mukherjee formula was used to determine the grants given to these states before the 14th Finance Commission's recommendations, which effectively ended the SCS designation.  Andhra Pradesh does not currently hold SCS, and while Bihar has demanded it, it hasn't been granted.   Options (a), (b), and (d)  include incorrectly matched pairs.



**4. With reference to the formation of new states in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Commission/Committee                         Recommendation

2. S.K. Dhar Commission                         :   Primarily based reorganization on linguistic factors.
3. JVP Committee                                 :   Rejected language as the primary basis for state reorganization.
4.  Article 3 of the Constitution                 :   Empowers Parliament to form new states through ordinary legislation with a simple majority.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. The Fazl Ali Commission's recommendations, implemented through the 7th Constitutional Amendment Act of 1956, significantly reshaped the Indian states' map. The JVP Committee indeed rejected language as the sole criterion for reorganization.  Article 3 of the Constitution grants Parliament the power to create new states. The S.K. Dhar Commission prioritized administrative convenience over linguistic factors, making option 2 incorrect. Options (a), (b), and (c) incorrectly exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Article of the Indian Constitution          Subject Matter
1. Article 270                               :   Levy and collection of taxes by the Union and distribution between Union and States
2. Article 275                               :   Grants-in-aid to states
3. Article 292                               :   Borrowing powers of the Union government
4. Article 280                               :   Establishment of Finance Commission
5. Article 246                               :   Allocation of tax powers between the Union and States

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Article 270 deals with the distribution of net proceeds of certain taxes between the Union and the States. Article 275 mandates the Union government to provide grants-in-aid to states. Article 292 outlines the borrowing powers of the Union. Article 280 establishes the Finance Commission. Article 246 clearly delineates the powers of the Union and States to levy and collect taxes, forming the bedrock of India's fiscal federalism.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs.  Understanding these articles is crucial for analyzing India's fiscal federalism and center-state relations, a key area in the UPSC examination.

The 14th Finance Commission's recommendations led to the phasing out of the Special Category Status (SCS). The 5th Finance Commission introduced the concept of SCS. **4. Consider the following statements regarding the Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution:**

1. It resulted from the recommendations of the Bardoloi Committee.
2. It empowers the Governor to create Autonomous District Councils (ADCs) and Autonomous Regional Councils (ARCs).
3.  ADCs have a maximum of 30 members, with 4 nominated by the Governor and 26 elected.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct. The Sixth Schedule, under Article 244(2), is a direct outcome of the Bardoloi Committee's recommendations. It grants the Governor the power to establish ADCs and ARCs in specified states. ADCs are constituted with a maximum of 30 members, comprising 4 nominated by the Governor and 26 elected members.  These provisions are designed to grant autonomy to tribal regions, a crucial aspect of India's governance structure.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incomplete and thus incorrect.


**5. Consider the following pairs related to the formation of new states in India:**

   Constitutional Provision         Specific Power or Procedure

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only the first two pairs are correctly matched. Article 3 of the Indian Constitution deals with the formation of new states and the alteration of areas, boundaries, or names of existing states.  A bill for the formation of a new state must be introduced in Parliament only on the recommendation of the President. While State Reorganisation Commissions have been used historically, they are not the *currently* primary body for recommending new state formations. The process is now more directly under the purview of the Parliament and the executive branch. Therefore, option (b) is the only correct answer.  Option (c) and (d) are incorrect because they include the inaccurate pairing related to the State Reorganisation Commission.

The question assesses the candidates’ understanding of the constitutional provisions underpinning fiscal federalism in India. **1. With reference to the Right to Information (RTI) Act, 2005, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                      Description
1. Section 8                                    :   Specifies exemptions from information disclosure
2. Second Schedule                               :   Lists certain intelligence and security organizations exempt from RTI
3. RTI (Amendment) Act, 2019                    :   Granted the Central Government power to determine the terms of service for CICs and ICs
4. Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) Act, 2023 :   Amended Section 8(1)(j) to exempt all personal information from disclosure


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The RTI Act, 2005, aims to empower citizens by providing them with access to information held by public authorities.  However, certain categories of information are exempt from disclosure to protect national security,  privacy, and other vital interests. Section 8 of the Act explicitly outlines these exemptions. The Second Schedule further specifies certain intelligence and security organizations that are exempted from the ambit of the RTI Act.  The RTI (Amendment) Act, 2019, significantly altered the process of appointing and managing Information Commissioners (ICs) at both the central and state levels, granting the central government greater control over their terms and conditions of service.  The DPDP Act, 2023, introduced a crucial amendment to Section 8(1)(j) of the RTI Act, broadening the scope of exempted personal information.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Option (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.


**2. With reference to Aadhaar, consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                     Description
1. 12-digit unique identification number     :   Can be deactivated or omitted by UIDAI
2. Issued by UIDAI                             :   Serves as authoritative proof of date of birth
3. Linked to individual biometrics             :   Guarantees no resident can have a duplicate number


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Aadhaar, a 12-digit unique identification number, is issued by the Unique Identification Authority of India (UIDAI).  A crucial feature is its linkage to individual biometrics, ensuring uniqueness and preventing duplication. The UIDAI retains the power to deactivate or omit Aadhaar numbers under specific circumstances. However, it's crucial to note that while Aadhaar can be used to establish identity, the Supreme Court has clarified that it is not considered authoritative proof of date of birth.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched.  Pair 2 is incorrect because Aadhaar doesn't serve as definitive proof of date of birth. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they either include the incorrectly matched pair 2 or exclude correctly matched pairs.


**3. With reference to the Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                     Feature
1. Admissibility of electronic records          :   Carries the same legal weight as paper records
2. Oral evidence                               :   Can only be given in person before the court
3. Joint trials                                 :   Applies only to offences with a maximum sentence of less than seven years


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Bharatiya Sakshya Adhiniyam, 2023, modernizes India's evidence law. A key provision is the equal admissibility of electronic and digital records alongside paper records, enhancing the use of digital evidence in legal proceedings.  However, the Act also allows for oral evidence to be given electronically, contradicting option 2.  Joint trials are permitted under the Act for multiple accused individuals, but this feature isn't limited to offences with sentences below seven years, making option 3 incorrect. Therefore, only pair 1 is correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include the incorrectly matched pairs 2 and/or 3.


**4. With reference to the Digital Personal Data Protection (DPDP) Act, 2023, consider the following pairs:**

   Entity/Right                                  Description
1. Data Principal                               :   Has the right to seek correction and erasure of personal data
2. Data Fiduciary                              :   Must erase personal data as soon as the purpose is met
3. Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDFs)          :   Are not subject to any data protection obligations
4. Cross-border data transfer                   :   Is permitted only to countries specified by the government


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The DPDP Act, 2023, establishes a framework for protecting digital personal data. Data principals, individuals whose data is being processed, possess several rights, including the right to seek correction or erasure of their data. Data fiduciaries, entities processing personal data, have obligations such as ensuring data accuracy and erasing data when its purpose is fulfilled unless legally required for retention.  The Act designates certain data fiduciaries as Significant Data Fiduciaries (SDFs) based on factors like data volume and sensitivity, but these entities are *not* exempt from data protection obligations; rather, they face additional responsibilities.  Cross-border data transfer is permitted, but only to countries approved by the government. Therefore, pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched. Pair 3 is incorrect. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair 3 or exclude correctly matched pairs.


**5. With reference to the President's powers concerning mercy petitions, consider the following pairs:**

   Article                                     Power Granted
1. Article 72                                  :   Applies only to offenses against laws relating to matters under the Union's executive power
2. Article 72                                  :   Includes the power to pardon individuals convicted by court-martial
3. Article 142                                 :   Provides the basis for the curative petition process


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment, including commutation or suspension of sentences. This power extends to cases involving convictions by court-martial and offenses under laws where the Union's executive power applies.  While Article 142 empowers the Supreme Court to do complete justice, it's not directly related to the President's mercy petition powers; the curative petition process is a separate Supreme Court mechanism. Therefore, pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched, while pair 3 is incorrect. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either incorrectly include pair 3 or exclude correctly matched pairs.

   Amendment/Provision                         Focus

Many of these amendments have focused on addressing issues such as offenses against women and food adulteration. **8. With reference to the Bharatiya Nagarik Suraksha Sanhita, 2023 (BNSS), consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                   Feature
1. Detention of undertrials                    :   Mandatory release on bail after completing one-third of the maximum sentence for first-time offenders
2. Medical examination                         :   Can only be requested by a senior police officer
3. Forensic investigation                       :   Mandatory for offences punishable by less than seven years imprisonment


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The BNSS, 2023, which replaces the CrPC, 1973, introduces several procedural changes.  It mandates the release of first-time offenders on bail after they have served one-third of their maximum sentence.  However, this provision has exceptions for certain serious offenses.  Any police officer, not just a senior one, can request a medical examination of an accused in specific cases.  Forensic investigations are mandatory for offences punishable with at least seven years, not less than seven years, of imprisonment. Therefore, only pair 1 is correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they include the incorrectly matched pairs 2 and/or 3.


**9. With reference to preventive detention, consider the following pairs:**

   Law                                          Grounds for Detention
1. National Security Act, 1980                 :   Maintenance of essential services
2. Conservation of Foreign Exchange and Prevention of Smuggling Activities Act (COFEPOSA), 1974 :   Security of the State
3. Unlawful Activities (Prevention) Act (UAPA), 1967 :   Maintenance of Public Order


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Preventive detention laws allow for the detention of individuals without trial to prevent them from engaging in activities deemed harmful to national security or public order.  The National Security Act, 1980, COFEPOSA, 1974, and UAPA, 1967, all provide for preventive detention based on grounds such as the security of the state, maintenance of public order, and maintenance of essential services. Therefore, all three pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.


**10. With reference to personality rights, consider the following pairs:**

   Aspect                                       Feature
1. Protection in Indian Statute                 :   Explicitly mentioned in the Indian Constitution
2. Posthumous Personality Rights             :   Cannot be claimed by family members
3. International Conventions                   :   A comprehensive international treaty exists on the subject


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) None
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Personality rights, encompassing the right to protect one's name, image, and other identifying features, are not explicitly mentioned in any specific Indian statute. While they are often linked to the right to privacy and property, there is no single comprehensive statutory protection.  Posthumous personality rights can be claimed by family members, particularly in defamation suits.  There is no single, universally ratified international convention specifically dedicated to personality rights. Therefore, none of the pairs are correctly matched.

   Body                                  Associated Act/Amendment

3.  National Commission for Scheduled Castes (NCSC) :  The Constitution of India
Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The National Human Rights Commission (NHRC) is a statutory body established under the Protection of Human Rights Act (PHRA), 1993, as amended in 2006 and 2019.  This act defines its powers, functions, and composition.  The UPSC's establishment and functions are detailed within the Constitution of India, specifically relating to the recruitment of civil servants. Similarly, the NCSC's constitutional basis is found within the Constitution of India, outlining its role in safeguarding the rights and interests of Scheduled Castes.  All three pairs accurately reflect the primary legal framework governing each body's existence and operation. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair, failing to acknowledge the constitutional or statutory basis of these crucial governance bodies.  A comprehensive understanding of India's constitutional and statutory framework is essential for effective governance and public administration, hence the importance of correctly identifying the legal basis for these institutions.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Article                  Provision Related To
1. Article 72                               :  President's Power of Pardon
2. Article 129                               :  Supreme Court's Contempt Power
3. Article 215                               :  High Court's Contempt Power
4. Article 244(2)                           :  Establishment of Gram Nyayalayas
5. Article 282                               :  Discretionary Grants


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1 and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Article 72 of the Indian Constitution explicitly grants the President the power to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to suspend, remit, or commute the sentence of any person convicted of any offense.  Articles 129 and 215, respectively, vest the Supreme Court and High Courts with the inherent power to punish for contempt of court.  Article 282 empowers both the central and state governments to make grants for any public purpose, not necessarily within their legislative competence, which is relevant to the concept of discretionary grants.  Article 244(2) deals with the administration of scheduled areas and tribal areas, not the establishment of Gram Nyayalayas; that is established under the Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008. Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, 3, and 5 are correctly matched. Option (b) accurately reflects this.  Options (a), (c), and (d) include incorrect pairings, demonstrating a lack of precise understanding of the constitutional provisions.

(d) Only one


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Citizenship Amendment Act, 2019, notably reduced the naturalization period for certain categories of migrants.  The Foreigners (Tribunals) Order, 1964, established the quasi-judicial bodies known as Foreigners Tribunals.  These are correctly matched pairs (2 and 5).  The Aadhaar Act, 2016, is not a proof of citizenship but a unique identification number.  The Gram Nyayalayas Act, 2008, does not exempt all states but specifically exempts certain states and tribal areas.  The Right to Information Act, 2005,  was later amended by the Digital Personal Data Protection Act, 2023, to exempt certain personal information, but this wasn't an original feature. Therefore, only option (a) correctly identifies the accurately matched pairs. Options (b), (c), and (d) contain inaccurate or incomplete pairings, highlighting the importance of precise knowledge about the acts and their provisions.

**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Contempt of Court                    Description
1. Civil Contempt                            :   Publication that scandalizes a court
2. Criminal Contempt                         :   Wilful disobedience of a court order
3. Civil Contempt                            :   Interference with the administration of justice
4. Criminal Contempt                         :   Willful breach of an undertaking to a court


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Wilful disobedience of a court order and willful breach of an undertaking given to a court are both accurate descriptions of criminal contempt.  (pairs 2 and 4).  Publication that scandalizes a court and interference with the administration of justice are aspects of criminal contempt, not civil contempt.  Civil contempt primarily involves the willful disobedience of court orders or undertakings.  Therefore, only option (a) correctly pairs the types of contempt with their accurate descriptions. Options (b), (c), and (d) reflect a conflation of the characteristics of civil and criminal contempt, highlighting the need for precise understanding of legal definitions and procedures.

(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) Only one

Centrally Sponsored Schemes (CSS) are jointly funded by the central and state governments, not solely by the central government. Therefore, only option (a) correctly identifies the accurate matches. Options (b), (c), and (d) contain inaccuracies, demonstrating the need for precise knowledge of the funding mechanisms and constitutional provisions related to different financial schemes and provisions within the Indian federal system.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Scheme/Act                                     Key Feature/Provision
1. Jan Yojana Abhiyan (People’s Plan Campaign) :   Introduced as ‘Sabki Yojana Sabka Vikas’ in 2018
2. Sixth Schedule of the Indian Constitution    :   Resulted from recommendations of the Bardoloi Committee
3. Article 282 of the Indian Constitution        :   Empowers the Centre and states to make discretionary grants
4. Aadhaar Act, 2016                             :   Aadhaar mandatory for accessing social welfare schemes (as per 2018 SC Judgement)
5. Right to Information Act, 2005              :   Replaced the Freedom of Information Act, 2002

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched.  The Jan Yojana Abhiyan, launched in 2018, was initially known as ‘Sabki Yojana Sabka Vikas’. The Sixth Schedule, under Article 244(2), directly stems from the Bardoloi Committee's recommendations. Article 282 explicitly grants the power to the central and state governments to provide discretionary grants for public purposes.  The 2018 Supreme Court judgment in *Justice K.S. Puttaswamy v UoI* affirmed the constitutionality of the Aadhaar Act and its use for accessing social welfare schemes, although not mandatory for all services. **2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Constitutional Provision/Body                  Function/Power
1. Article 72                                     :   Grants pardons, reprieves, etc., for offences against Union laws
2. Curative Petition                             :   Last constitutional remedy after review petition dismissal by SC
3. Foreigners Tribunals                           :   Power to declare a person a foreigner in India
4.  President's Mercy Petition                     :   Relates to death sentences and court-martial convictions
5.  Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs)          :   Swift disposal of rape and POCSO Act cases

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Article 72 of the Indian Constitution empowers the President to grant pardons, reprieves, respites, or remissions of punishment or to commute sentences in certain cases, including death sentences and court-martial convictions. A curative petition is indeed the last resort available to a litigant whose review petition has been dismissed by the Supreme Court.  Foreigners Tribunals, established under the Foreigners (Tribunals) Order, 1964, possess the sole authority to declare an individual a foreigner. The President's power to consider mercy petitions extends to death sentences and court-martial convictions, as explicitly mentioned in Article 72. Finally, the Fast-Track Special Courts (FTSCs) were established to expedite the disposal of cases related to rape and the Protection of Children from Sexual Offences (POCSO) Act.  Therefore, option (d) is the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete and thus incorrect.

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched. The NITI Aayog is currently leading the revamp of Centrally Sponsored Schemes. The Ministry of Electronics & IT oversees the implementation of the Common Service Centres (CSCs) scheme.  The Election Commission of India (ECI) is responsible for the EVM-VVPAT system and the enforcement of the Model Code of Conduct.  Finally, the Department of Personnel and Training under the Ministry of Personnel, Public Grievances and Pensions coordinates the implementation of the Right to Information Act, 2005. Each pairing accurately reflects the responsible authority or agency for the respective act or scheme.  Therefore, option (d) is the correct answer, which includes all correctly matched pairs. Other options are incomplete and therefore incorrect.


**5. With reference to Indian Citizenship and related laws, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Rule                                       Key Provision/Feature
1. Citizenship Act, 1955                          :   Defines Indian citizenship and various modes of acquisition
2. Citizenship (Amendment) Rules, 2024           :   Enforces the Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA), 2019
3.  Assam Accord, 1985                            :   Confers citizenship to migrants from East Pakistan until March 24, 1971
4. Foreigners (Tribunals) Order, 1964             :   Establishes quasi-judicial bodies to determine foreigner status.
5. Passport Act, 1920                              :   Governs the issuance of passports in India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched. The Citizenship Act of 1955 lays the foundation for Indian citizenship, outlining the processes for acquiring and losing citizenship. The Citizenship (Amendment) Rules, 2024, are designed to implement the Citizenship Amendment Act (CAA), 2019. The Assam Accord of 1985 addresses the issue of citizenship for migrants from East Pakistan (now Bangladesh).  The Foreigners (Tribunals) Order, 1964, established the quasi-judicial bodies responsible for determining the status of foreigners in India.  The Passport Act of 1920 governs the issuance of passports to Indian citizens. Thus, each pair accurately describes a key aspect of the corresponding act or rule.  Option (d) is the correct answer, as it includes all correctly matched pairs; other options are incomplete and incorrect.
